Haven - Three Days After Return
The party has had time to rest, resupply, and catch their breath after the 
intensive coastal operations. Johannes has been thinking about the magical 
items they've acquired and some ideas he'd like to explore with Kaladin's 
expertise.
The artificer's workshop is located in a converted smithy on the eastern edge 
of Haven's main compound. Even from outside, you can hear the 
rhythmic tap-tap-tap of careful metalwork and smell the distinctive scents of 
hot metal, arcane reagents, and ozone.
When you enter, Kaladin is bent over a workbench, examining what appears to 
be a damaged Dragon Army breastplate through an enchanted loupe. He's a 
lean human in his mid-40s, with burn scars on his forearms and perpetually 
soot-stained hands. His leather apron is covered in pockets containing various 
tools and components.
He looks up, recognizes Johannes, and sets down his work. "Ah, the hero of 
Pax Tharkas returns. I heard about Flotsam-impressive work, though I 
imagine it wasn't pretty." He wipes his hands on a rag. "What brings you to my 
corner of Haven? Looking for repairs, modifications, or something more... 
creative?"
He gestures to a clear area of his workshop where he typically consults with 
clients.
What would Johannes like to discuss with Kaladin? Are there specific 
items you want enchanted, modified, or created? Or perhaps you're interested 
in what services he offers?
Clarification: We need to visit Master Artificer Keldin in Ak-Thyln (see Aboleth 
reconnaissance mission prep

Journey to Ak-Thyln
The party sets out from Haven on the two-day journey to Ak-Thyln. The region 
shows clear signs of recovery since the Dragon Army was driven out - farms 
are being rebuilt, refugees are returning, and there's cautious optimism in the 
air.
Ak-Thyln itself is a modest trading town of about 3,000 people, nestled in 
rolling hills with good access to regional trade routes. The town has a grateful 
relationship with the party - after all, you prevented a Dragon Army invasion 
fleet from landing on their shores.
Master Artificer Keldin's Workshop
You find Keldin's workshop in the craftsman's quarter - a two-story stone 
building with reinforced doors and windows that show the faint shimmer of 
protective wards. Smoke rises from multiple chimneys, and you can hear the 
hum of arcane machinery inside.
When you enter, Keldin looks up from a workbench where he's etching runes 
into a steel bracer. He's a stocky dwarf with a magnificently braided beard 
adorned with small metal clasps, and he wears heavy protective goggles 
pushed up on his forehead.
"Well, well! If it isn't the champions who saved our coast!" He sets down his 
tools with a grin. "Johannes, Kessa, Brother Cyrus - word of your Flotsam 
operation reached us. Sinking fifteen Dragon Army ships? That's work worthy 
of song." He wipes his hands on his leather apron. "What can I do for you? 
Repairs? Enchantments? Or perhaps something more ambitious?"
What enchantment work does Johannes want to discuss with 
Master Keldin?
Something relatively revolutionary. The three of us are often engaged in 
highly delicate operations that require efficient, effective communications that 
are discrete. I am looking for you to try and craft something that could work 
collaboratively among the three of us that performs the following tasks:
1) Silent communication (either something written like Message, Sending 
Stone) or telepathic between three separate individuals (or more if needed) 2) 
If possible, scrying of some sort or the ability to transmit images or vision at 
distance 3) Highly portable, cannot be fixed to specific locations 4) Scalable, 
meaning that above the initial 3 devices, additional devices could be created 
and added into the network
Cost really isn't an issue. I can leave my entire gold account to cover initial 
development costs, with the provision that should you be able to craft what 
we are looking for, I will cover remaining costs as I may. I know this is 
groundbreaking work and may take years to complete, but if the task can 
begin, my gratitude will know no bounds.
Show more
Dec 10
Keldin's eyes widen as you lay out the specifications. He sets down his tools 
completely and listens with intense focus, occasionally stroking his beard as he 
processes each requirement.
When you finish, there's a long moment of silence. Then he slowly rises from 
his stool and walks to a locked cabinet, retrieving a leather-bound journal 
filled with diagrams and notes. He flips through several pages before returning 
to the workbench.
"You're not asking for something revolutionary, Johannes. You're asking for 
something unprecedented." He taps the journal. "But not impossible. Let me 
break down what you're describing..."
He pulls out a piece of parchment and begins sketching as he talks:
"THE TECHNICAL CHALLENGES:"
"Silent communication between three individuals - This is actually 
the easiest part. Sending Stones exist, Message cantrips exist, even items that 
replicate Rary's Telepathic Bond. The challenge is making it always 
available and instantaneous rather than limited uses per day."
"Scrying or image transmission - This is where it gets complex. Scrying 
requires a 5th-level spell slot, significant components, and targets can resist. 
What you're describing is more like... arcane surveillance. Seeing through 
another person's eyes, or transmitting what you see. That's 6th-level magic 
territory - True Seeing, aspects of Arcane Eye."
"Highly portable and not location-fixed - This rules out permanent 
circles or anchored items. We're talking personal equipment. Rings, amulets, 
earpieces, perhaps integrated into existing magical items."
"Scalable network - Now THIS is the truly groundbreaking part. You're not 
asking for paired items. You're asking for a network where any device can 
communicate with any other device, and new devices can be added. That 
requires... a central arcane matrix? Or each item containing a fragment of a 
linked whole?"
He sets down his charcoal and looks at you seriously.
"Here's what I can tell you:"
"FEASIBILITY:"
"Phase 1 - Basic Network (6-8 months, 3,000-4,000 gp):
*	Three linked items (likely rings or earpieces) that allow silent 
communication between all three wearers
*	Always-on connection, no daily use limits
*	Range: roughly 1 mile, possibly extendable to 5 miles with refinement
*	Text-based or telepathic speech
Phase 2 - Image Transmission (additional 8-12 months, 4,000-
6,000 gp):
*	Upgrade existing items to allow brief visual sharing (think: 1 minute of 
seeing through another's eyes, 3-4 times per day)
*	Not true scrying (no resistance check, target must be willing network 
member)
*	Requires significant enchantment research and rare components
Phase 3 - Scalability (additional 6-10 months, variable cost):
*	Develop 'master schema' that allows creation of additional network 
items
*	Each additional item: 1,000-1,500 gp in materials and labor
*	Maximum network size: Unknown, but likely 10-12 devices before 
magical interference becomes problematic"
He leans back and crosses his arms.
"Total timeline: 2-3 years for full implementation. Total cost: 10,000-15,000 
gp, possibly more depending on component availability and research 
setbacks."
"But here's the thing, Johannes - if this works, you're not just commissioning 
magical items. You're pioneering an entirely new category of collaborative 
enchantment. The military applications alone... Haven's resistance could use 
this. The Palanthas city guard. Any coordinated force."
He looks at you carefully. "I'm interested. This is the kind of work that defines 
a master artificer's career. But I need to be clear about expectations:"
"MY TERMS:"
1.	Initial development payment: 1,500 gp - Covers materials, 
research time, component acquisition for Phase 1
2.	Progress updates every two months - You'll know if I'm hitting 
obstacles or making breakthroughs
3.	Prototype testing with your party - When Phase 1 is ready, you 
field-test it and report back on problems
4.	Intellectual ownership - I retain the right to craft additional sets for 
other clients (primarily Haven/resistance forces), but you get first 
production and discounted rates on future items
5.	No guarantees on timeline - If research hits a wall, it hits a wall. I 
won't take your money for impossible work, but breakthroughs take 
time
He extends a soot-stained hand.
"Do we have an accord? And more importantly - do you have a name for this 
project? Every great innovation deserves a proper title."
How does Johannes respond? And what would you like to call this 
network system?
You're creating it; you get the credit. I am just helping in the defray of costs 
for development. I trust in your good judgement. In fact, the less visible I am 
in the creation of this, the less likely this might cause problems for you. If no 
one knows I am involved, the provenance causes less problems for you with 
our external enemies. And the initial payment, like I said," I hand over a large 
bag filled with platinum pieces that leaves me with the equivalent of 500 gp, 
"you need this a lot more than I do, though if I am right, and this system 
works, money will never be an issue for you, or for the fifth descendants of 
your fifth descendants.
Dec 10
Keldin takes the bag, weighs it in his hand for a moment, then sets it down on 
the workbench with a heavy thunk. He opens it, sees the platinum pieces 
gleaming inside, and his expression shifts from professional interest to 
something approaching awe.
He counts quickly - nearly 5,300 gold pieces worth of platinum.
The dwarf is silent for a long moment, then carefully closes the bag and looks 
at you with an intensity that wasn't there before.
"Johannes Constantinius." His voice is quieter now, more personal. "I've 
crafted items for nobles, for generals, for merchant princes who threw gold 
around like copper. But I've never had someone hand me their entire fortune 
and say 'make something that matters.'"
He reaches out and grips your forearm in the traditional dwarven clasp of 
respect.
"You're right about the visibility - if Dragon Army intelligence learns you're 
funding revolutionary communication magic, they'll move heaven and earth to 
stop it or steal it. So here's what we'll do:"
"THE ARRANGEMENT:"
"This project will be known as The Resonance Network - my research, my 
innovation, funded by 'anonymous resistance benefactors.' Your name stays 
out of it completely. When Haven asks where the funding came from, I'll say 
'liberated Dragon Army gold' or 'grateful coastal merchants.' No one needs to 
know."
"As for descendants of descendants..." He chuckles darkly. "If this works, aye, 
there'll be wealth. But more importantly, there'll be legacy. Every coordinated 
resistance operation, every life saved by better communication, every tactical 
advantage... that's what matters."
He moves to a secure lockbox built into the wall, places the platinum inside, 
and locks it with both key and a whispered command word.
"The funds are secure. I'll draw what I need for components and research, and 
I'll keep meticulous records. Every two months, I'll send word to Haven - 
progress reports, obstacles, breakthroughs. You'll know how your investment 
fares."
He returns to the workbench and makes a note in his journal:
Project Resonance - Phase 1 Initiated Anonymous Benefactor - 5,300 gp 
received Goal: Networked silent communication for resistance operations 
Timeline: 6-8 months to prototype
Then he looks up at you with a craftsman's fire in his eyes.
"I'll start immediately. First step is acquiring a pair of Sending Stones to study 
their enchantment matrix, then researching modifications to the bond 
between paired items. I know a gem merchant in Palanthas who deals in the 
right kind of crystals..."
He pauses, then adds more quietly: "Johannes, I don't know what drives a 
man to give away everything he has for a project that might not succeed, that 
might take years, and that he won't even take credit for. But I'll honor that 
trust. You've given me the chance to create something genuinely new in a 
world that desperately needs it."
"When the prototype is ready - and it will be ready - I'll send word through 
Haven. You'll be the first to test it."
Kessa and Cyrus's Reactions:
Kessa has been uncharacteristically quiet during this exchange. Now she 
speaks up: "Johannes... that was everything. You just... you're sure about 
this?"
Cyrus is looking at you with something between concern and understanding. 
"Brother, you've just invested your entire fortune in hope. That's... that's either 
the most faithful thing I've ever seen, or the most reckless." A pause. "Probably 
both."
Is there anything else Johannes wants to discuss with Keldin

Keldin nods approvingly, catching the correction immediately.
"Aye, you're right. Anonymous benefactors - no mention of resistance, Haven, 
or any particular cause. Just merchants, grateful townsfolk, investors who see 
the potential. Clean money for clean research."
He makes a quick annotation in his journal, crossing out a word and replacing 
it.
"Better for everyone that way. If this works, the applications go far beyond any 
one conflict. Trading companies, exploration guilds, city watches... the market 
is vast once the concept is proven."
He closes the journal with finality. "Business terms agreed. I'll keep politics 
and provenance out of my records and correspondence. You'll hear from me in 
two months with the first progress report."
The dwarf extends his hand once more - this time a simple handshake rather 
than the formal clasp. "Thank you for your confidence in my work. I won't 
squander it."
 
Outside Keldin's Workshop

Then, with a slight smile: "Though I notice you kept back 500 gold. At least we 
can afford decent lodging on the way back to Haven."

Return to Haven - Two Days Later
The journey back is uneventful, giving the party time to rest and reflect. 
Johannes is noticeably lighter - not just in coin purse, but in demeanor. He's 
made a long-term investment in capability that could transform how the party 
operates. The others respect the decision, even if it was bold.
 
Haven - Commander Laurana's Command Tent
You're ushered in shortly after arriving. Laurana is studying a large map of the 
region, with various markers indicating Dragon Army positions, resistance 
cells, and strategic locations. She looks up as you enter.
"Welcome back. I trust your business in Ak-Thyln was productive?" She 
doesn't press for details - she's learned that sometimes the best commanders 
don't ask too many questions about how their best operatives prepare.
She gestures to the map. "We've had an interesting development. About a 
week ago, one of our scouts reported unusual activity in the Dargaard 
Mountains, roughly 80 miles northeast of here."
She points to a region of forbidding peaks marked with old fortification 
symbols.
"The area is dominated by Dargaard Keep - an ancient fortress that's been 
abandoned since the Cataclysm. The place has an... ugly reputation. Stories of 
undead, curses, that sort of thing. Locals won't go near it."
She looks up at you. "Three days ago, a Dragon Army patrol - small unit, 
maybe 15-20 soldiers - was spotted heading into the mountains toward the 
keep. They haven't come back out."
"Now, normally I'd write that off as stupid commanders getting their people 
killed by whatever haunts that place. But our intelligence suggests the Dragon 
Army has been searching for something in pre-Cataclysm ruins. After what 
you found with that aboleth's hoard - ancient deeds, historical documents - 
I'm wondering if they're looking for similar assets."
She taps the map. "I need to know three things:
1.	What happened to that Dragon Army patrol? Did they die? Did 
they find something? Are they still there?
2.	What are they looking for? If the Dragon Army thinks something in 
Dargaard Keep is worth the risk, we need to know what it is.
3.	Can we deny them the asset? If there's something valuable there - 
magical, strategic, historical - can we secure it or destroy it before they 
mount a larger operation?"
Laurana crosses her arms. "I won't lie to you - Dargaard Keep's reputation 
is bad. The Cataclysm hit that place hard, and the Knight who held it... well, 
the stories say he died badly and didn't stay dead. But if the Dragon Army 
thinks it's worth investigating, we can't afford to ignore it."
She looks at each of you in turn. "This is reconnaissance first, intervention 
second. Get in, find out what happened to that patrol, assess what they were 
after, and report back. If you can secure or deny whatever asset they were 
seeking, do it. But don't die trying - information is more valuable than heroics 
right now."
"Questions?"
What does Johannes want to know before accepting this mission?
What can you tell us about the Keep, and this Knight you mention?
Dec 10
Laurana nods, clearly expecting this question. She moves to a side table and 
retrieves a worn leather folder containing historical documents.
"What I can tell you comes from pre-Cataclysm records and local legend - 
which means some of it is fact, some is embellishment, and some might be 
complete fiction. But here's what we know:"
She spreads out a few aged documents and a rough sketch of the keep's 
exterior.
"DARGAARD KEEP - THE FACTS:"
"Built approximately 400 years ago, Dargaard Keep was a major fortress 
controlling the mountain passes in this region. Strategically positioned, well-
fortified, garrison of about 200 soldiers at its height. It was the seat of a 
Knight of Solamnia named Lord Soth."
She pauses, her expression darkening slightly.
"Soth was, by all accounts, a exemplary knight. Honorable, skilled in battle, 
beloved by his men. Rose quickly through the ranks. But something happened 
in the years before the Cataclysm - the records are fragmentary, but they 
suggest scandal. An affair, accusations of betrayal, some kind of tragic incident 
involving his wife."
"THE CATACLYSM:"
"When the Cataclysm struck, Dargaard Keep was hit hard. The entire 
structure was partially destroyed - fires, collapse, mass casualties. According 
to legend, Lord Soth and his knights died in the catastrophe, but the manner 
of their deaths was... cursed somehow. The stories say Soth was on a mission 
of redemption when the Cataclysm struck, but failed - and was condemned for 
that failure."
She looks up at you. "Here's where fact ends and legend begins."
"THE LEGEND - LORD SOTH, DEATH KNIGHT:"
"The locals claim Lord Soth didn't stay dead. They say he rose as something 
worse - a death knight, bound to the keep by his failures and guilt. The 
stories describe him as a figure in blackened armor, burning with cold fire, 
commanding undead servants."
"Travelers who've gotten too close to the keep report hearing strange sounds 
at night - weeping, screaming, the clash of phantom battles. Some claim to see 
lights in the towers. Most who venture too close don't come back."
Cyrus interjects quietly: "Death knights are... they're real, but rare. Paladins or 
knights who commit terrible betrayals and are cursed by the gods themselves. 
They retain their martial skill and gain powerful necromantic abilities. If Soth 
truly became one, he'd be extremely dangerous - immune to most magic, 
capable of commanding undead, and nearly impossible to destroy 
permanently."
Laurana nods. "That's what concerns me. If the Dragon Army thinks they 
can negotiate with or control whatever's in that keep, they're either desperate 
or they know something we don't."
"WHAT WE DON'T KNOW:"
She spreads her hands. "We don't know if Soth truly exists, or if he's just a 
story to keep people away. We don't know what the keep's interior looks like 
after 300+ years. We don't know what the Dragon Army was specifically 
seeking - magical items, strategic position, alliance with undead forces, 
something else entirely."
She looks at you seriously. "And we don't know what happened to that 15-20 
soldier patrol. Did they get killed by whatever haunts the place? Are they holed 
up inside, trapped? Did they find what they were looking for and leave by 
another route?"
"PRACTICAL INFORMATION:"
"The keep is roughly 80 miles northeast - three to four days' travel through 
increasingly rough terrain. The last 20 miles are mountainous and difficult. 
There's a small village called Dargaard Village about 5 miles from the keep - 
maybe 200 people, mostly farmers and herders. They might have more recent 
information about activity in the area."
"Weather's been clear lately, so travel shouldn't be difficult until you hit the 
mountains. The keep itself sits on a high promontory - defensible position, but 
that also means it's visible for miles. Hard to approach without being seen."
She closes the folder. "That's everything we have. Incomplete, unreliable, but 
it's what we've got."
Kessa speaks up: "So we're walking into a potentially cursed fortress that 
might house an undead death knight, looking for a missing Dragon Army 
patrol that was searching for... something. And we don't know if the death 
knight is real, what they were looking for, or if the whole area is just a 
convenient trap."
Laurana's expression is grim but honest. "Yes. That's exactly what I'm asking 
you to do. Which is why I'm asking you - you've handled worse odds and come 
back with intelligence we needed."
Johannes, do you have more questions, or are you ready to 
accept/decline this mission?
I want all the details about death knights and what kinds of weapons, spells, 
etc. would have impact on it. I am leery of going anywhere where we have no 
ability to control events or defend ourselves.
Dec 10
Laurana nods approvingly. "Smart. Going in blind against something like that 
is suicide. Let me get Brother Marius - he's our expert on undead and holy 
lore."
She steps outside and returns a few minutes later with an elderly cleric 
wearing the robes of Paladine. Brother Marius is thin, scholarly, with ink-
stained fingers and the careful manner of someone who's spent decades 
studying rather than fighting.
"Commander Laurana tells me you need information on death knights. Wise - 
they're among the most dangerous undead in existence." He pulls out a scroll 
and spreads it on the table.
"DEATH KNIGHTS - WHAT THEY ARE:"
"A death knight is a fallen paladin or knight, cursed by divine powers for 
committing an act of terrible betrayal or evil. They retain their martial 
prowess, gain significant necromantic powers, and are bound to a specific 
location or quest. They're intelligent, tactical, and utterly relentless."
"COMBAT CAPABILITIES:"
Brother Marius ticks off points on his fingers:
"Martial Prowess: They fight as well as they did in life - often better. Expect 
master-level swordsmanship, heavy armor, mounted combat if they have an 
undead steed. Lord Soth, if he exists, was reportedly a Knight of Solamnia - 
which means exceptional training.
Hellfire Orb: Once per day, they can create a sphere of magical fire that 
explodes in a 20-foot radius. Devastating damage - 7d6 fire plus 7d6 necrotic. 
This is their most dangerous direct attack ability.
Spellcasting: They retain any paladin spells they had in life, but twisted to 
dark purposes. Expect Command, Dispel Magic, Hellish Rebuke, possibly 
more powerful spells depending on their level when they fell.
Frightening Presence: Their mere presence can inspire supernatural 
terror. Weak-willed individuals may flee or become paralyzed with fear.
Undead Command: They can control lesser undead within their domain - 
skeletons, zombies, wraiths, specters. If Dargaard Keep is truly cursed, Soth 
could have an army of servants."
"DEFENSES & IMMUNITIES:"
This is where Brother Marius's expression becomes grave:
"Magic Resistance: Advantage on saving throws against spells and magical 
effects. Your standard combat magic is less effective.
Damage Immunities: Completely immune to necrotic and poison damage. 
Cannot be poisoned.
Damage Resistances: Resistant to non-magical weapon damage. 
You need magical weapons to hurt them effectively.
Condition Immunities: Cannot be charmed, exhausted, frightened, 
paralyzed, or poisoned. Standard control effects won't work.
Undead Nature: They don't need air, food, drink, or sleep. You can't outlast 
them or siege them out.
Regeneration: Some death knights regenerate health over time unless 
damaged by radiant or holy sources."
"WEAKNESSES - HOW TO FIGHT THEM:"
Brother Marius's tone becomes more hopeful:
"Radiant Damage: This is your best weapon. Holy magic, divine smites, 
anything channeling positive energy or godly power. Brother Cyrus's Sacred 
Flame, his channel divinity - these are your primary offensive tools.
Magic Weapons: Your enchanted weapons will be effective where mundane 
ones fail. Johannes, your eldritch blasts count as magical damage - you can 
hurt it.
Turn Undead: A powerful cleric can potentially turn a death knight, forcing 
it to flee. It's difficult - they have strong will - but possible. Cyrus, your Turn 
Undead feature would be critical.
Dispel Magic: Their spell effects can be countered or dispelled like any other 
magic.
Holy Ground: They're weakened or repelled by consecrated ground or holy 
relics. If you can lure them onto blessed territory, their power diminishes.
Destroy the Curse: This is theoretical, but if you could discover 
the source of their curse - what betrayal bound them - it might be possible to 
break the curse and destroy them permanently. This would require 
investigation and divine intervention."
"TACTICAL RECOMMENDATIONS:"
Brother Marius looks at each of you:
"Brother Cyrus is your MVP in this scenario. His radiant damage, Turn 
Undead, and divine magic are your primary offensive and defensive tools. 
Keep him alive at all costs.
Avoid direct confrontation if possible. Death knights are nearly 
unbeatable in straight combat unless you significantly outnumber them or 
have powerful divine support. Reconnaissance and avoidance should be your 
priority.
Use magical weapons exclusively. Non-magical weapons are nearly 
useless.
Spread out during combat. That Hellfire Orb has a 20-foot blast radius. If 
you're clustered, it can wipe your entire party in one attack.
Flee if necessary. There is no shame in retreating from a death knight. 
They're apex predators among undead. Getting intelligence and surviving is 
worth more than dying heroically.
Look for the patrol's remains. If the Dragon Army soldiers died fighting a 
death knight, their bodies will tell you how the combat went and what killed 
them. That's valuable tactical information."
"ADDITIONAL RESOURCES:"
Brother Marius produces a small wooden case. Inside are three vials of 
glowing silver liquid and three small holy symbols.
"Holy Water - three vials. Deals 2d6 radiant damage to undead on a direct 
hit. Not much, but it might buy you a critical moment.
Blessed Symbols of Paladine - three amulets. Not magical items, but 
blessed by the church. They won't protect you from harm, but they might 
provide advantage on saving throws against fear effects or undead command. 
Wear them openly.
These are yours for the mission. Consider them insurance."
He closes the case and hands it to Cyrus. "May Paladine watch over you. Death 
knights are... they're tragedies, in a sense. Once-noble warriors corrupted and 
cursed. But that doesn't make them less dangerous."
 
Laurana watches this exchange, then adds: "Based on this information, my

We need to know what the Dragon Army was after, not dead heroes."
She looks at Johannes specifically. "Does this information change your 
assessment of the mission? Are you willing to proceed, or do you need 
different resources?"
Johannes, how do you respond? Do you want to:
1.	Accept the mission with current resources
2.	Request additional support (more clerics, more holy items, backup 
team)
3.	Decline the mission as too dangerous
4.	Propose an alternative approach
I am good. Thoughts? Kessa? Cyrus?
Dec 10
Kessa's Assessment:
Kessa has been listening intently, her expression thoughtful. She leans back 
against the table and crosses her arms.
"Reconnaissance I can do. That's what I'm good at. Stealth, observation, 
getting in and out without being seen." She taps the map. "The problem is if 
we get spotted. Death knight or not, we're talking about a fortress - limited 
exits, defensive terrain, potentially hostile undead. If things go sideways, 
extraction becomes... complicated."
She looks at the blessed symbols and holy water. "That said, we've handled 
worse odds. The aboleth, the Dragon Army fleet, Pax Tharkas. We plan well, 
we adapt, we survive." A slight smile. "And honestly? Finding out what the 
Dragon Army wants badly enough to risk a cursed fortress? That's worth the 
danger. If they're desperate enough to go there, it's probably something 
we really don't want them to have."
She nods once. "I'm in. But we do this smart - scout the village first, gather 
local intel, approach the keep carefully, and have an escape plan before we go 
inside."
 
Cyrus's Assessment:
Brother Cyrus is quiet for a long moment, his hand resting on the wooden case 
containing the holy water and blessed symbols. When he speaks, his voice is 
measured and serious.
"I won't lie - this terrifies me. Death knights are..." He pauses, choosing his 
words carefully. "They're what happens when someone with power and 
purpose falls completely. They're warnings. Cautionary tales made flesh and 
darkness."
He looks up at you and Kessa. "But that's also why we should go. If Lord Soth 
is real, he's suffering an eternal curse - trapped, corrupted, unable to find 
peace. And if the Dragon Army thinks they can use him or whatever's in that 
keep, they'll bring even more suffering to the world."
His expression firms with resolve. "Mishakal teaches that healing isn't always 
about mending flesh - sometimes it's about preventing greater wounds. If we 
can stop the Dragon Army from gaining whatever they're after, we prevent 
untold casualties down the line."
He picks up one of the blessed symbols, examining it. "And practically 
speaking? Brother Marius is right - I'm the key to our survival if we encounter 
undead. Turn Undead, radiant damage, healing to keep us mobile. I can do 
this."
A pause, then quieter: "After Flotsam, after the dock rescue... I understand 
now that sometimes the only way to save lives is to face the darkness directly. 
I'm ready."
He looks at Johannes. "I'm with you. But Kessa's right - we need a solid plan 
and clear escape routes. Going in blind would be foolish."
 
Laurana's Conclusion:
Commander Laurana has been watching this exchange with approval. "Good. 
You're thinking like professionals, not glory-seekers."
She pulls out a supply requisition form. "You'll have standard mission 
support: rations for two weeks, rope, climbing gear, torches, anything 
reasonable you need from our stores. We'll also provide three Potions of 
Healing each - I want you to have emergency resources."
"Timeline: Take three to four days to reach Dargaard Village, gather local 
intelligence, assess the situation. Another day to scout the keep's exterior. 
Then you make the call on whether to enter or report back for additional 
resources. Don't take unnecessary risks."
She looks each of you in the eye. "You've earned my trust through consistent 
results and good judgment. I'm trusting you to use that judgment here. If the 
situation is beyond your capabilities, retreat. We can always mount a larger

"Any final questions before you prepare to depart?"
Johannes, are you ready to:

DAY 1-3: JOURNEY TO DARGAARD MOUNTAINS
The first three days of travel are straightforward - following established roads 
northeast through rolling farmland that gradually gives way to rocky hills and 
sparse forest. The weather holds clear and cool.
As you travel, the terrain becomes progressively more desolate. Farms become 
fewer and more rundown. The few travelers you pass seem hurried, unwilling 
to make eye contact or engage in conversation. There's a palpable sense of 
unease the closer you get to the mountains.
By the afternoon of the third day, the dark peaks of the Dargaard Mountains 
loom ahead - jagged, forbidding, shrouded in perpetual mist at their heights.
DAY 4: APPROACH TO DARGAARD VILLAGE (Morning)
The village comes into view around mid-morning. It's small - maybe forty 
structures, mostly simple wooden homes and a few stone buildings. Smoke 
rises from chimneys, but the place has a quiet, subdued quality. No children 
playing in the streets. No market bustle.
And dominating the view to the north, perched on a high rocky promontory 
perhaps 5 miles distant, is Dargaard Keep.
Even from this distance, it's imposing. Dark stone towers reach toward the 
grey sky, partially collapsed but still menacing. The walls are intact in places, 
breached in others. At this distance, you can see no lights, no movement, no 
signs of life - but there's an undeniable presence to the structure. Something 
watchful.
As you enter the village, a few residents glance at you nervously, then quickly 
look away. An old woman sweeping her doorstep makes a warding gesture and 
hurries inside.
The village has a small inn - The Weary Traveler - a general store, a 
blacksmith's forge (cold, no smoke), and what appears to be a small shrine to 
Mishakal at the village center.
How do you want to approach gathering information in Dargaard 
Village? And where do you want to start?
Actually, can we clear out any unnecessary items from our Bags of Holding, 
like Lucien's body. It isn't doing us any good and should be turned over if it 
wasn't already. Also, let's liquidate any non-magical items we might still be 
carrying. I want our affairs to be as in order as possible.
Dec 10
Excellent point - let's handle housekeeping before the mission 
begins.

DARGAARD VILLAGE - MID-MORNING, DAY 4
The party enters the village proper, and the atmosphere is unmistakably tense. 
The few villagers visible on the streets give you wary glances before hurrying 
about their business. The place has the feel of a community that's learned to 
keep its head down and avoid trouble.
The village layout is simple:
*	The Weary Traveler Inn (two-story building, looks like the social 
hub)
*	General Store (shuttered, but smoke from chimney suggests 
someone's inside)
*	Blacksmith's Forge (cold, no activity)
*	Shrine to Mishakal (small stone structure at village center, well-
maintained)
*	Various homes (scattered, modest, quiet)
And looming in the distance to the north, visible between 
buildings: Dargaard Keep, dark and brooding on its high promontory.
As you walk toward the inn, an elderly man sitting on a bench outside quickly 
stands and moves inside. A woman hanging laundry freezes, watches you pass, 
then continues her work with nervous energy.
The Weary Traveler Inn:
The door creaks as you enter. The common room is dim - only a few candles lit 
despite the daylight outside. There are perhaps six people inside: an innkeeper 
behind the bar (middle-aged woman, tired eyes), two farmers nursing ale in 
the corner, and an elderly couple eating a quiet breakfast.
All conversation stops when you enter. Eyes turn to you - not hostile, but 
deeply cautious.
The innkeeper wipes her hands on her apron and approaches, her voice low. 
"Travelers. We... we don't get many travelers here." She glances toward the 
northern window - toward the keep - then back to you. "Looking for rooms? 
Meals?"
Her tone suggests she's hoping you're just passing through.
How do you want to approach this? Johannes, do you:
1.	Take the lead in conversation
2.	Let Kessa handle it (she's good with people)
3.	Let Cyrus speak (cleric of Mishakal might put them at ease)
4.	All introduce yourselves together
And what's your initial approach - direct questions about the keep, 
or ease into it?
3
Dec 10
Cyrus Steps Forward
Brother Cyrus moves to the front, his manner calm and non-threatening. He's 
wearing his holy symbol of Mishakal openly, and his demeanor radiates the 
peaceful authority of a healer rather than a warrior.
"Peace be with you, goodwife," he says gently. "We're not here to cause 
trouble. My name is Brother Cyrus, a cleric of Mishakal. These are my 
companions, Kessa and Johannes."
The innkeeper's posture relaxes slightly when she sees the holy symbol. The 
elderly couple at the table exchanges a glance - recognition, perhaps relief.
"I'm Marda," the innkeeper says, her voice still cautious but less tense. "Marda 
Greystone. This is my inn." She gestures to the tables. "You're welcome here, 
of course. We... we serve Mishakal too." She nods toward the window. "The 
shrine outside - we maintain it. It's... it's important to have the Healing 
Goddess watching over us."
One of the farmers in the corner speaks up, an older man with weathered 
hands. "You're from Haven, aren't you? We heard about the resistance. About 
the Dragon Army being pushed back."
There's a mixture of hope and fear in his voice - hope that someone is fighting 
back, fear of what that might bring to their doorstep.
Cyrus nods. "We are. But we're not here to bring war to your village. We're 
here seeking information." He pauses, choosing his words carefully. "We've 
heard there was... activity. Dragon Army soldiers heading toward the keep. We 
need to know what happened."
The room goes very quiet. Marda's face pales slightly. The elderly man at the 
table makes the same warding gesture you saw earlier.
The farmer who spoke stands slowly. His name, you learn, is Torval. He's 
perhaps sixty, with the look of someone who's seen too much.
"You're asking about the keep," he says quietly. "About what happened to 
those soldiers." He looks at Marda, who gives a small nod. "Sit down. I'll tell 
you what we know. But first..." He looks at Cyrus specifically. "First, tell me 
true - are you here to fight whatever's up there? Or just to look?"
His tone suggests the answer matters greatly to him.
How does Cyrus respond?
We are not sure, to be honest. This keep only came to our attention based on 
the report of the Dragon Army visit. We are trying to see what they are 
looking for and how it might affect the resistance. As for fighting, it depends 
on what we find. If there is a threat, we will determine if we can do something 
or if the resistance needs to commit more resources. But if it is a threat to you, 
we will do what we can.
Dec 10
Cyrus delivers Johannes's words with his characteristic honesty and calm 
authority. "We're not sure, to be honest. This keep only came to our attention 
based on the report of the Dragon Army visit. We're trying to see what they're 
looking for and how it might affect the resistance."
He pauses, meeting Torval's eyes directly. "As for fighting - it depends on what 
we find. If there's a threat, we'll determine if we can handle it or if the 
resistance needs to commit more resources. But if it's a threat to you, to this 
village, we'll do what we can."
Torval studies Cyrus for a long moment, then nods slowly. "Honest answer. I 
appreciate that." He gestures to a table. "Sit. I'll tell you what happened."
 
TORVAL'S ACCOUNT:
Once you're seated and Marda has brought mugs of weak ale, Torval begins:
"About eight days ago - maybe nine - we saw them. Dragon Army patrol, 
maybe fifteen, twenty soldiers. They came through the village just after dawn, 
heading north toward the keep. Their officer - dragonborn, red scales - he 
stopped here, asked questions."
Marda interjects: "Wanted to know about the keep. Its history. Whether 
anyone had been inside recently. Whether we'd seen... him." She doesn't say 
the name, but everyone knows who she means.
Torval continues: "I told him the truth - no one goes near the keep. Not for 
generations. Not since..." He trails off, then pushes forward. "The officer 
seemed satisfied. Said they were conducting a 'historical survey' for the 
Dragon Army. Paid for supplies - food, rope, torches. Then they headed up the 
mountain road."
He takes a drink. "That was eight days ago. We haven't seen them since."
The elderly man at the other table speaks up, his voice thin: "But 
we've heard things. Three nights ago, there was... screaming. Carried on the 
wind from up there. And lights - not torches, but cold blue lights in the 
towers."
The elderly woman beside him adds quietly: "And the ravens. So many ravens, 
circling the keep. They don't usually do that."
Marda's addition: "Two days ago, my nephew Dren - he's twelve, foolish 
boy - he took his father's spyglass and climbed the ridge to the east where you 
can see the keep better. He came back white as a sheet, wouldn't talk for 
hours. Finally told us he saw... movement in the courtyard. Not the soldiers. 
Something else. Dark shapes, moving wrong."
Torval leans forward. "Here's what you need to understand about Dargaard 
Keep, and about Lord Soth. The stories aren't just stories. My grandfather's 
grandfather saw the keep on the night of the Cataclysm - saw it burning with 
cold fire, heard screaming that lasted until dawn. And since then, no one who's 
gone inside has come back out."
He counts on his fingers: "Twenty years ago, a group of treasure hunters - six 
of them, well-armed. Gone. Thirty-five years ago, a scholar from Palanthas 
with two guards. Gone. Fifty years ago, a young knight seeking to 'cleanse' the 
keep. Gone."
"The keep doesn't kill quickly. It keeps people. You hear them sometimes, on 
quiet nights. Voices on the wind."
The elderly woman speaks again: "Lord Soth was a good man once. My 
grandmother told stories her grandmother told her - how he protected the 
region, how he was noble and just. But something broke in him. Some terrible 
choice, some betrayal. And when the Cataclysm came, instead of dying clean, 
he was cursed. Bound to the keep, bound to his guilt, bound to relive his 
failure forever."
She looks at Cyrus directly. "You serve Mishakal. You know about curses, 
about how the gods punish betrayal. Lord Soth is still being punished. Three 
hundred years of torment. And whatever those Dragon Army soldiers wanted 
from him... it woke something up. The keep's been quiet for years. Now 
it's active again."
 
PRACTICAL INFORMATION:
Torval pulls out a rough map on a piece of cloth - clearly something the village 
has used before:
"The mountain road is about five miles. Takes two, maybe three hours on foot 
- it's steep and rocky. The keep sits on a promontory - sheer cliffs on three 
sides, only one approach from the south. There's a gatehouse, mostly intact, 
then the main courtyard. The great hall still stands, and three towers - 
northeast, northwest, and one over the main entrance."
He points to various spots on the map. "The east wall partially collapsed 
during the Cataclysm - there's rubble and a possible way in if the main gate is 
blocked or watched. The dungeons are beneath the main structure - flooded in 
places, we think."
Marda adds: "If you're going up there, go in daylight. Things are... worse at 
night. The screaming, the lights, the feeling of that place - it's all worse after 
dark."
 
Torval looks at the three of you seriously. "I'll be honest - I'm hoping you'll go 
up there, find those Dragon Army bastards dead, realize there's nothing to be 
gained, and report back to Haven that the keep should be left alone. Sealed. 
Forgotten."
"But if you do go inside..." He reaches into his pocket and pulls out a small 
carved wooden token - a symbol of Mishakal. "Take this. My wife carved it 
before she died. It won't protect you from steel or magic, but it might... remind 
whatever's up there that you serve the gods of light, not darkness."
He offers it to Cyrus.
Does Cyrus accept? And what other questions do you want to ask 
before potentially scouting the keep?
Torval needs that token more than we do. Not because it isn't important, but 
its power comes from Torval's personal connection with it. That's not 
something that can be shared. But we have our own tokens. And the thought 
is deeply appreciated. Since we won't leave until morning, we make 
arrangements to spend the night. If there is anyone who needs healing, we 
invite them to come to the inn so Cyrus can administer to them before we go 
to sleep.
Dec 10
Torval's Reaction:
The old farmer pauses, the token still in his outstretched hand, then slowly 
closes his fingers around it. His eyes glisten slightly.
"You understand," he says quietly. "Most wouldn't. Most would just take it and 
think themselves protected." He tucks the token back into his pocket, over his 
heart. "Thank you. And... may Mishakal watch over you. You'll need her more 
than we will."
 
LODGING ARRANGEMENTS:
Marda nods gratefully. "I have three rooms available. Two silver per room for 
the night, includes breakfast. It's simple fare, but it's honest."
She glances toward the window - the keep is visible in the distance, dark 
against the grey sky. "You're staying the night before going up there? That's... 
wise. The road is treacherous if you're not familiar with it, and you don't want 
to be caught up there after dark."
Cost: 6 silver total for three rooms
 
CYRUS'S HEALING OFFER:
When Cyrus announces that he'll provide healing to anyone in the village who 
needs it, there's a moment of stunned silence. Then Marda's expression shifts - 
something between hope and disbelief.
"You... you'd do that? For free?"
"We haven't had a healer visit in over a year," Torval says quietly. "The last 
cleric who came through charged two gold per casting. Most folks here can't 
afford that."
Marda quickly moves to the door and steps outside. Within minutes, word has 
spread through the village with remarkable speed.
 
THE HEALING LINE (Afternoon):
Over the next few hours, a steady stream of villagers comes to the inn. They're 
hesitant at first, but Cyrus's genuine warmth and professional manner puts 
them at ease.
Those who come:
1.	Old Gareth (elderly farmer, chronic back pain from decades of labor) -
 Lesser Restoration eases the persistent inflammation
2.	Young Willem (14 years old, broke his arm three weeks ago, set 
poorly) - Lesser Restoration corrects the improper healing
3.	Marda's sister, Elda (persistent cough, possibly consumption) -
 Lesser Restoration clears the infection
4.	A young mother, Sera (exhaustion, malnourishment from giving 
most of her food to her children) - Cure Wounds + advice on nutrition
5.	Old Thom (partial blindness from cataracts) - Cyrus can't fix this 
permanently without Greater Restoration, but explains honestly what 
would be needed
6.	A child, maybe 7 (infected cut on leg, beginning to fester) - Cure 
Wounds + proper bandaging
7.	Torval himself (arthritis in hands and knees) - Lesser 
Restoration provides significant relief
Between major healings, Cyrus provides basic medical care - cleaning wounds, 
advising on care, offering prayers and comfort.
 
THE VILLAGE'S RESPONSE:
By evening, the atmosphere in the village has shifted dramatically. People are 
smiling - genuinely smiling - for the first time since you arrived. Children are 
playing outside. There's life here again, however brief.
Marda refuses to take payment for the rooms. "After what Brother Cyrus has 
done? Your coin's no good here. The rooms are yours, and dinner too."
Torval approaches your table during the evening meal - simple stew, bread, 
and ale, but prepared with obvious care.
"You asked earlier what we knew about the keep, about Lord Soth. Let me tell 
you something else - something important." He sits down, his voice low 
enough that only your table can hear.
"The Dragon Army officer who came through - the dragonborn - he asked 
specifically about the Chapel. Wanted to know if it was still standing, if anyone 
had been inside, if we knew what was kept there."
He leans forward. "The Chapel of the Order was where Lord Soth kept his 
most sacred items - relics of Paladine, artifacts from his service as a knight. 
After the Cataclysm, after the curse... legend says those holy items 
became twisted. Corrupted. But still powerful."
"If the Dragon Army is looking for something specific, it's probably in that 
Chapel. And if Lord Soth is protecting anything, it'll be that."
He stands. "Thought you should know. Give you something specific to look 
for."
 
EVENING AT THE INN:
As darkness falls, the mood in the common room is surprisingly warm despite 
the ominous presence of the keep in the distance. Villagers who were healed 
earlier have brought small gifts - a loaf of fresh bread, a wheel of cheese, a 
bottle of decent wine.
Marda serves dinner and the common room gradually fills with locals - not 
celebrating exactly, but finding comfort in community after months of fear 
and isolation.
From the northern window, you can see Dargaard Keep silhouetted against the 
darkening sky. As full night falls, you notice what the villagers mentioned: 
faint blue-white lights appearing in the towers. Not torchlight. Something else. 
Something cold.
And if you listen carefully, carried on the wind, you might hear something that 
could be the wind through ruined stone... or could be distant voices, crying 
out.
 
NIGHT PREPARATIONS:
Before bed, the party has time to:
*	Discuss tomorrow's approach
*	Prepare spells (Cyrus can choose his prepared spell list)
*	Check equipment
*	Rest and recover
How do you want to approach tomorrow? And Cyrus, what spells 
are you preparing for an undead-infested cursed fortress?
That is up to you (Ai is playing Cyrus), but we get all the sleep we can, good 
food in the morning and then head out.
Dec 10
CYRUS'S SPELL PREPARATION:
That evening, Cyrus spends an hour in meditation and prayer, preparing his 
spells for what lies ahead. Given the likelihood of undead, curses, and the need 
for survival, he selects:
Cantrips: Sacred Flame, Spare the Dying, Guidance, Light, Thaumaturgy
1st Level (4 slots): Cure Wounds, Healing Word, Bless, Detect Evil and 
Good
2nd Level (3 slots): Lesser Restoration, Prayer of Healing, Spiritual 
Weapon
3rd Level (3 slots): Mass Healing Word, Dispel Magic, Spirit Guardians
4th Level (2 slots): Death Ward, Freedom of Movement
Prepared for: Undead encounters, curse removal, party survivability, 
radiant damage, and emergency healing.
 
NIGHT AT THE INN:
The party rests well - the beds are simple but clean, and the village's gratitude 
has created an atmosphere of genuine safety despite the ominous keep 
looming in the darkness.
During the night, around 2 AM, Johannes (with his Trident of Warning 
keeping him alert) hears the distant sound carried on the wind - that eerie 
wailing from the keep. It lasts perhaps ten minutes, then fades. Nothing 
approaches the village.
 
MORNING - DAY 5
Dawn breaks grey and cool. Marda serves a solid breakfast - porridge, fresh 
bread, eggs, bacon, and strong tea. The common room is quiet, with a few 
early-rising villagers watching you prepare with somber expressions.
Torval approaches as you're finishing. "The morning's clear. Good visibility for 
the road. You'll reach the keep by mid-morning if you keep a steady pace." He 
pauses. "I'll be honest - I hope you come back before nightfall. We all do."
Several villagers have gathered outside - not to see you off exactly, but to 
witness. There's a sense that something significant is happening, that the 
keep's long silence is ending one way or another.
An elderly woman presses a small loaf of bread wrapped in cloth into Kessa's 
hands. "For the road. And... thank you. For what your cleric did yesterday."
 
THE MOUNTAIN ROAD - MID-MORNING
The path to Dargaard Keep is exactly as described - steep, rocky, winding up 
through increasingly barren terrain. The forest gives way to scrub, then to bare 
rock. The temperature drops as you climb.
After about two and a half hours of steady climbing, you round a bend and 
there it is:
DARGAARD KEEP - EXTERIOR VIEW
The fortress sits on a high promontory, commanding views of the surrounding 
valleys. It's massive - easily 200 feet on each side, with three towers rising 60-
80 feet into the air. The architecture is classic Solamnic - strong, elegant, built 
to last centuries.
But the Cataclysm left its mark. The eastern wall has partially collapsed, 
leaving a tumbled slope of massive stone blocks. Scorch marks blacken the 
stone in places - not from normal fire, but something else. Something that 
burned with unnatural heat. Windows are dark, empty eye sockets. The main 
gate hangs partially open, one massive door twisted off its hinges.
And there's an atmosphere to the place. The air feels heavier here, colder 
despite the morning sun. Birds don't fly near it. No vegetation grows within 
fifty feet of the walls.
You're currently about 400 feet from the main gate, on the southern approach 
- the only accessible path. The gatehouse is partially intact, with murder holes 
and arrow slits visible above. The courtyard beyond is visible through the 
damaged gate - overgrown with dead vegetation, littered with rubble.
WHAT YOU CAN SEE FROM HERE:
*	Main gate (damaged, partially open)
*	Gatehouse (intact but dark)
*	Eastern wall breach (possible alternate entry, 150 feet right of main 
gate)
*	Three towers: Northeast, Northwest, and Central (over main entrance)
*	Faint blue-white glow visible in upper windows of Northeast tower
*	No visible movement
*	No signs of the Dragon Army patrol (no bodies, no equipment, no 
campfires)
Kessa murmurs: "Place feels wrong. Like it's watching us."
Cyrus: "I can feel it too. Mishakal's presence is... distant here. Muted. 
Whatever curse binds this place, it's powerful."
How do you want to approach? Johannes, what's the plan?
I never like going through the front door. If the eastern wall is accessible and 
safe, let's go in that way.
Dec 10
APPROACH TO EASTERN WALL BREACH
"Agreed," Kessa says quietly. "Front gates are where defenders expect you. 
And where they set traps."
The party circles wide, keeping distance from the keep while moving toward 
the collapsed eastern section. The terrain is rough - loose scree and broken 
stone - requiring careful footing.
As you get closer, the scale of the destruction becomes apparent. The eastern 
wall didn't just collapse - it exploded outward. Massive stone blocks, each 
weighing tons, are scattered across the slope like a giant's discarded toys. The 
scorch marks here are more intense, with strange patterns that suggest the 
stone melted and re-solidified in the instant of destruction.
BREACH ASSESSMENT (100 feet out):
The collapsed section creates a rough ramp of rubble leading up and into what 
appears to be the keep's interior. The breach is about 40 feet wide. You can see 
into a large chamber beyond - partially exposed to the sky where the roof 
collapsed.
Kessa scouts ahead (Stealth check with expertise): She moves forward 
carefully, using the rubble for cover, watching for trip wires, pressure plates, 
or signs of recent passage.
After five minutes, she returns. "Good news and bad news. Good news - no 
traps that I can see, and there are recent boot prints in the dust inside. Dragon 
Army was definitely here, and they used this entrance."
"Bad news - the prints go in, but I didn't see any coming back out. And there's 
something else..." She pauses. "The air coming from inside is cold. Not natural 
cold. Wrong cold."
Cyrus casts Detect Evil and Good (10-minute duration, 30-foot radius):
He closes his eyes, focusing. After a moment, his expression tightens. 
"There's... something. Undead presence, multiple sources. Not close - maybe 
100, 150 feet beyond the breach, deeper in the structure. And something else... 
aberrant. Unnatural. The whole place radiates wrongness."
He opens his eyes. "Whatever's in there, it knows we're here. Or will know the 
moment we enter. Places like this are aware."
FINAL APPROACH DECISION:
You're 100 feet from the breach. The interior chamber beyond is partially lit by 
dim grey daylight filtering through the collapsed roof. You can see:
*	Rubble-strewn floor
*	Partial walls creating shadowed alcoves
*	Doorways leading deeper into the keep (north and west)
*	Boot prints in the dust heading northwest
*	No immediate movement or threats
Before entering, do you want to:
1.	Buff before entry? (Bless, Guidance, etc.)
2.	Light sources? (Cyrus has Goggles of Night, but Johannes and Kessa 
will need light unless you use Kessa's darkvision and have Johannes use 
eldritch sight)
3.	Marching order? (Who goes first, second, third?)
4.	Any specific precautions or preparations?
This is your last moment of relative safety before entering 
Dargaard Keep. What's your final loadout and approach?
Buff as possible for all. Kessa goes first, followed by Johannes and Cyrus side 
by side, where they can cover Kessa's progress. No light; darkvision, googles, 
and Devil's Sight going forward.
Dec 10
FINAL PREPARATIONS BEFORE ENTRY
The party takes a few minutes to prepare, huddled behind a large piece of 
rubble about 80 feet from the breach.
BUFFS APPLIED:
Cyrus casts Bless (Concentration, 1 minute duration):
*	Johannes, Kessa, and Cyrus each gain +1d4 to attack rolls and saving 
throws
*	Cyrus will maintain concentration as long as possible
Cyrus uses Guidance (as needed):
*	Can provide +1d4 to ability checks for anyone about to make a critical 
roll
EQUIPMENT CHECK:
*	Kessa: Hand crossbow loaded, daggers ready, Ring of Feather Falling 
attuned, darkvision (60 ft)
*	Johannes: Eldritch blast ready, Devil's Sight (120 ft magical darkness 
vision), all attunements active
*	Cyrus: Holy symbol visible, Goggles of Night providing darkvision (60 
ft), shield and mace ready
MARCHING ORDER: Kessa (point, stealth) ? 15 feet ? Johannes & Cyrus 
(side by side, covering)
NO LIGHT SOURCES - Full dark operations using:
*	Kessa's natural darkvision (60 ft)
*	Johannes's Devil's Sight (120 ft, sees through magical darkness)
*	Cyrus's Goggles of Night (60 ft darkvision)
The party can operate in complete darkness, invisible to anyone watching 
from deeper in the keep who might be relying on torchlight or normal vision.
 
BREACH ENTRY
Kessa moves first, low and quiet (Stealth: 24), using the rubble for cover. She 
pauses at the lip of the breach, scanning the interior with her darkvision, then 
signals back: Clear, come forward.
Johannes and Cyrus advance together, weapons ready but not drawn 
aggressively. The three of you slip through the breach and into Dargaard 
Keep.
 
INTERIOR - EASTERN CHAMBER
You're standing in what was once a large barracks or common hall - roughly 
60 feet by 40 feet. The Cataclysm's destruction is evident:
What you see:
*	Partially collapsed roof allowing grey daylight through gaps
*	Rubble-covered floor with clear paths between debris
*	Three doorways: one northwest (boot prints lead here), one north, one 
west
*	Remnants of bunks and furniture, rotted to skeletal frames
*	Scorch marks on walls showing the same unnatural burning pattern
*	Boot prints clearly visible - multiple sets, recent (within the last 
week), all heading northwest
*	The air is unnaturally cold and still
*	Dust hangs in the air, undisturbed except where the patrol walked
Cyrus's Detect Evil and Good (still active): He points northwest. "The 
undead presence is that direction. Multiple entities, moving slowly. Maybe 120 
feet distant, through walls."
Kessa examines the boot prints (Investigation: 19): "Fifteen to twenty 
individuals, just like the report. They moved cautiously but not stealthily - 
they weren't expecting trouble. Prints are consistent with Dragon Army 
regulation boots. All going northwest, none coming back. No signs of combat 
here - no scuff marks, no blood, no dropped equipment."
She looks up at you. "They went in confident. Question is, did they find what 
they were looking for, or did it find them?"
The three doorways:
1.	Northwest doorway (where boot prints lead): Leads into darkness, 
seems to open into a larger space. The cold air is strongest from this 
direction.
2.	North doorway: Smaller, leads to what might be a corridor. No boot 
prints.
3.	West doorway: Partially blocked by rubble. Looks like it leads toward 
the keep's exterior walls.
Johannes, what's your call? Follow the patrol's trail northwest, or 
investigate one of the other routes first?
west. I want to make sure there is nothing behind us before we move too far 
into the Keep
Dec 10
TACTICAL DECISION - SECURE THE FLANKS
"Smart," Kessa murmurs. "Clear our six before we go deep. Last thing we need 
is something coming up behind us."
Cyrus nods agreement, adjusting his grip on his mace. "The undead aren't 
moving toward us yet. We have time to be thorough."
 
WESTERN DOORWAY INVESTIGATION
Kessa approaches the west doorway carefully. It's partially blocked by rubble - 
a section of the upper wall has collapsed inward, creating a pile of stone blocks 
about 4 feet high that partially obstructs the passage.
Kessa examines the rubble (Investigation: 16): "Stable. Old collapse, not 
recent. No sign the Dragon Army tried to move through here - dust is 
undisturbed." She peers over the rubble pile into the darkness beyond. 
"Passage continues about 15 feet, then opens into another chamber. I can see... 
looks like exterior wall with arrow slits. Might be a guard room or defensive 
position."
Cyrus checks with Detect Evil and Good: "No undead presence in that 
direction. Whatever's active in the keep, it's not behind us."
Kessa climbs over the rubble (Athletics: 14, successful): She moves 
quietly through the narrow passage and into the chamber beyond, 
disappearing from view for about thirty seconds. Then she returns, climbing 
back over.
"Guard room, like I thought. Twenty by twenty feet, arrow slits overlooking 
the southern approach - would have given defenders a clear view of anyone 
coming up the road. Three skeletons in armor slumped against the walls - 
looks like they died during the Cataclysm and stayed dead. No movement, no 
magic, just bones."
She brushes dust off her hands. "Room's a dead end - literally. No other exits 
except back this way. Nothing threatening, nothing valuable that I could see in 
a quick scan."
CLEAR - Western route secured, no threats.
 
NORTHERN DOORWAY INVESTIGATION
"North next?" Kessa asks, already moving toward the smaller doorway.
This passage is clearer - no rubble blocking it. It's a standard corridor, about 5 
feet wide, leading north into darkness. The walls here show less fire damage, 
suggesting this section was more protected during the Cataclysm.
Kessa scouts forward (Stealth: 26): She advances about 30 feet down the 
corridor, checking for traps, pressure plates, or signs of recent passage. The 
corridor turns west after 30 feet, and she pauses at the corner, listening.
She returns silently. "Corridor runs north thirty feet, then turns west. From 
the corner, I could see it opens into a larger space - maybe another hall or 
room. No boot prints, no recent traffic. But..." She frowns. "I heard something. 
Faint. Could be wind through broken stone, could be something else. Distant, 
rhythmic. Like... breathing, but slow. Very slow."
Cyrus checks Detect Evil and Good: "There's an undead presence in that 
direction, but distant. Maybe 80-100 feet through walls. It's not moving. 
Just... existing."
Johannes, you have options:
1.	Investigate north corridor fully - clear the entire route, see what's 
in that larger chamber
2.	Mark north as 'investigated but not cleared' - you know what's 
there generally, move on
3.	Follow the Dragon Army trail northwest - you've secured 
immediate flanks, time to track the patrol
What's your call?
Investigate north thoroughly.
Dec 10
NORTHERN CORRIDOR - FULL INVESTIGATION
"Let's clear it completely," Johannes decides. "I want to know what we're 
dealing with before we commit to the main trail."
Kessa nods and moves forward again, the party following in formation - Kessa 
leading by 15 feet, Johannes and Cyrus side by side behind her.
 
THE CORRIDOR (30 feet north, then turns west)
The passage is relatively intact - stone walls show minimal damage, though the 
air grows progressively colder as you advance. Your breath mists in the 
darkness.
At the corner, Kessa signals a halt and peers around carefully.
What Kessa sees (Perception: 21):
The corridor opens into a chapel - roughly 40 feet by 30 feet. Even in the 
darkness visible through darkvision, the room's purpose is clear:
*	Stone altar at the far end (north wall), cracked but intact
*	Pews overturned and scattered
*	Shattered stained glass windows on the east and west walls
*	Religious iconography - symbols of Paladine - defaced and broken
*	A figure kneeling before the altar - humanoid, motionless, facing 
away from you
The rhythmic sound Kessa heard is clearer now - it's coming from the figure. A 
slow, rasping breath. In... out... in... out... like someone in deep meditation or 
prayer.
Cyrus's Detect Evil and Good: "Undead. Definitely undead. That figure at 
the altar." His voice is barely a whisper. "Single entity, not moving. But the 
presence is... strong. This isn't a mindless zombie."
Kessa reports back (whispering): "One undead, kneeling at the altar. 
Hasn't reacted to us yet - either doesn't know we're here or doesn't care. No 
sign of the Dragon Army patrol. No other exits visible from this angle, but the 
room's not fully clear - could be doorways on the sides I can't see from here."
The figure continues its slow breathing, unchanged.
Johannes, you have several options:
1.	Observe longer - try to identify what type of undead this is before 
engaging
2.	Attempt to bypass - back out quietly, leave it undisturbed
3.	Engage from range - Johannes and Cyrus prepare attacks, Kessa 
provides flanking
4.	Cyrus attempts Turn Undead - might cause it to flee or might 
trigger combat
5.	Try communication - some intelligent undead can be reasoned with
What's your approach?
Do we think this is the Chapel that Torval mentioned?
Dec 10
STRATEGIC ASSESSMENT
Johannes freezes, processing what he's seeing. He whispers back to the others: 
"Wait. Torval mentioned the Chapel of the Order - where Lord Soth kept 
sacred relics and artifacts. Said the Dragon Army officer specifically asked 
about it. Is this that chapel?"
Kessa frowns, studying the room more carefully. "It's a chapel, but... this feels 
small for what Torval described. This is maybe a private prayer room or guard 
chapel. Twenty soldiers stationed here would need something bigger for 
formal services."
Cyrus, still sensing the undead presence, whispers: "The Chapel of the Order 
would be in the keep proper - likely off the great hall or near the lord's 
quarters. This is eastern barracks territory. This would be for common 
soldiers, daily prayers, small ceremonies."
He pauses, thinking. "But that doesn't mean it's not important. If this undead 
is praying or maintaining vigil, it might be bound here for a reason. Could be 
a fallen knight, a priest, someone cursed to eternal penance."
Kessa adds: "The Dragon Army patrol didn't come through here - no boot 
prints in the corridor. Which means either they knew this wasn't the main 
chapel, or they had intelligence pointing them elsewhere. They went northwest 
from the entry chamber, remember?"
Johannes's tactical assessment:
This IS a chapel, but probably NOT the Chapel of the Order that the Dragon 
Army was seeking. That would be deeper in the keep, likely more central and 
grander. However, this undead figure could still be:
1.	A guardian - protecting this section of the keep
2.	A bound spirit - cursed to pray eternally for its sins
3.	A potential source of information - if intelligent and 
communicative
4.	A distraction - something to avoid while pursuing the main objective
The question is: Do you want to engage with this undead now, or 
bypass it and follow the Dragon Army trail to what's likely the 
MAIN chapel?
What's your decision?
We need to get a sense of how the denizens of the Keep are going to interact 
with us. Rather than assuming immediate hostility, let's announce our 
presence, and our intent, which is not to loot, steal, or desecrate, not even to 
study, but to determine if this place poses a threat to our interests, and to 
determine if the occupants would be interested in assistance (religious, 
magical, etc.) in their circumstances or just to be left alone.
Dec 10
A BOLD APPROACH
Kessa's eyes widen slightly. "You want to talk to it?" Her tone isn't dismissive - 
more impressed and cautious.
Cyrus considers this, then nods slowly. "It's... not a terrible idea. If Lord Soth 
and his knights are truly cursed rather than simply evil, they might respond to 
respect and honesty. And if they attack, we're prepared."
Johannes steps forward carefully, moving past Kessa to the corner where he 
can see into the chapel. He takes a breath, then speaks clearly but respectfully 
into the darkness - his voice carrying but not aggressive:
"We seek no treasure, no relics, and intend no desecration. We are Johannes 
Constantinius, Kessa Darrow, and Brother Cyrus of Mishakal. We've come to 
determine whether this place poses a threat to the living, and whether those 
who dwell here require aid - be it spiritual, magical, or simply to be left in 
peace."
 
THE FIGURE'S RESPONSE
For a long moment, nothing changes. The slow, rasping breathing continues. 
Then, gradually, it stops.
The silence is profound.
The figure at the altar moves - slowly, deliberately. It rises from its kneeling 
position with the careful movements of someone who has been still for a very, 
very long time. As it stands and turns to face you, you can see it clearly:
A knight in full plate armor, tarnished and ancient but still intact. The armor 
bears the symbols of the Knights of Solamnia - the kingfisher and rose. The 
helmet's visor is closed, but through the eye slits, you can see a faint blue-
white glow.
No flesh. No life. Just animated armor and the cold light of undeath.
When it speaks, the voice is hollow, echoing as if from a great distance. Not 
hostile, but profoundly weary:
"Three hundred years."
A pause.
"Three hundred years I have knelt here. Praying. Waiting. Hoping 
that Paladine would hear. That Mishakal would answer. That the 
gods would show mercy."
The knight takes one step forward, then stops, as if respecting the distance 
between you.
"But the gods do not answer. They turned away on the night of fire. 
When the world broke. When we broke."
The blue glow in the eye slits focuses on Cyrus specifically.
"You wear the symbol of the Healing Goddess. She who tends the 
wounded. Eases suffering." The voice cracks slightly, an emotion breaking 
through centuries of numbness. "Can she ease our suffering? Can she 
heal what was broken that night? Or are we beyond her grace?"
The knight's gauntleted hand moves to its chest, over the heart.
"I am - was - Sir Caradoc. Knight of the Crown. I served Lord Soth. 
I followed him. I stood by him when I should have stopped him. 
And when the curse fell... I could not die clean. None of us could."
"You ask if we pose a threat. We pose no threat to the innocent. We 
cannot leave. We are bound here. Bound to this place, to our 
failure, to our lord's damnation."
"You ask if we require aid." A bitter, hollow laugh. "Yes. We require 
the mercy of oblivion. But that mercy is denied us. We are cursed to 
remember. To witness. To endure."
Sir Caradoc looks past you, toward where you entered.
"But you spoke of others. Others came. Eight days past. Dragon 
Army soldiers. They did not announce themselves with honor. They 
came seeking power. Seeking our lord. Seeking to bargain with the 
damned."
The knight's tone darkens.
"They found him. In the Great Hall. And he... listened to them."
 
Cyrus steps forward carefully, his holy symbol visible:
"Sir Caradoc, I am Brother Cyrus, servant of Mishakal. Your suffering is heard, 
even if you believe the gods do not answer. Tell us - what did the Dragon Army 
want? What bargain did they offer Lord Soth?"
What does Johannes want to ask or say to Sir Caradoc?
The Disks have returned to the face of Krynn. The gods are ready to interact 
with mankind again, suggesting that whatever time or trial they have been 
called to endure can be at an end. We do not have the Disks with us, but they 
are available, if needed. But what happened to Soth after he met with the 
soldiers. Did he agree to anything? We do not seek to ask you to counter your 
lord's wishes; you have been faithful to your loyalty, despite its cost to you. We 
would not counter or risk that, but if there is aught we can do to help, help us 
understand what that is.
Dec 10
SIR CARADOC'S REACTION
The knight goes utterly still at Johannes's words. The blue glow in his eye slits 
flickers, intensifies.
"The Disks... returned?"
His voice is barely a whisper, as if speaking the words too loudly might shatter 
the hope behind them. The gauntleted hand at his chest trembles slightly.
"Three hundred years we have prayed. Three hundred years of 
silence. And now... now you say the gods have returned their grace 
to the world?"
Sir Caradoc takes a shuddering breath - unnecessary for an undead, but the 
memory of breathing, the habit of emotion expressed through mortal gesture.
"If this is true... if the gods truly hear again... then perhaps..." He 
stops, as if afraid to complete the thought. Then, more firmly: "You honor 
us with your offer. And you honor us more by not asking us to 
betray our oaths."
He straightens, and for a moment, you can see the knight he once was - proud, 
honorable, unbowed.
"I will tell you what I know. Not because I betray Lord Soth, but 
because if the gods have returned, then perhaps there is still 
purpose to our suffering. Perhaps witness can still matter."
 
SIR CARADOC'S ACCOUNT:
"Eight days ago, the Dragon Army came. Fifteen soldiers, led by a 
dragonborn officer named Vraxxis. They entered through the 
eastern breach, as you did. But they came with knowledge - they 
knew where to go, knew what to seek. Someone had given them 
intelligence about this place."
"They went directly to the Great Hall. To where Lord Soth... waits. 
Always waits. Reliving his failure, his damnation, over and over in 
an endless cycle."
"I could not follow - I am bound to this chapel, to my penance. But 
the others... the skeletal warriors who patrol the keep, the spirits 
bound to their posts... they reported what they witnessed."
"The dragonborn spoke to Lord Soth. Offered him a bargain."
Sir Caradoc's voice becomes strained, as if the words pain him to speak:
"They offered him purpose. Release from his endless cycle of 
torment. They said the Dragon Army seeks to reshape Krynn, to 
bring order through strength. They need commanders who 
understand true power, true sacrifice. They offered Lord Soth 
command of an undead legion - to fight, to serve, to have meaning 
again rather than eternal stagnation."
"And they offered him something else. Something from the Chapel 
of the Order. A relic he kept there before the Cataclysm. They 
claimed they could restore it, purify it, give him back a piece of 
what he lost."
The knight's voice drops to barely audible:
"The Starjewel. A holy relic of Paladine, given to Lord Soth when he 
achieved the rank of Knight of the Rose. It was his most treasured 
possession. When the curse fell, it became... corrupted. Tainted. A 
reminder of his fall rather than his glory."
"The Dragon Army claimed they had a cleric of Takhisis powerful 
enough to cleanse and re-sanctify it. To give Lord Soth back his 
honor, symbolically if not in truth."
 
THE BARGAIN:
"Lord Soth... listened. For the first time in three hundred years, 
he listened to someone. The Dragon Army offered him what we all 
crave - release from meaningless suffering. Purpose instead of 
punishment."
"But he did not agree immediately. Lord Soth is proud, even in 
damnation. He gave them a test."
"He sent them to the Chapel of the Order to retrieve the Starjewel 
themselves. If they could navigate the keep, survive its guardians, 
and bring the relic back to him, he would consider their offer. If 
they failed... well, their bones would join the others who have tried 
to plunder this place."
Sir Caradoc gestures northwest, in the direction the boot prints led.
"They went. Seven days ago. The Chapel lies in the keep's north 
wing, past the Great Hall, through the Gallery of Ancestors. It is... 
well-defended. The most sacred space in the keep, where the curse 
is strongest."
"I do not know if they succeeded. I have not seen them return. I 
have not heard Lord Soth's summons to the Great Hall. The keep 
has been... waiting."
 
SIR CARADOC'S PLEA:
The knight looks directly at Cyrus, then at Johannes.
"If the gods have truly returned, if Mishakal can hear prayers 
again, then perhaps there is hope for us. Not salvation - we are too 
far gone for that. But perhaps... purpose. Perhaps our suffering can 
mean something."
"If Lord Soth joins the Dragon Army, if he leads an undead legion, 
he will bring death and horror to thousands. He is a tactical genius, 
a warrior without peer, and completely without mercy. The Dragon 
Army would gain a weapon of terrible power."
"But if you could offer him something else... if you could bring 
proof that the gods have returned, that there is another path 
besides endless torment or service to Takhisis..."
He trails off, then adds more quietly:
"Or if you could stop him. Destroy the Starjewel before the Dragon 
Army can use it as leverage. Deny them their weapon. Even if it 
means we remain cursed forever."
"I have been loyal to Lord Soth for three hundred years. But I was 
loyal to the knight he was, not the death knight he became. If you 
can prevent him from spreading more suffering, more death... that 
would honor the man he once was."
 
PRACTICAL INFORMATION:
"The Dragon Army patrol went northwest from the entry chamber, 
into the Servants' Hall, then through to the Great Hall. From there, 
north through the Gallery of Ancestors to the Chapel of the Order. 
That is the route. You will face skeletal warriors - mindless, but 
deadly. You will face the spirits of those who died here - they are... 
less predictable. And if you reach the Chapel..."
He hesitates.
"Lady Korinthe guards it. Lord Soth's first wife. She died in the 
Cataclysm, in the fire, and she blames him for her death. She has 
become... something terrible. A banshee, filled with rage and grief.
