She cannot leave the Chapel, but within it, she is nearly 
unstoppable."
"If the Dragon Army soldiers are still alive, they are likely trapped 
there, unable to retrieve the Starjewel, unable to retreat."
 
Sir Caradoc waits for your response, the blue glow in his eye slits steady now. 
He has unburdened himself of information he's carried for days, and there's a 
sense of relief in his posture despite the weight of his words.
Johannes, how do you respond? And what is your plan?
I thank you for your honesty, Ser. We will also visit your Lord, and receive his 
permission to investigate the Chapel and what it holds. As we have said, we 
are not here for sordid mortal needs, but we seek to do what is right as it is 
given for us to know. If we are successful, we will do what we can to allow you 
the rest so long denied you. And we will leave word with the Clerics in Haven, 
that even should we fall, the Disks can be brought here, if needed, to end your 
vigil once and for all.
Dec 10
SIR CARADOC'S FAREWELL
The knight is silent for a long moment. Then, slowly, he places his right fist 
over his heart - the formal salute of the Knights of Solamnia. The gesture is 
precise, practiced, unchanged by three centuries of undeath.
"You have given me something I had not felt in three hundred 
years, Johannes Constantinius. Hope."
His voice is steadier now, stronger.
"You speak with honor. You approach our lord with respect rather 
than greed or fear. This... this is how knights once conducted 
themselves. How we once conducted ourselves, before the fall."
He lowers his hand.
"Go to the Great Hall. Announce yourself as you announced 
yourself to me - with honesty and respect. Lord Soth is... proud. 
Bitter. Consumed by his guilt and rage. But he was once the finest 
knight of his generation. That man still exists, buried beneath the 
curse. If anyone can reach him, it might be those who approach 
without deception."
"And if you succeed in bringing the Disks here, if the gods can 
finally grant us release..." His voice cracks slightly. "Then we will have 
endured for purpose. Our three hundred years of suffering will 
have meant something. We will have borne witness to darkness, 
and at the end, we will have been seen by the light."
He steps back toward the altar, then pauses.
"One more thing. When you face Lady Korinthe in the Chapel... do 
not fight her with steel or spell alone. She is grief and rage made 
manifest. If you must confront her, remember she was once a 
woman who loved deeply, who was betrayed, who died in terror 
and pain. She is as much a victim of the curse as any of us."
"Perhaps words of truth and compassion will reach her where 
violence cannot. Perhaps a servant of Mishakal can do what three 
hundred years of isolation could not."
He kneels once more before the altar, resuming his vigil position.
"May the gods you serve watch over you. And may you survive to 
bring their mercy to those of us who thought mercy lost forever."
The blue glow in his eye slits dims as he returns to his meditation, the slow 
rasping breath beginning again.
 
CYRUS'S REACTION:
As you leave the chapel and return to the corridor, Cyrus is visibly moved. He 
wipes his eyes.
"Three hundred years. Three hundred years of prayer with no answer. And he 
still hopes. Still believes." He grips his holy symbol. "Johannes, if we survive 
this, if we can help them... bringing the Disks here might be the most 
important thing we ever do."
KESSA'S ASSESSMENT:
"So we're going to walk up to a death knight and ask permission to investigate 
his cursed chapel? That's..." She pauses, then smiles slightly. "Actually 
brilliant. Respectful, unexpected, and if he says no, we've learned something. 
If he says yes, we have safe passage."
She checks her weapons. "Though I'm betting the Dragon Army didn't ask 
permission, which is why they might be trapped or dead in that Chapel."
 
ROUTE TO GREAT HALL:
You return to the eastern entry chamber. The boot prints still lead northwest 
through the doorway you haven't yet investigated.
The party prepares to follow the Dragon Army's trail to confront 
Lord Soth himself.
Marching order remains the same? Kessa forward, Johannes and 
Cyrus behind? And you're maintaining Bless and full dark 
operations?
Ready to proceed to the Great Hall?
Cyrus should go first, his mantle and tokens of office on full display. We follow 
a few steps behind. I encourage Cyrus to repeat the gist of what was shared 
with Caradoc, and in the same manner, when we reach Soth.
Dec 10
REVISED FORMATION - HERALD APPROACH
"Johannes is right," Cyrus says, his voice steady despite the gravity of what 
they're about to do. "If we're approaching as emissaries rather than intruders, 
I should lead. This is a matter of faith, honor, and divine authority. That's my 
domain."
He adjusts his holy symbol of Mishakal so it catches what little light there is, 
prominently displayed on his chest. He straightens his posture - no longer the 
cautious adventurer, but a cleric on holy business.
Kessa nods. "I'll stay close behind you two. If things go wrong, I can provide 
cover. But let Cyrus do the talking."
NEW MARCHING ORDER: Cyrus (leading, visible holy authority) 
? 5 feet ? Johannes & Kessa (flanking support)
Bless still active (6 more rounds/~36 seconds remaining)
 
NORTHWEST PASSAGE - FOLLOWING THE DRAGON ARMY 
TRAIL
Cyrus leads through the northwest doorway, following the clear boot prints in 
the dust. The passage is a wide corridor - 10 feet across - with vaulted ceilings 
that speak to the keep's former grandeur. Scorch marks mar the walls, and the 
air grows progressively colder.
After 30 feet, the corridor opens into a larger chamber.
SERVANTS' HALL (40 ft x 50 ft)
Once a bustling area where the keep's staff worked and lived. Now:
*	Long tables overturned and rotted
*	Scattered bones (non-animated) wearing the remains of servant clothing
*	Boot prints continue straight through, heading north toward a large 
archway
*	Two skeletal warriors standing motionless on either side of the north 
archway, wearing tattered Solamnic tabards, rusty swords in hand
The skeletons don't move or react as you enter. They simply stand at 
attention, like guards at their eternal post.
Cyrus pauses, then speaks clearly: "We come in peace, seeking audience with 
Lord Soth. We mean no desecration or theft."
The skeletons' empty eye sockets track his movement, but they make no 
hostile action. After a moment, one raises its sword in a vertical salute - the 
formal acknowledgment of one knight to another passing through their post.
Then both resume their motionless guard positions.
"They're... letting us pass," Kessa whispers, clearly impressed and unnerved.
 
THROUGH THE ARCHWAY - APPROACH TO GREAT HALL
Beyond the archway is a grand corridor - 15 feet wide, 20 feet high, with 
remnants of tapestries hanging in tatters. The boot prints continue forward.
At the end of this 40-foot corridor, you can see massive double doors, partially 
open. Cold blue light spills through the gap, and you can hear something:
A woman's voice, singing.
Not live singing - this is ethereal, distant, like a memory of music. The song is 
in a language you don't understand, but the emotion is unmistakable: grief, 
loss, accusation. The melody is beautiful and heartbreaking.
Cyrus recognizes it (Religion check: 18): "That's The Lament of Isolation - 
an old Solamnic funeral dirge. It's sung for those who die without honor, 
without redemption. It's... it's what Lady Korinthe would have sung for Lord 
Soth, if he had died clean."
The singing continues, echoing through the stone halls.
As you approach the doors, you can see into the Great Hall beyond:
*	Massive chamber, 80 feet long and 60 feet wide
*	High vaulted ceiling with collapsed sections letting in grey light
*	A throne at the far end, facing the entrance
*	Skeletal warriors (12-15) standing along the walls like statues
*	Ghostly figures (5-6) floating near the ceiling, translucent and ethereal
*	And on the throne, unmoving:
LORD SOTH
Even from 60 feet away, his presence is overwhelming. Full blackened plate 
armor wreathed in cold flames that don't consume. A greatsword laid across 
his lap. The helmet's visor open, revealing a skull with points of burning blue-
white light in the eye sockets.
He is perfectly still, staring forward at nothing, as the lament continues to sing 
around him.
The Dragon Army soldiers are visible too - their corpses, scattered around 
the hall. Fifteen bodies in Dragon Army uniforms, some skeletal, some 
partially preserved by the unnatural cold. They died violently - crushed armor, 
broken bones, evidence of massive trauma.
They never made it past the Great Hall.
 
Cyrus stops at the threshold, standing in the doorway where the light from 
outside meets the cold blue glow from within. He takes a breath, then speaks - 
his voice clear, respectful, carrying the authority of his office:
"Lord Soth, Knight of the Rose, Master of Dargaard Keep. I am 
Brother Cyrus, servant of Mishakal, the Healing Goddess. With me 
are Johannes Constantinius and Kessa Darrow. We come not as 
thieves or desecrators, but as seekers of truth and understanding."
The singing stops.
The silence is absolute.
Lord Soth's head turns - slowly, deliberately - to look at the doorway. At Cyrus. 
At the holy symbol of Mishakal gleaming on his chest.
When he speaks, his voice is like stones grinding together, ancient and heavy 
with centuries of pain:
"A cleric of Mishakal. In MY hall. Speaking of HEALING."
The cold flames around his armor flare brighter.
"What healing can you offer the damned, priest? What 
understanding exists for those who have already lost everything?"
Cyrus, the floor is yours. How do you present your case to Lord 
Soth?
A response based on the introduction we gave to Caradoc, including the 
information about the reemergence of the Disks.
Dec 10
CYRUS'S ADDRESS TO LORD SOTH
Brother Cyrus stands firm in the doorway, his voice steady and respectful, 
showing no fear despite the overwhelming presence before him:
"My lord, we seek no treasure, no relics, and intend no desecration. 
We come to determine whether this place poses a threat to the 
living, and whether those who dwell here require aid - be it 
spiritual, magical, or simply to be left in peace."
He pauses, then delivers the most important news:
"The Disks of Mishakal have returned to Krynn. After three 
hundred years of silence, the gods are ready to interact with 
mankind again. Whatever time or trial you and your knights have 
been called to endure may be at an end."
The cold flames around Lord Soth's armor flicker, dimming slightly. The death 
knight remains motionless, but there's a quality to his stillness now - not the 
frozen stasis of before, but the acute attention of someone hearing something 
they thought impossible.
Cyrus continues, his voice gaining strength:
"We do not have the Disks with us, but they exist. They have been 
found. The gods hear prayers again. Your suffering has been 
witnessed, my lord. Three hundred years of torment, three 
hundred years of isolation - it need not continue forever."
He gestures to the corpses of the Dragon Army soldiers scattered across the 
hall.
"Others came seeking to use your pain for their purposes. To offer 
you false purpose in service to Takhisis and her Dragon Army. But 
we come offering something different - the possibility of true 
resolution. Of ending this curse with divine grace rather than 
exchanging one form of damnation for another."
"Sir Caradoc told us of the Dragon Army's offer. Of the Starjewel. 
Of their test. We ask your permission to investigate what happened 
to these soldiers, to determine what transpired in the Chapel of the 
Order, and to understand what the Dragon Army truly sought 
here."
Cyrus places his hand over his heart in the Solamnic salute:
"We do not ask you to betray your nature or your oaths. We ask 
only to understand the truth of this place, and if it is within our 
power, to help bring you and your knights the mercy that has been 
denied for so long."
 
LORD SOTH'S RESPONSE
The death knight is silent for a long, terrible moment. The skeletal warriors 
along the walls remain frozen. The ghostly figures hover, watching. The only 
sound is the faint whisper of wind through broken stone.
Then Lord Soth rises from his throne.
The movement is fluid, powerful, despite three centuries of sitting. He stands 
at full height - easily six and a half feet tall in his armor - and the greatsword 
remains in his gauntleted hand, point resting on the stone floor.
He descends the steps from the throne platform, walking toward the three of 
you. Each footfall echoes like a death knell. The cold flames around his armor 
cast dancing shadows across the hall.
He stops twenty feet from the doorway, close enough that you can see the 
details of his armor - once magnificent, now scorched and blackened. The 
symbols of Solamnia are still visible, but twisted, corrupted.
"The Disks have returned."
His voice is hollow, devoid of hope but carrying a terrible weight of longing.
"Three hundred years I have sat in this hall. Three hundred years I 
have listened to the lament of my failure. Three hundred years I 
have waited for the gods to speak, to judge, to grant me either 
redemption or oblivion."
"And in all that time, NO ONE has offered mercy. Only fear. Only 
greed. Only hatred."
He looks directly at Cyrus, the burning points of light in his eye sockets boring 
into the cleric.
"You speak of the Dragon Army's offer. You are correct - they 
promised purpose. An end to meaningless suffering. The chance to 
MATTER again, even in service to darkness."
"But you..." He gestures with the greatsword toward Cyrus's holy 
symbol. "You offer something I had thought impossible. You offer 
HOPE."
The word is spoken with such pain, such desperate hunger, that it's physically 
uncomfortable to hear.
"Hope is the cruelest torture for the damned, priest. Because hope 
can be destroyed. And when it is destroyed, the fall back into 
despair is worse than never hoping at all."
He looks at the scattered corpses of the Dragon Army soldiers.
"These fools came with arrogance and greed. They demanded I 
serve them, that I bow to their Dragon Highlords, that I trade my 
eternal punishment for temporary purpose. I gave them a test - 
retrieve the Starjewel from the Chapel. If they could face Lady 
Korinthe and survive, perhaps they were worthy of commanding 
the damned."
"They failed. She destroyed them. Their screams lasted three days 
before the last one fell silent."
He turns back to Cyrus.
"But YOU... you speak of the gods' return. You speak of mercy. You 
offer investigation, understanding, rather than demands or theft."
"Very well. I grant you permission to enter the Chapel of the Order. 
To investigate what the Dragon Army sought. To face Lady 
Korinthe, if you dare."
"But know this: If you lie to me, if the Disks do not exist, if this is 
deception or manipulation... I will hunt you across Krynn. I will 
find you. And your deaths will make these Dragon Army fools look 
merciful."
"And if you speak truth... if the gods truly have returned... then 
bring proof. Bring the Disks here. Let the gods judge me 
themselves. Let them grant me either redemption or the oblivion I 
have craved for three centuries."
He raises the greatsword in formal salute - knight to knight, warrior to 
warrior.
"You have my permission. The skeletal guardians will not attack 
you. The spirits will let you pass. But Lady Korinthe..." His voice 
becomes almost sad. "She is beyond my control. She is rage and grief 
given form. If you can reach her, if you can survive her, then 
perhaps you truly do serve the gods of mercy."
"The Chapel lies north, through the Gallery of Ancestors. Follow 
the corridor past this hall. You will know when you near it - the air 
grows colder, the walls weep blood, and you will hear her singing."
"Go. Investigate. Survive if you can. And if you do survive, if you 
find what the Dragon Army sought, return to me. We will speak 
further of gods, mercy, and the possibility of ending three hundred 
years of damnation."
He turns and walks back to his throne, each step echoing through the hall. He 
sits, lays the greatsword across his lap, and resumes his eternal vigil - staring 
at nothing, waiting for something that may finally, after three centuries, be 
coming.
The skeletal warriors return to their motionless guard positions. The ghostly 
figures fade back into the shadows.
The path north is open.
 
Cyrus exhales slowly, his hand trembling slightly as he lowers it 
from his heart. "That... that worked. I can't believe that worked."
Kessa whispers: "We just got permission from a death knight to investigate 
his cursed chapel. This is either brilliant or insane."
Johannes, you have Lord Soth's permission and safe passage. The 
path to the Chapel of the Order is clear. What do you want to do?
1.	Proceed immediately to the Chapel - follow the north corridor to 
the Gallery of Ancestors
2.	Investigate the Dragon Army corpses first - see what equipment 
or intelligence they might have
3.	Rest and prepare - Bless has expired, you might want to rebuff before 
facing Lady Korinthe
4.	Ask Lord Soth additional questions - you have his attention, 
perhaps there's more to learn
With Soth's permission, we will examine the bodies. Also, please have Cyrus 
query Soth about the nature of his curse, its cause, and how this involves Lady 
Korinthe. If we do face her, we may have to take steps to protect ourselves. 
We do not wish to dishonor her, her pain, or Soth himself, but we also do not 
wish to bring his wrath should anything happen to the Lady.
Dec 10
EXAMINING THE DRAGON ARMY CORPSES
Johannes approaches the scattered bodies carefully, noting Lord Soth's 
unmoving presence on the throne. The death knight doesn't object as you 
begin your investigation.
Kessa assists with the search (Investigation: 21):
The fifteen corpses are in various states of decay - some reduced to skeletons 
in armor, others partially preserved by the unnatural cold. The manner of 
death is consistent and brutal:
"Crushed. All of them," Kessa reports quietly. "Massive blunt force trauma. 
Broken bones, shattered armor. Whatever killed them hit like a battering ram. 
Multiple victims show signs of being... thrown. Slammed into walls with 
enough force to crack stone."
She examines the dragonborn officer's body - identifiable by his rank insignia. 
"Commander Vraxxis. His spine is shattered, ribs pulverized. He died fast, at 
least."
Equipment recovered:
*	Standard Dragon Army gear (swords, spears, shields) - damaged beyond 
use
*	340 gold pieces total (distributed among the soldiers)
*	Maps of the region (nothing you don't already know)
*	Orders signed by a Dragon Highlord: "Secure alliance with Lord Soth or 
retrieve Starjewel for sanctification. Use of force authorized if 
negotiation fails."
*	A sealed scroll case containing a letter of introduction from "High Cleric 
Moranthas of Takhisis"
*	Holy symbol of Takhisis (silver, worth ~50 gp)
*	Rope, torches, rations (standard expedition gear)
Most importantly: A leather journal belonging to Vraxxis. Kessa flips 
through it:
"Detailed intelligence on Dargaard Keep. Someone gave 
them good information - layout, history, even notes on Lord Soth's personality 
and the curse. The last entry is from seven days ago: 'Soth has agreed to test. 
Will retrieve Starjewel from Chapel. If successful, he joins the cause. For 
Queen Takhisis, for the glory of the Dragon Army.'"
Johannes pockets the journal and orders for later analysis.
 
CYRUS'S INQUIRY TO LORD SOTH
While Johannes and Kessa examine the bodies, Brother Cyrus approaches the 
throne platform - not presumptively close, but near enough to speak 
respectfully.
"My lord, if we are to face Lady Korinthe, we would understand what we're 
walking into. Not to dishonor her or her pain, but to approach with wisdom 
rather than ignorance."
He pauses, choosing his words carefully. "You have granted us permission to 
investigate the Chapel. We do not wish to bring your wrath upon ourselves 
should anything happen to the Lady during our encounter. Can you tell us the 
nature of your curse, its cause, and how Lady Korinthe came to guard the 
Chapel?"
 
LORD SOTH'S ACCOUNT - THE CURSE
The death knight is silent for a long moment, as if deciding whether to speak. 
Then, surprisingly, he does - his voice heavy with centuries of guilt:
"You ask about the curse. Very well. If you are to face her, you 
should understand what made us what we are."
"I was once the finest knight of my generation. Knight of the Rose, 
chosen by Paladine himself. I was noble, honorable, good. I had a 
wife - Gladria - and a son. I had duty, purpose, meaning."
"But I was also proud. And when I met Korinthe..." His voice softens 
almost imperceptibly. "She was an elf maiden, beautiful beyond 
measure. I fell in love with her. And in my pride, in my arrogance, I 
believed I deserved that love more than I deserved my duty."
"I betrayed Gladria. I committed adultery. When Gladria 
discovered the truth, she died - some say by her own hand, some 
say by design. The truth is lost to time and guilt."
"But I married Korinthe. Made her my lady. And we had a son 
together."
The cold flames around his armor flicker more intensely.
"Then the gods sent me a vision. A warning. The Cataclysm was 
coming - divine judgment for the Kingpriest's pride. They gave me a 
quest: ride to Istar, stop the Kingpriest, prevent the catastrophe. I 
could save the world."
"But Gladria's relatives accused me before the Knighthood. They 
claimed I had murdered her to marry Korinthe. They said I was 
unworthy, that my son was illegitimate, that I had broken every 
oath I swore."
"And they convinced Korinthe. They poisoned her against me with 
their lies - or perhaps with truth I refused to see. She believed I had 
murdered my first wife. She believed I was a monster."
"I rode to save her honor, to prove my worthiness. But on the road, 
I hesitated. I turned back. I chose Korinthe over the world."
His voice becomes hollow, dead:
"And that is when the Cataclysm struck."
"The gods threw fire from the heavens. Mountains rose, seas fell, 
cities burned. Millions died. And I could have stopped it. I SHOULD 
have stopped it. But I chose personal love over divine duty."
"When I returned to Dargaard Keep, it was burning. Korinthe was 
trapped in the Chapel with our son and her handmaidens. They 
were burning alive. I tried to save them. I tried. But the flames 
were not natural fire - they were divine judgment, and they would 
not be quenched."
"I listened to her scream my name. I listened to my son cry. I 
listened to them die in agony. And I could do nothing."
"That is when the curse fell. The gods judged me. Not for adultery. 
Not for betrayal. But for choosing personal desire over the world's 
salvation. For failing in my moment of greatest purpose."
"I was condemned to become what I am now - a death knight. 
Immortal, powerful, and forever denied what I desire most: death, 
forgiveness, peace. I am cursed to relive that moment every night. 
To hear Korinthe's screams. To remember my failure."
"And Korinthe..." His voice becomes pained. "She died believing I 
betrayed her. Died in terror and agony. And when she rose as a 
banshee, she rose with that belief intact. She blames me for her 
death. For our son's death. For everything."
"She guards the Chapel because that is where she died. That is 
where the Starjewel rests - the symbol of my supposed honor, now 
corrupted and tainted. She will not let anyone take it. Not the 
Dragon Army. Not you. Not even me."
"If you face her, you face three hundred years of rage, grief, and 
betrayal given supernatural form."
 
LORD SOTH'S WARNING:
"Lady Korinthe's wail can kill. Literally. Those who hear her death 
scream at full force die instantly if their will is not strong enough. 
Her touch drains life itself. She can phase through walls, become 
incorporeal, and she is immune to most forms of harm."
"But she is also trapped by her grief. She believes I murdered 
Gladria. She believes I am a monster. And she is RIGHT to believe 
it, because I AM a monster. But not for the reasons she thinks."
"If you wish to survive her, you cannot fight her with steel alone. 
You must reach through the rage to the woman she was. You must 
make her see truth - not the lies she died believing, not the hatred 
that sustains her, but the actual, terrible truth."
"That I loved her. That I failed her. That I chose her over the world, 
and the world burned because of that choice."
He looks directly at Cyrus:
"If you can make her understand that her death was not murder 
but the consequence of divine judgment for MY sin... if you can 
make her see that she is as much a victim as I am a perpetrator... 
then perhaps, PERHAPS, her rage will falter."
"But I warn you: the truth may not set her free. It may only make 
her angrier. Because the truth is that she died for MY choices, MY 
failures, MY sins. And that is a burden even a banshee's rage 
cannot fully express."
"As for protecting yourselves..." He considers. "Her wail can be 
resisted with strong will. Her touch can be avoided if you are swift. 
And she is a creature of negative energy - radiant damage, holy 
power, these will harm her. But most importantly: if you harm her, 
if you destroy her, I will consider it an attack upon what remains of 
the woman I loved. And you will answer to me."
"So you face an impossible choice: survive her without destroying 
her. Reach her without breaking her. Or die trying."
He gestures toward the north corridor:
"The Gallery of Ancestors lies that way. Follow it to its end. You will 
find the Chapel. And you will find Lady Korinthe, singing her 
eternal lament."
"If you survive, return to me. If you do not..." A pause. "Your bodies 
will join the others. And I will continue waiting."
 
The information is laid bare. You know the curse, you know Lady 
Korinthe's nature, and you know the stakes.
Cyrus looks shaken. "He's asking us to face a banshee powerful enough to 
kill fifteen Dragon Army soldiers, survive her wail and her rage, and somehow 
reach through three hundred years of pain to help her... without destroying 
her."
Kessa: "And if we hurt her, Soth kills us. No pressure."
Johannes, what's your plan? Do you want to:
1.	Proceed immediately to the Gallery - while the information is 
fresh
2.	Prepare and buff - Bless has long expired, you might want Protection 
from Evil and Good, Death Ward, etc.
3.	Discuss strategy - how exactly do you approach a banshee without 
fighting her?
4.	Ask Lord Soth anything else - any final questions before you go?
Any final insights before we face her? Is there anything you would have us tell 
her, even if she is not capable of hearing them?
Dec 10
LORD SOTH'S FINAL WORDS
The death knight rises from his throne once more - a gesture of respect for the 
question, perhaps, or simply the weight of what he's about to say.
He walks to the edge of the platform, looking down at the three of you. The 
cold flames around his armor dim slightly, and for just a moment, you can 
almost see the knight he once was beneath the curse.
"What would I have you tell her?"
His voice is quieter now, almost human in its pain:
"Tell her... tell her I am sorry. Not the empty apology of a man 
seeking forgiveness, but the acknowledgment of one who truly 
understands what was taken from her."
"Tell her that she was right to hate me. That her rage is justified. 
That I DID fail her, though not in the way she believes."
"Tell her that our son - Peradur - died calling for both of us. That 
his last word was not a curse, but a child's cry for his parents. Tell 
her that I heard him. That I will always hear him."
He pauses, the burning points of light in his eye sockets dimming:
"Tell her that if I could trade places with her, if I could bear her 
curse instead of my own, I would do so without hesitation. Not to 
ease my own suffering, but to ease hers."
"Tell her that she deserved better than me. Better than this. Better 
than three hundred years of rage in a chapel where she died in 
terror."
"And tell her..." His voice becomes almost a whisper, "...that I loved her. 
Truly loved her. And that love was not a lie, even if everything else 
was built on betrayal and failure. The love was real. The love 
was good. And the love is why I failed the world - because in that 
moment, I chose her over everything else."
"Tell her that her death is my greatest punishment. Not the curse, 
not the immortality, not the flames or the endless guilt. But 
knowing that she died believing I murdered her. That she died in 
pain, calling my name in fear rather than love. THAT is my 
damnation."
He returns to his throne slowly, as if the weight of these words has exhausted 
even an undead warrior.
"But Johannes Constantinius..." He looks at you directly. "Know this: 
she may not be capable of hearing. Banshees are creatures of 
singular purpose, locked into the moment of their death and the 
emotion that killed them. Three hundred years of rage and grief 
have calcified around her soul like armor."
"Your words may not reach her. Your compassion may not 
penetrate. And if they do not, if she attacks with full fury, you must 
make a choice: die with honor, or survive by any means necessary 
and face my wrath afterward."
"I do not envy you this task. It is crueler than anything I have faced 
in three centuries."
He gestures one final time toward the north corridor:
"Go. Face what I created through my failures. And if you survive, if 
you somehow reach her, if you can do what I could not... then 
perhaps there is hope for both of us."
"May the gods you serve grant you wisdom I never possessed. You 
will need it."
 
FINAL PREPARATIONS
The path north is clear. Lord Soth has said all he will say. The skeletal warriors 
stand motionless. The ghostly figures watch from the shadows with something 
that might be curiosity or pity.
Cyrus takes a deep breath. "We should prepare. Fully. Lady Korinthe is... 
this is going to be the hardest thing we've ever done. We're not fighting an 
enemy. We're trying to reach a victim through centuries of trauma."
Kessa: "And if we fail, we either die to her wail, or we hurt her and Soth kills 
us. Johannes, we need every advantage we can get."
AVAILABLE PREPARATION OPTIONS:
1.	Cyrus can cast buffs:
*	Bless (concentration, +1d4 to attacks and saves for all three)
*	Death Ward (4th level, target doesn't die from next instance of 
damage that would reduce them to 0 HP)
*	Protection from Evil and Good (advantage on saves vs undead, 
they have disadvantage to hit you)
*	Aid (increases max HP for all three)
2.	Consume resources:
*	Holy Water (3 vials available, 2d6 radiant damage to undead)
*	Potions of Healing (emergency backup)
*	Blessed symbols (advantage vs fear effects)
3.	Strategic discussion:
*	Who speaks to Korinthe?
*	What's the approach - immediate dialogue or cautious entry?
*	What's the emergency retreat plan if things go catastrophically 
wrong?
How do you want to prepare, and what's your strategy for 
approaching Lady Korinthe?
Suggestions, guys?
Dec 10
PARTY STRATEGY DISCUSSION
The three of you move to a corner of the Great Hall, speaking in low voices 
while Lord Soth remains motionless on his throne.
 
CYRUS'S RECOMMENDATIONS:
"We need to maximize our survivability and our chances of being heard. 
Here's what I'm thinking:"
Buffs:
*	Death Ward on all three of us - "Her wail can kill instantly. This 
gives each of us one guaranteed save from death. It's our insurance 
policy." (Uses both 4th-level slots, would need to choose who gets the 
third)
*	Bless - "The +1d4 to saving throws could be the difference between 
resisting her wail or dying."
*	Protection from Evil and Good on Johannes - "You'll be doing 
the talking. You need advantage on saves against her, and she'll have 
disadvantage attacking you. It's concentration, so I can't stack it with 
Bless, but if you're the primary target..."
Approach: "Johannes should speak. You made the connection with Caradoc, 
you negotiated with Soth. You have the diplomatic instinct. I'll support with 
spiritual authority, but this needs to be personal, human connection, not just 
priestly platitudes."
"Kessa and I should stay back initially - not cowering, but not threatening. Let 
Johannes try to reach her first. If she attacks, we react, but our goal is survival 
and retreat, not combat."
Emergency Plan: "If she unleashes her full wail, if multiple people drop, we 
RUN. Grab whoever fell, use Healing Word to get them conscious, and we 
retreat to the Great Hall. Soth gave us permission to try - he didn't demand we 
succeed or die. There's no shame in recognizing when we're outmatched."
 
KESSA'S TACTICAL ASSESSMENT:
"I hate everything about this, but here's my thinking:"
Positioning: "Banshees can phase through walls and become incorporeal. 
There's no 'safe' position. But we should enter spread out - at least 15-20 feet 
between us. Her wail has an area effect. If we're spread, maybe not all of us get 
hit at once."
My Role: "I'm not the diplomat. I'm not the holy warrior. But I'm fast, and I 
have the Ring of Feather Falling. If this goes wrong, if someone drops, I can 
reach them quickly, grab them, and we can retreat down whatever vertical 
surface we need to."
"Also..." She hefts her hand crossbow. "If - IF - it comes to combat and Soth's 
permission somehow extends to defending ourselves, I can provide ranged 
support. But that's absolute last resort."
Reading the Room: "When we enter, I'll be watching her, not speaking. 
Body language, reactions, emotional cues. If Johannes's words are reaching 
her, I'll see it. If she's about to attack, I'll see it. I'll signal if we need to shift 
strategy."
One More Thing: "We wear the blessed symbols openly. They might help 
with her fear effects, but more importantly, they show we're here with divine 
backing. We're not grave robbers or Dragon Army thugs. We're here with 
purpose."
 
KESSA'S QUESTION:
"Johannes, one thing I need to know: Are you planning to tell her about the 
Disks? About the possibility of ending the curse? Because that could go two 
ways - it could give her hope, or it could make her angrier that three hundred 
years of suffering might have been preventable."
 
CYRUS'S ADDITION:
"One more tactical note: Banshee wails target creatures within 30 feet who 
can hear her. If things go catastrophically wrong immediately, we could 
theoretically use Silence to create a zone where her wail doesn't work. But that 
also means we can't speak to her in that zone, so it's purely defensive."
"Also, I'll have Lesser Restoration prepared in case she causes fear effects that 
linger, and Mass Healing Word if multiple people drop. But honestly..." He 
looks grim. "If her wail hits multiple people at once, we're probably done. Our 
best defense is not getting hit in the first place."
 
FINAL RESOURCE ALLOCATION:
Cyrus proposes:
*	Death Ward on Johannes (you're speaking, you're primary target)
*	Death Ward on Cyrus (healer needs to stay alive)
*	Bless on all three (concentration, +1d4 to saves)
*	Save 3rd-level slots for emergency Mass Healing Word or Dispel 
Magic
*	Everyone wears blessed symbols openly
*	Holy water ready but not drawn (don't appear threatening)
"This uses my two 4th-level slots, but it gives us the best chance of surviving 
an instant-kill effect. Kessa, you don't get Death Ward because you're fastest 
and most likely to avoid being primary target. Is that acceptable?"
 
Kessa nods: "I'm good with that. I'll stay mobile, stay alert, and be ready to 
extract if needed."
Both look to Johannes:
"What do you think? Any changes to the buff package? Any specific approach 
you want to take when we enter the Chapel? And are you planning to mention 
the Disks to her?"
Johannes, what's your final strategy?
Actually, hear me out on this. We are dealing with trauma, personal hurt so 
deep it lives beyond death. So this really has nothing to do with Soth. He's 
right; she can't hear him, can't hear any of us. She is trapped in her own vision. 
And that is what has to break. So...what if we were to show her that? I am 
thinking Illusions - mirrors that alternate between her former self and her 
current state. Let her see what her grief has done to her, what it has taken, and 
what it has left behind. Everywhere she turns. Not as accusation, not as 
punishment, but as truth. Truth is the greatest weapon against guilt, against 
pain, because it is real. Immutable. And her grief is, in the end, not truth. It is 
only a facet, a specific perspective. And as such, it doesn't not qualify as truth.
Dec 10
PARTY REACTION TO JOHANNES'S STRATEGY
There's a moment of stunned silence as both companions process what 
Johannes just proposed.
CYRUS'S RESPONSE:
Cyrus's eyes widen, and he grips his holy symbol tightly. "That's... that's either 
brilliant or catastrophically dangerous. Maybe both."
He thinks it through aloud:
"You're right that words alone won't reach her. She's locked in the moment of 
her death, reliving her trauma eternally. Talking at her won't break that cycle - 
she can't hear past her own pain."
"But showing her... forcing her to see herself, to confront what she's become 
versus what she was... that bypasses the verbal. It's direct. Visceral."
He pauses, concern creeping into his voice:
"The risk is that it could enrage her further. Seeing what she's become, seeing 
the beauty she lost, the life that was stolen - it could amplify her grief into fury. 
She might see it as mockery rather than compassion."
"But..." He looks at Johannes with growing conviction. "From a theological 
perspective, this is actually sound. Banshees are trapped by their death-
moment, by a singular fixed perspective. Breaking that perspective, forcing 
them to see beyond the loop they're in - that's how curses break. Not through 
force, but through revelation."
Practical consideration: "You'd need illusions she can't immediately 
dismiss or ignore. Silent Image won't work - she'd see through it instantly. 
You'd need something more real, more undeniable. Major Image would work 
- it has sound, it can move, and it requires an Investigation check to disbelieve. 
But..." He hesitates. "Do you have access to illusion magic? That's not typically 
warlock territory."
 
KESSA'S ASSESSMENT:
Kessa has been listening intently, and she nods slowly. "I hate to say it, but 
Johannes is right. We can't tell her she's trapped. We have to show her."
"Think about it: she died three hundred years ago in terror and pain. She's 
been replaying that moment over and over. Every time she looks around, she 
sees the burning chapel, feels the flames, hears her son crying. That's her 
entire reality."
"If we can show her something different - show her what she was before, show 
her what she's become, show her that there's a reality beyond that single 
moment - it might crack the loop. It might give her perspective."
Tactical refinement: "Here's what I'm thinking: we don't just show her 
images of herself. We show her progression. Start with who she was - Lady 
Korinthe, beautiful, alive, loved. Then show the moment of death - the fire, the 
terror, but also the truth of it being the Cataclysm, not murder. Then show 
what she's become - the banshee, the rage, the three hundred years of 
isolation."
"Make it a narrative. Show her the whole story, not just fragments. Let her see 
the through-line from life to death to undeath. Let her see that her grief has 
trapped her in one moment when there's an entire history she's forgotten."
Kessa's concern: "But Johannes is right - this has to be truth, not 
accusation. We're not saying 'look what you've become, you monster.' We're 
saying 'look at the fullness of your story. See all of it, not just the worst 
moment.'"
 
CYRUS'S SPIRITUAL INSIGHT:
"There's another layer to this," Cyrus adds quietly. "Lady Korinthe believes 
Soth murdered Gladria and then came for her. That's the lie she died 
believing. If we can show her the actual sequence of events - Soth's choice, the 
Cataclysm, the divine judgment, the flames that consumed her - we show her 
she wasn't murdered. She was a casualty of cosmic consequence."
"That doesn't make it better. She still died horribly. Her son still died. But it 
changes the meaning. She's not a murdered victim. She's a tragic casualty of 
Soth's failure to save the world. That's truth. And truth can set people free, 
even the dead."
CRITICAL QUESTION:
"Johannes, you're a warlock. Do you have illusion magic available? Or were 
you thinking we find another way to create these reflections?"
 
ALTERNATIVE APPROACHES IF NO ILLUSION MAGIC:
Cyrus: "If you don't have illusion spells, we could try other methods:
*	I could use Thaumaturgy to create minor sensory effects - echoes of her 
voice when she was alive, flickering images
*	We could speak the story aloud while invoking her memories, painting 
word-pictures
*	There might be actual mirrors in the Chapel - reflective surfaces that 
could show her what she's become contrasted with what she was"
Kessa: "Or we focus on bringing objects that connect to her past. Soth 
mentioned the Starjewel was important to him - were there items important 
to her? Things that remind her of life before death?"
 
THE STRATEGY CRYSTALLIZES:
Core approach: Use reflection - literal or magical - to break Korinthe's 
death-loop by showing her the fullness of her story, forcing perspective 
beyond the single traumatic moment.
Johannes, the questions are:
1.	Do you have access to illusion magic (through spells, items, or 
other means)?
2.	If not, which alternative approach appeals to you - verbal 
narrative, sensory effects, physical mirrors, symbolic objects?
3.	Do you still want the defensive buffs (Death Ward, Bless) in case 
this goes wrong?
4.	Who creates/presents the reflections - Johannes alone, or 
collaborative effort?
What's your refined plan?
All I have is Minor Illusion. But could that be enough? Passing images as we 
speak to her, our words made life?
Dec 10
CYRUS'S EVALUATION OF MINOR ILLUSION
Cyrus considers this carefully, his scholarly mind working through the magical 
theory:
"Minor Illusion... it's limited. A 5-foot cube, static image or sound, no 
movement. But..." His expression shifts. "But used repeatedly, in sequence, 
like pages in a book..."
He looks at Johannes with growing excitement. "Yes. Yes, this could work. 
Here's why:"
THE STRATEGY WITH MINOR ILLUSION:
"You cast it again and again - each casting creates a new still image that lasts 
one minute. You build a gallery of images around her, one after another. Not a 
single moving illusion, but a series of frozen moments that surround her, that 
she cannot escape or ignore."
Sequence of images:
1.	Korinthe alive - beautiful, smiling, radiant. Before the tragedy.
2.	Soth and Korinthe together - the love that was real, even if flawed.
3.	Their son, Peradur - innocent, alive. The life she protected.
4.	The Cataclysm moment - fire falling from the heavens. Divine 
judgment, not murder.
5.	The Chapel burning - showing the cosmic scale, the world breaking, 
not personal betrayal.
6.	Korinthe now - the banshee, wreathed in ethereal fury. What three 
hundred years of grief has made her.
7.	The choice - two images side by side. The woman she was, the creature 
she's become. Past and present.
Kessa interjects: "And while you're creating these images, we speak. We 
narrate the truth. Your illusions give the words form. They become a story she 
can see while she hears. It bypasses her ability to shut us out verbally because 
the images force her to confront what we're saying."
 
CYRUS'S REFINEMENT:
"Here's the critical tactical element: Minor Illusion requires concentration, 
but each casting creates an image that persists. So you cast, the image appears, 
you drop concentration, cast again, new image. You can create multiple 
images simultaneously in the space because you're not maintaining them - 
they exist independently once created."
"It's like... hanging paintings in a gallery. Each one stays until you deliberately 
dismiss it or until the minute duration expires. You could theoretically fill the 
Chapel with seven or eight images, creating an immersive experience she 
cannot escape."
Timing consideration: "Each casting takes an action - six seconds. Seven 
images means 42 seconds of casting time. During that time, you're vulnerable. 
So here's what I propose:"
REVISED TACTICAL APPROACH:
Phase 1 - Entry and Assessment (First 30 seconds):
*	All three enter the Chapel together, spread out (20 feet between each)
*	Cyrus casts Bless immediately (bonus action) - all three get +1d4 to 
saves
*	We announce ourselves respectfully: "Lady Korinthe, we come bearing 
truth and witness"
*	Johannes begins casting Minor Illusion - first image appears
*	We assess her immediate reaction - does she attack instantly, or does 
curiosity/confusion give us a moment?
Phase 2 - Gallery Creation (Next 45 seconds):
*	Johannes continues casting Minor Illusion sequentially, building the 
gallery of images
*	Cyrus and Kessa position defensively, ready to intervene if she attacks
*	We speak while the images appear, narrating the story: "You were Lady 
Korinthe, beloved and beautiful..." (first image appears) "...you loved 
Lord Soth, and that love was real..." (second image appears)
*	Goal: complete 6-7 images before she can fully process and respond
Phase 3 - Revelation (Final minute):
*	All images present, surrounding her
*	Johannes delivers Lord Soth's message directly: his apology, his 
acknowledgment, his love
*	We emphasize: "You are trapped in one moment. But your story is 
larger. See the fullness of what was, what is, and what could be."
*	We offer hope: "The gods have returned. The Disks of Mishakal exist. 
This curse can end."
Emergency Protocols:
*	If she attacks during Phase 1-2, Cyrus casts Death Ward on whoever she 
targets (reaction, uses spell slot)
*	If she unleashes her wail, we make saves with Bless bonus, Death Ward 
catches anyone who fails
*	If multiple people drop, immediate retreat - Kessa grabs fallen, we run
 
KESSA'S ADDITION:
"One more thing: as Johannes creates images, I'll watch her. If an image 
affects her - if she recoils, if she reaches toward it, if she shows any emotional 
response - I'll signal which one hit home. Then you can emphasize that 
moment verbally, reinforce what's breaking through."
"We're essentially forcing her to witness her own story from the outside. To 
see herself as we see her - not as a monster, but as a victim of circumstances 
beyond her control who has agency to choose differently now."
 
CYRUS'S SPIRITUAL FRAMING:
"And here's the theological key: we're not fixing her. We're not curing her. 
We're offering perspective. The choice to change, to release the rage, to accept 
truth over the lie she died believing - that has to be hers. We can only 
illuminate the path. She has to choose to walk it."
"If she chooses continued rage... we retreat. If she chooses to listen... maybe, 
just maybe, we achieve what three hundred years couldn't."
 
FINAL BUFFS BEFORE ENTRY:
Cyrus proposes:
*	Bless on all three (cast immediately upon entry, lasts 1 minute - covers 
the entire encounter)
*	Death Ward held in reserve as emergency reaction (can cast as needed 
if someone's about to drop)
*	Blessed symbols worn openly
*	Holy water accessible but not drawn
*	3rd and 4th level slots preserved for emergency healing/protection
Total resource commitment: 1st level slot for Bless, potentially 4th level 
for Death Ward if needed
 
Cyrus and Kessa both look at Johannes:
"This is your plan. Your vision. We'll support you completely. But you need to 
be ready to cast seven times in quick succession while maintaining composure 
and speaking truth to a banshee. Can you do this?"
Kessa adds: "And one final question: what specifically do you want each 
image to show? We should agree on the sequence now so we're all aligned 
when we speak the narrative."
Johannes, are you ready to commit to this approach? And what 
specific moments do you want each Minor Illusion to depict?
Let's do it, as discussed. In the order and manner discussed. There should be 
enough paintings and portraits in the area that we can get a sense of who she 
was in life. We also include images of her son, but nothing of Soth.
Dec 10
FINAL PREPARATION
"Nothing of Soth," Cyrus agrees. "This is about her story, not his. He's a part 
of the context, but she needs to see herself, her son, her own journey. Smart."
Kessa nods. "Let's scout the Gallery of Ancestors on the way - if there are 
portraits of the family, we can reference them for accuracy. The more true the 
images are, the more they'll resonate."
 
BUFFS APPLIED:
Before leaving the Great Hall, Cyrus prepares the party:
Cast now:
*	Blessed symbols worn openly by all three
*	Equipment check complete
*	Mental preparation
Cast upon Chapel entry:
*	Bless (immediate, all three, +1d4 to attack rolls and saves)
Held in reserve:
*	Death Ward (emergency only, whoever needs it)
*	Mass Healing Word (if multiple people drop)
*	Holy Water (accessible but not threatening)
 
LEAVING THE GREAT HALL
The three of you turn toward the north corridor. As you walk past Lord Soth's 
throne, the death knight remains motionless, but his voice carries across the 
hall one final time:
"You go to face what I could not save. What I created through my 
failure."
A pause.
"If you succeed... if you reach her... tell her I will wait. For as long 
as it takes. For redemption, for oblivion, or simply for the gods to 
finally judge us both."
The skeletal warriors along the walls raise their swords in silent salute as you 
pass - a gesture of respect from those who know what you're about to attempt.
 
GALLERY OF ANCESTORS
The north corridor from the Great Hall is grand but decayed - 15 feet wide, 
lined with alcoves that once held statues and displays. The Cataclysm 
destroyed most, but fragments remain.
After 60 feet, the corridor opens into the Gallery of Ancestors - a long hall 
(80 feet by 30 feet) with high vaulted ceilings. The walls are lined with 
portraits, though many have been damaged by fire, water, and time.
What remains visible:
Portraits of Solamnic Knights - generations of warriors, all in formal 
armor, all bearing the symbols of the Knighthood. Most are too damaged to 
identify.
One large portrait, partially intact - clearly Lord Soth in his prime. 
Young, handsome, confident. The image shows him before the fall - before the 
curse, before the tragedy. A knight at the height of his glory.
Three portraits that survived relatively intact:
1.	Lady Korinthe (full-length portrait, 6 feet tall) - An elven woman of 
extraordinary beauty. Dark hair, luminous eyes, elegant bearing. She 
wears a flowing gown in deep blue, and there's a circlet of silver in her 
hair. She's smiling - not a formal portrait smile, but genuine warmth. 
One hand rests on her heart, the other extends outward in a gesture of 
welcome or blessing. The painting radiates grace and life.
2.	Korinthe with infant (smaller portrait, 3 feet tall) - She holds a baby 
wrapped in white cloth, looking down at him with pure maternal love. 
The child's face is barely visible, but you can see dark hair and tiny 
hands reaching toward her face. The tenderness in the image is 
heartbreaking.
3.	Young boy, perhaps 4-5 years old (portrait, 4 feet tall) - Dark-
haired child with elven features and his mother's luminous eyes. He's 
wearing a small noble's outfit and holding a wooden sword, clearly 
playing at being a knight. He's laughing. This must be Peradur, their 
son.
Kessa studies the portraits carefully (Perception: 22): "These are... these 
are good references. The artist captured not just appearance but personality. 
Look at her expression - that's not formal nobility, that's genuine warmth. And 
the boy... gods, he's just a child."
Cyrus stands before Korinthe's portrait for a long moment. "She was 
beautiful. Not just physically - you can see the kindness in her eyes, the 
openness. This is who we're trying to reach. This is who's trapped beneath 
three hundred years of rage."
Johannes can study these portraits to inform his Minor Illusion 
castings - you now have clear visual reference for:
*	Korinthe's appearance (facial features, clothing, bearing, expression)
*	Her relationship with her son (the maternal bond)
*	Peradur's appearance (young, innocent, full of life)
 
THE CHAPEL DOOR
At the far end of the Gallery, the corridor narrows to a single doorway. The 
door is intact but slightly ajar - ornate oak with silver inlay showing symbols of 
Paladine. The symbols are tarnished and corrupted, but still recognizable.
Cold air seeps through the gap. Colder than anywhere else in the keep. Your 
breath mists heavily.
And you can hear it now - clearly, unmistakably:
Singing.
A woman's voice, ethereal and haunting, singing in Elvish. The melody is 
the Lament of Isolation - the funeral dirge for those who die without honor. 
But the voice carries such pain, such longing, such fury that it's almost 
physically uncomfortable to hear.
The words, translated, speak of betrayal, of fire, of a child's scream, of love 
turned to ash.
Kessa whispers: "She's in there. Right now. Singing."
Cyrus grips his holy symbol: "Last chance to change the plan. Are we 
doing this?"
The door is 10 feet ahead. Beyond it lies the Chapel of the Order, 
Lady Korinthe, and the test of whether truth and compassion can 
reach through three centuries of grief.
Johannes, do you:
1.	Enter immediately - push the door open, commit fully
2.	Take one more moment - final words with companions, final mental 
preparation
3.	Approach differently - announce yourselves before entering, knock, 
something else
What are your final actions before entering the Chapel?
Do it.
Dec 10
ENTERING THE CHAPEL
Johannes pushes the door open.
The hinges don't creak - they're silent, as if the keep itself wants to witness 
what happens next.
 
THE CHAPEL OF THE ORDER
The chamber beyond is roughly 50 feet long and 30 feet wide. Unlike the rest 
of the keep, this space is almost perfectly preserved - as if frozen in the 
moment of the Cataclysm.
What you see:
*	Stone altar at the far end (north wall), still intact, with symbols of 
Paladine carved into it
*	Pews arranged in neat rows, facing the altar - charred but standing
*	Stained glass windows on the east and west walls - shattered, but 
fragments remain showing scenes of knightly virtue
*	Scorch marks everywhere - walls, floor, ceiling - but these aren't 
random. They form patterns, like reaching hands, like grasping flames
*	The Starjewel rests on the altar - a fist-sized gem in a silver setting, 
glowing with sickly green-black light. Once holy, now corrupted.
And floating before the altar, Lady Korinthe.
 
LADY KORINTHE - THE BANSHEE
She hovers three feet above the ground, translucent and ethereal. You can see 
through her to the altar beyond, but she's present in a way that defies the 
semi-corporeal form.
She wears the same flowing gown from the portrait, but it's tattered, burned, 
moving in an unfelt wind. Her dark hair floats around her head like she's 
underwater. Her face...
Her face is beautiful and terrible. The same features from the portrait - the 
luminous eyes, the graceful bone structure - but twisted by grief and rage. Her 
eyes burn with cold blue-white fire. Her mouth is open in song, and when she 
sings, frost forms in the air.
Her hands are extended toward the altar, as if reaching for something that 
isn't there. Or perhaps reaching for her son, who died here.
She doesn't notice you immediately. She's lost in her song, in her eternal 
moment, replaying the death over and over.
 
INITIATIVE
The three of you enter in formation:
*	Cyrus (center, 10 feet inside the door)
*	Johannes (left, 10 feet inside, 20 feet from Cyrus)
*	Kessa (right, 10 feet inside, 20 feet from Cyrus)
Spread out, as planned. Blessed symbols visible.
CYRUS ACTS IMMEDIATELY (Bonus Action):
He raises his holy symbol and casts Bless: "Mishakal, grant us your grace."
Golden light flows from the symbol, touching all three of you. You feel warmth 
despite the cold, clarity despite the fear.
[All three: +1d4 to attack rolls and saving throws for 1 minute]
 
KORINTHE NOTICES
The moment Cyrus's divine magic manifests, her singing stops.
The silence is absolute.
She turns - slowly, like a predator locating prey - and sees the three of you.
Her expression shifts from grief to confusion to fury in the span of a 
heartbeat.
"INTRUDERS."
Her voice is layered - multiple tones at once, as if several versions of her are 
speaking in harmony. The sound reverberates in your bones.
"You DARE enter this place? You DARE stand where my son DIED? 
Where I BURNED?"
She floats forward ten feet, her hands curling into claws. The temperature 
drops another ten degrees. Frost spreads across the floor from where she 
hovers.
"The others came seeking POWER. Seeking to STEAL what is 
MINE. They died screaming. YOU will join them."
 
THIS IS THE MOMENT
She hasn't attacked yet - she's speaking, which means there's a window. But 
that window is closing fast. Her rage is building visibly.
JOHANNES - YOUR TURN
You need to act now. Cast Minor Illusion, speak truth, begin the gallery before 
she unleashes her wail.
What is the FIRST image you create, and what do you say as you 
cast it?
The floor is yours. Cyrus and Kessa are positioned defensively, ready to 
support or react. But this moment - this critical first impression - belongs to 
Johannes.
What do you do?
"What was it that was yours, My Lady? This? Your youth and beauty? I project 
the first image.
Dec 10
JOHANNES'S OPENING MOVE
Johannes raises his hand, his voice steady and respectful despite the 
supernatural terror before him. He casts Minor Illusion.
FIRST IMAGE APPEARS (5-foot cube, to Korinthe's left, 10 feet from her):
Lady Korinthe as she was in life - the portrait come to three dimensions. 
Beautiful, radiant, dark hair cascading down, wearing the elegant blue gown. 
She's smiling that genuine, warm smile. One hand over her heart, the other 
extended in welcome. Alive. Whole. Real.
The image is still, frozen in that moment of grace and life.
 
KORINTHE'S REACTION
She whips her head toward the image, her ethereal form shuddering. The rage 
in her expression falters - just for an instant - replaced by confusion, then 
recognition, then anguish.
"What... what is this... trickery?"
Her voice cracks, the multiple tones becoming discordant. She stares at the 
image of herself, her translucent hand reaching toward it but not touching.
"That was... I was..."
Then the rage returns, defensive, protective:
"You mock me! You show me what was STOLEN! What the flames 
TOOK!"
But she doesn't look away from the image. She can't look away.
 
JOHANNES - YOUR ACTION CONTINUES
You have her attention. The image has pierced through the immediate fury. 
She's engaged, even if it's painful engagement.
What is the SECOND image you create, and what do you say?
Reminder: You can cast Minor Illusion again as an action (6 seconds). The 
first image persists for 1 minute. You're building the gallery sequentially.
Cyrus and Kessa hold position, watching her reaction, ready to 
intervene if needed.
Continue, Johannes. What's the next piece of truth you show her?
"Never, my Lady. I mock nothing. But this" I gesture at the image, " this wasn't 
the truth, was it? You knew change, your youth was only yours for a time. But 
as time passed, other things came, Things even more beautiful. Like this." You 
show her her son.
Dec 10
SECOND IMAGE APPEARS
Johannes casts Minor Illusion again, creating a second image to Korinthe's 
right, opposite the first.
The boy - Peradur - perhaps four years old, dark-haired with his mother's 
luminous eyes. Wearing his small noble's outfit, holding the wooden sword, 
caught mid-laugh. Pure joy, pure innocence, pure life. A child who knew he 
was loved.
The image stands there, frozen in that moment of childhood happiness.
 
KORINTHE'S REACTION
The effect is immediate and devastating.
She makes a sound - not words, but a wail of pure grief that isn't her death 
scream, just raw maternal anguish. She moves toward the image of her son, 
her translucent hands reaching, grasping at air.
"Peradur... my son... my baby..."
All the rage drains from her voice, replaced by heartbreak so profound it's 
almost tangible. She tries to touch the image, her hands passing through it 
uselessly.
"He was so young. So small. He called for me. In the flames, he 
called for me, and I couldn't... I couldn't reach him..."
She's weeping now - if banshees can weep. No tears fall, but her form 
shudders, the ethereal gown rippling with the force of her grief.
"He died afraid. He died calling my name. And I could do 
NOTHING."
She turns back toward you, and the rage is returning, but it's different now - 
not directed at you, but at the universe, at the injustice:
"Soth did this. Soth brought the flames. Soth murdered Gladria 
and brought divine judgment on us all. My son paid for HIS sins!"
 
CRITICAL MOMENT
She's engaged. She's feeling. But she's still locked in her narrative - that Soth 
murdered Gladria, that he's to blame, that she and Peradur were victims of his 
personal evil rather than cosmic consequence.
This is where you need to pivot. To show her the truth of what happened.
JOHANNES - YOUR NEXT MOVE
What is the THIRD image, and how do you bridge from her 
maternal grief to the larger truth about the Cataclysm?
You're doing exactly what you planned - breaking through her rage to the 
grief beneath. Now comes the harder part: showing her that her 
understanding of events is incomplete.
Cyrus and Kessa remain positioned, watching intently. Cyrus's 
hand is on his holy symbol, ready to support if needed.
Continue, Johannes. Show her the truth.
"But, my Lady, truth is greater than ourselves, isn't it? There is more than just 
what WE see, what WE hear, isn't there. The birds sing, just as sweetly, even if 
we are not beneath them circling in the sky. The scent of the rose floats on the 
breeze, even if our noses cannot catch it in the springtime? Yes, your 
experience was as tragic as any in known memory, but it was not the full 
extent of pain, of loss, was it?" I show images of the Cataclysm, of other 
mothers, other children, other innocents lost.
Dec 10
THIRD IMAGE - FOURTH IMAGE - FIFTH IMAGE
Johannes casts Minor Illusion three more times in quick succession, creating 
a panorama of devastation:
Third image (behind Korinthe, forcing her to turn): A city burning - not 
Dargaard Keep, but Istar, or any of a dozen cities. Buildings collapsing. The 
sky itself falling. Mountains rising where plains once stood. The 
world breaking.
Fourth image (to her left): Another mother, another child - humans, 
clutching each other as fire falls from the heavens. Their expressions mirror 
Korinthe's own terror. Different faces, same tragedy.
Fifth image (to her right): More victims - a family huddled together, an 
elderly couple, a young woman alone. All consumed by the same cosmic fire. 
All dying in the same moment across Krynn.
The images surround her now - five frozen moments of the Cataclysm's 
devastation. A gallery of universal suffering.
 
KORINTHE'S REACTION
She spins, looking from image to image, her ethereal form becoming more 
agitated. She sees herself reflected in these other victims - the same terror, the 
same pain, the same innocence destroyed.
"No... no, this is... this was..."
Her voice wavers, the multiple tones becoming uncertain.
"The Cataclysm. The gods' judgment. I remember... the world 
shook. The sky burned. But..."
She looks back at the image of herself alive, then at Peradur, then at the 
burning victims.
"But Soth... he BROUGHT this. He murdered Gladria, he broke his 
vows, he-"
She stops, confusion breaking through the certainty.
"They told me... Gladria's family, they told me he was a murderer. 
That he killed her to have me. That he was corrupt, fallen, 
unworthy..."
Her hands clench and unclench.
"And then the flames came. And he couldn't save us. He stood 
outside and let us BURN. If he loved me, if he was good, he would 
have saved us!"
The rage is returning, but it's defensive now - protecting the narrative she's 
clung to for three centuries because without it, what does her suffering mean?
"Tell me, priest!" She turns toward Cyrus, her voice desperate and 
furious. "Tell me my death meant something! Tell me it was 
MURDER, not just... not just CHANCE! Not just being in the wrong 
place when the gods decided to punish the WORLD!"
 
CRITICAL PIVOT POINT
She's almost there. She's seeing the larger context. But she's resisting because 
if her death wasn't personal - if it wasn't about her, wasn't someone's fault - 
then it was just random cosmic tragedy. And that's somehow worse.
She needs to understand: it WAS personal, but not in the way she thinks.
JOHANNES - NEXT MOVE
This is where you show her Soth's actual choice. Not murder, but a 
different kind of betrayal. The sixth image should show the truth: 
Soth on the road, turning back, choosing her over the world.
What do you create, and what do you say to bridge from "random 
tragedy" to "consequence of choice"?
You're breaking through. Keep going. Cyrus and Kessa are watching, ready 
to support.
"My lady. None of us are ever capable of doing ALL that lies within our power 
to do. We all fall short. Even your husband," an image of him , turning from 
Istar, returning to be by her side, turning from his very oaths out of love for 
her. And then of him, failing to break through the door, body wreathed in fire 
as he is on his knees before the Chapel doors. "But how can we judge the 
failings within ourselves, within others, when we know we cannot know all 
things? As mortals, it falls beyond us. It is the duty and obligations of the 
Gods, is it not?"
Dec 10
SIXTH IMAGE - SEVENTH IMAGE
Johannes casts Minor Illusion twice more, completing the narrative:
Sixth image (central, impossible to ignore): Lord Soth on horseback on a 
mountain road, turning away from a distant city (Istar). His posture shows the 
weight of decision - shoulders slumped, head bowed. Not triumphant, not 
malicious. Just... choosing. Choosing her over the world. Choosing love over 
duty.
Seventh image (directly before the altar, between Korinthe and the 
Starjewel): Soth on his knees before the Chapel doors, the same doors you just 
entered through. His armor is wreathed in flames - divine fire, the same fire 
that consumed everything. His gauntleted hands are on the door, pushing, 
trying desperately to break through. Failing. The image captures his anguish, 
his helplessness. A knight who could break armies, unable to save the ones he 
loved most.
 
KORINTHE STARES
She floats before these two images, looking from one to the other. The road. 
The doors. The choice. The consequence.
"He... he turned back?"
Her voice is small now, stripped of the layered echo. Almost human.
"He was riding away. To Istar. I remember... he said he had a 
quest. A divine mission. Gladria's family said he was fleeing justice, 
but he said..."
She looks at the image of him on the road.
"He chose me. He turned back for me."
Then she looks at the image of him at the doors, wreathed in flames.
"And he couldn't reach us. The fire... it wasn't natural. It wouldn't 
yield to strength or will. It was divine judgment, and he was as 
helpless before it as we were."
Her form wavers, becoming less distinct.
"Three hundred years. Three hundred years I believed he let us die. 
That he stood outside by choice, listening to us scream because we 
no longer mattered to him."
"But he tried. He TRIED. And he failed because the gods 
themselves had judged, and no mortal - not even the finest knight - 
could stand against that."
She turns to look at all the images surrounding her: herself alive, Peradur 
laughing, the Cataclysm's victims, Soth's choice, Soth's failure.
"My death wasn't murder. It was... consequence. Soth failed the 
world to save me. And the world burned. And I burned with it. Not 
because he didn't love me, but because he loved me TOO MUCH."
The realization is breaking something in her - three centuries of rage built on a 
false foundation, crumbling.
"What have I... what have I BEEN for three hundred years?"
 
EIGHTH IMAGE - THE MIRROR
This is the moment Johannes planned for. The final piece.
JOHANNES - YOUR FINAL ILLUSION
Cast Minor Illusion one more time. Show her what she's become. 
Not as accusation, but as truth. The banshee - wreathed in ethereal 
fire, face twisted by rage and grief, hands like claws. Place it beside 
the image of her alive, so she can see both at once.
What do you say as you show her this final reflection?
Cyrus and Kessa are absolutely still, barely breathing. They're watching a 
three-hundred-year-old curse crack open before their eyes.
Finish it, Johannes. Show her the choice she has now.
I create two images - one of her before, then...what she is now.
Dec 10
EIGHTH IMAGE - NINTH IMAGE
Johannes casts Minor Illusion twice more, placing them directly in front of 
Korinthe, side by side, unavoidable:
Left image: Lady Korinthe as she was - the radiant elven woman from the 
portrait. Beautiful, warm, alive. The smile that welcomed guests. The hand 
over her heart. Grace and kindness made manifest.
Right image: Lady Korinthe as she is now - the banshee. Translucent, 
wreathed in cold ethereal flames. Face twisted by three centuries of rage and 
grief. Eyes burning with blue-white fire. Hands curled into claws. Hair floating 
in an unfelt wind. Beautiful still, but terrible. A victim transformed into 
something that perpetuates suffering.
The two images stand side by side. Past and present. Woman and wraith. 
What was and what is.
 
KORINTHE SEES HERSELF
She floats before the two images, staring. Her translucent hands rise slowly to 
her face, as if she could feel features she no longer possesses.
"Is that... is that what I've become?"
Her voice is barely a whisper now, all the multiple tones collapsing into a 
single, fragile sound.
She looks at the image of herself alive - the warmth, the welcome, the life. 
Then at the banshee - the rage, the cold, the death.
"I was... I was beautiful once. Not just in form, but in spirit. I 
welcomed travelers. I loved my son. I tended the gardens. I sang 
songs of joy, not lament."
She reaches toward the image of her living self, her hand passing through it.
"And now I am... this. Three hundred years of hate. Three hundred 
years of screaming at doors that will never open, at a man who 
cannot hear me, at gods who turned away."
"I have become what killed me. I have become fire and pain and 
death."
Her form flickers, unstable, as if the realization is undermining her very 
existence.
"Peradur would not know me. If my son could see what his mother 
became... he would be afraid. He would run from me."
The truth of that statement seems to physically wound her. She doubles over, 
her ethereal form curling in on itself.
"What have I done? How many have I killed? How many mothers, 
how many sons have I destroyed in my rage?"
She's weeping now - truly weeping, though no tears fall. The cold in the Chapel 
lessens slightly. The frost on the floor begins to melt at the edges.
"I blamed Soth. I blamed the gods. I blamed everyone but myself 
for choosing to remain here, choosing rage over rest, choosing to 
be THIS-" She gestures at the banshee image, "-instead of accepting 
what happened and... and letting go."
 
SHE TURNS TO THE THREE OF YOU
Her burning eyes focus on Johannes, then Cyrus, then back to Johannes.
"You came here... why? The Dragon Army soldiers came for power, 
for the Starjewel, for an alliance with the damned. But you..."
She looks at Cyrus's holy symbol of Mishakal, still glowing faintly.
"You came with truth. You showed me what I could not see for 
three hundred years. You gave me... perspective."
Her voice becomes urgent, almost pleading:
"The cleric spoke of the Disks. Of the gods returning. Is this true? 
Can the gods truly see us again? Can they... can they grant mercy 
even to ones such as I, who have spent centuries spreading the very 
pain I suffered?"
"Can this-" She gestures at herself, at the banshee she's become, "-be 
undone? Or am I damned to remain this monster forever, even now 
that I SEE what I've become?"
 
THE MOMENT OF CHOICE
The Chapel is silent except for the faint dripping of melting frost. The nine 
images surround Korinthe like a gallery of truth - her life, her son, the 
Cataclysm, Soth's choice, Soth's failure, and the mirror showing what she was 
versus what she is.
She's listening. She's present. The rage has given way to grief, and the grief 
has given way to... possibility.
CYRUS STEPS FORWARD
Brother Cyrus approaches slowly, respectfully, holding his holy symbol of 
Mishakal openly.
"Lady Korinthe, I am Brother Cyrus, servant of Mishakal, the Healing 
Goddess. And I tell you this truth: the Disks of Mishakal have returned to 
Krynn. The gods can hear prayers again. Three hundred years of silence has 
ended."
He stops ten feet from her, close enough to speak intimately but respecting her 
space.
"I cannot promise redemption. I cannot promise salvation. That judgment 
belongs to powers far beyond me. But I can promise this: your suffering has 
been witnessed. Your pain has been seen. And if there is mercy to be found, if 
there is healing even for wounds three centuries old... Mishakal offers it."
He looks at her directly, unafraid despite the supernatural terror she 
represents:
"The question is: what do you choose? You have agency, my lady. You always 
have. Will you remain trapped in the moment of your death, forever raging at 
what cannot be changed? Or will you accept what happened, release the rage, 
and allow yourself to... rest?"
 
KORINTHE LOOKS AT CYRUS
Then at Johannes. Then at Kessa, who has remained silent but supportive 
throughout.
"You three... you risked death to bring me this truth. You walked 
into a cursed keep, faced a death knight, and stood before a 
banshee to show me... what I had forgotten. Who I once was."
She looks at the image of Peradur, her son, frozen in laughter.
"If the gods can grant mercy... if there is rest to be found... then I 
choose..."
She pauses, the weight of three hundred years of habit warring with this new 
clarity.
"I choose to let go."
 
What happens next?
This is a pivotal moment. Korinthe has made her choice, but 
the mechanism of release is unclear.
Does she:
1.	Need the Disks physically present to break the curse?
2.	Need Cyrus to perform some ritual or prayer?
3.	Simply... fade, now that she's released the rage that sustained her?
4.	Need to confront Soth directly, to grant and receive forgiveness?
Johannes, Cyrus - what do you say or do in response to her choice? 
And how do you help her find the rest she seeks?
"My Lady, you have a choice. Even as you felt like it had been taken from you, 
others are also trapped. What is your choice? You can free yourself from your 
own pain, find absolution and freedom through the sacred rites Cyrus can 
offer. And none on this plane of existence could fault or even question your 
right to do so. You can be freed even as the words are uttered, free to rejoin 
your lost loves, your friends, your family, even your son."
"But, out of the love you once held for your son, there are others, bound out 
of consequence, loyalty, even love. The greatest revenge is to offer mercy, 
especially when there is no right to ask or expect it. To give what they cannot 
ask for, how is that not both freedom for you, and freedom for them? We do 
not ask this of you, but offer you the opportunity to choose for yourself. If you 
would, we can ask one, one worthy to bear the Disks of our goddess, who can 
stand in judgement, to ascertain, in your presence, the full truth of his actions, 
his thoughts, and his intents, but only if you are willing to forgo your own 
justice, to allow that truth to dictate his fate."
"What say you, my Lady?"
Show more
Dec 10
KORINTHE'S CONTEMPLATION
The banshee floats silently, suspended between past and present, between 
rage and mercy. The nine images surrounding her bear witness - her beauty, 
her son, the truth of the Cataclysm, the mirror of what she's become.
She looks at the image of Peradur - her laughing child, frozen in innocent joy.
"If I let go now... if I simply accept Cyrus's rites and pass beyond... I 
find peace. I find rest. I am reunited with my son, free from three 
hundred years of torment."
Her voice is steady, thoughtful. The desperate, layered echo is gone. She 
sounds almost... human again.
"But Soth remains. And Sir Caradoc. And the others - the knights 
who followed him, who stood by him, who share his curse not 
because they failed the world, but because they followed one who 
did."
She turns to look toward the Chapel doors, toward where the Great Hall lies 
beyond.
"They are trapped as I was trapped. Locked in their guilt, their 
failure, their endless punishment. And I..." She looks at her translucent 
hands, at the cold flames that wreathe her. "...I have been their 
tormentor, haven't I? Every night, singing my lament. Every day, 
radiating my rage. I have been part of their punishment for three 
hundred years."
She looks at Johannes, and there's something ancient and weary in her 
burning eyes, but also something awakening - purpose beyond pain.
"You offer me a choice. True choice, not the illusion of it. Rest for 
myself... or justice for others. Mercy I could take... or mercy I could 
give."
"You speak of bringing one who bears the Disks. One who can 
stand in judgment, who can see truth and pronounce it. Not me, 
with my three hundred years of hatred. Not Soth, drowning in his 
guilt. But an impartial witness to finally, FINALLY judge whether 
this curse has been punishment enough."
She floats closer to Johannes and Cyrus, her form becoming more distinct, 
more solid, as if making this choice is giving her substance.
"If I choose this... if I forgo my own rest to be present for his 
judgment... what happens? Do I remain as I am? Do I become
