something else? Do I risk being trapped here forever if the gods 
judge him unworthy of release?"
Her voice isn't fearful, just... careful. She's thinking like the woman she was - 
the lady of a keep who made decisions that affected more than just herself.
"And Soth... you would bring the Disks to him? You would allow 
him to stand before divine judgment after what he's done? After 
the world he failed to save?"
She pauses, then more quietly:
"After the love he bore me, misguided and destructive as it was, 
that led to all of this?"
 
CYRUS SPEAKS
"My lady, if you choose to wait, to be present for his judgment, I believe 
Mishakal would sustain you. Not as this-" he gestures at her banshee form, 
"-but as something more peaceful. A witness rather than a tormentor. Your 
rage has already begun to fade. Your clarity has returned. That transformation 
would continue."
"As for risk... yes, there is risk. If Soth is judged and found still unworthy, if 
the curse continues, you might remain. But..." He looks at her seriously. "You 
would remain by choice, not compulsion. And choice transforms suffering into 
purpose. You would not be trapped - you would be bearing witness."
"And if he is judged worthy of release, if the curse is lifted... then you both find 
rest together. The curse that bound you would release you simultaneously."
 
KESSA ADDS QUIETLY
"Three hundred years you've blamed him. Hated him. Raged at him. If you 
leave now without seeing the truth pronounced, without witnessing his 
judgment... part of you might always wonder. Was your rage justified? Was 
the curse fair? Did he deserve what he got?"
"But if you're there when the Disks reveal the full truth - his sins, his 
intentions, his three hundred years of penance - then you'll know. And 
knowledge brings closure in ways that assumption never can."
 
KORINTHE LOOKS AT THE IMAGE OF HERSELF - THE LIVING 
WOMAN
"She would choose mercy. The woman I was - the one who 
welcomed guests, who tended gardens, who loved deeply - she 
would not take her own peace while leaving others in torment."
"But she was also foolish. Naive. She believed in a murderer, 
trusted when she should have questioned, and died for it."
Then she looks at the banshee image.
"And this creature would choose vengeance. Would take her rest 
and let Soth rot forever in his guilt. Would say 'he deserves every 
moment of suffering.'"
"But she... I... have spent three hundred years being that creature. 
And what has it brought me? What has vengeance given me except 
more pain?"
She looks directly at Johannes, and when she speaks, her voice is clear and 
decided:
"I choose to wait. I choose to be present for his judgment. Bring the 
Disks. Bring your bearer who can see truth. Let Soth stand before 
divine judgment with me as witness."
"Not because I forgive him - I am not sure I can, not yet. But 
because after three hundred years of rage, I want to know 
the truth. The full truth. Not the fragments I died believing, not the 
assumptions that sustained my hatred, but the complete, 
undeniable, divine truth of what he did, why he did it, and whether 
his penance has been sufficient."
"And if the gods judge him worthy of release... then I will accept 
that judgment. And if they judge him still wanting... then at least he 
will have had a fair trial, not just an eternity of self-inflicted 
torment."
She turns to Cyrus:
"Can you... help me? Transform me from this-" she gestures at 
herself, "-into something that can wait with dignity rather than 
rage? I do not wish to be a banshee for however long this takes. I 
wish to be... myself again. As much as is possible."
 
THE STARJEWEL
As if responding to her choice, the corrupted gem on the altar flickers. The 
sickly green-black light pulses once, twice, then begins to fade. Not 
extinguishing, but... cleansing. Slowly, over the course of several seconds, the 
corruption drains away, and the gem begins to glow with pure, clear light - 
silver-white, holy.
The Starjewel is restoring itself.
JOHANNES, CYRUS - How do you respond to her choice? And 
Cyrus, can you perform a ritual or prayer to help transform her 
from vengeful banshee to peaceful witness?
And what is your plan for bringing the Disks to Dargaard Keep for 
Soth's judgment?
I leave Cyrus to deal with this. I pull out the Sending Stone and send word to 
Laurana to send for Goldmoon and the Disks to be brought with all haste to 
Dargaard Keep. All will be explained, but it is critical that they both arrive as 
soon as possible.
Dec 10
JOHANNES USES THE SENDING STONE
While Cyrus begins ministering to Lady Korinthe, Johannes steps back toward 
the Chapel entrance, pulling the Sending Stone from his pouch. He activates it, 
feeling the familiar warmth as the connection establishes.
Johannes's message to Commander Laurana (25 words):
"Dargaard Keep secure. Send Goldmoon with Disks immediately. Divine 
judgment required. Death knight seeks redemption. Curse may end. Come 
with all haste. Will explain upon arrival."
There's a pause - perhaps ten seconds - then Laurana's voice comes through, 
tense and surprised:
"Goldmoon with Disks? Johannes, are you- Never mind. I trust you. She's in 
Haven. I'll dispatch immediately. Expect arrival in four days. Stay alive."
The connection closes.
Four days. Goldmoon is at Haven, roughly 80 miles away. With urgent 
travel, magical assistance if needed, and the importance of the mission... four 
days is optimistic but achievable.
 
MEANWHILE - CYRUS AND LADY KORINTHE
Brother Cyrus approaches the altar carefully, his holy symbol of Mishakal 
glowing softly in his hand. Lady Korinthe floats before him, her banshee form 
flickering between rage and peace, between monster and woman.
"My lady, what you're asking... I've never attempted anything like this. 
Transforming an undead creature while keeping them extant, changing their 
nature without destroying them..." He pauses, thinking. "But Mishakal is the 
goddess of healing, and healing isn't always about flesh. Sometimes it's about 
spirit."
He closes his eyes, praying silently, then speaks:
"Lady Korinthe, I cannot make you mortal again. I cannot give you 
life. But perhaps... perhaps I can ease the curse. Transform you 
from a creature of rage and death into something more... benign. A 
spirit at rest, waiting for judgment rather than raging against it."
CYRUS'S RITUAL (Improvised, using Channel Divinity creatively):
Cyrus places his holy symbol on the altar beside the now-cleansing Starjewel. 
He begins to pray - not a memorized liturgy, but spontaneous supplication:
"Mishakal, Healing Goddess, Light-Bringer, Merciful Mother - hear your 
servant. Before you is one who has suffered beyond measure, who has raged 
beyond reason, and who now seeks peace without yet seeking rest. She asks 
not for redemption, but for clarity. Not for forgiveness, but for truth. Grant 
her the grace to wait with dignity for divine judgment."
He extends his hands toward Korinthe:
"Transform rage into patience. Transform vengeance into witness. Let her 
pain subside without her existence ending. Let her remain, not as tormentor, 
but as testament to suffering acknowledged and justice pursued."
DIVINE RESPONSE:
The Chapel fills with warm golden light - not the cold blue-white of undeath or 
the sickly green of corruption, but genuine divine radiance. It flows from 
Cyrus's holy symbol, washing over Lady Korinthe like gentle rain.
She gasps - an unnecessary breath, but the memory of breathing, the habit of 
being alive.
THE TRANSFORMATION:
Her banshee form begins to change:
*	The cold flames wreathing her body fade, replaced by a soft silver glow
*	Her twisted, rage-filled expression softens, returning to the beauty of 
the portrait
*	Her clawed hands relax, becoming graceful once more
*	Her tattered, burned gown repairs itself, returning to the elegant blue 
she wore in life
*	The burning fury in her eyes dims to something gentler - still ethereal, 
still glowing, but without the rage
*	She becomes more present, more solid, though still clearly a spirit 
rather than flesh
She's no longer a banshee. She's... something else. A ghost, perhaps, but 
peaceful. A spirit at rest, awaiting judgment rather than perpetuating torment.
KORINTHE LOOKS AT HER HANDS:
"I can... I can feel again. Not physically, but... emotionally. The rage 
is gone. The need to destroy, to hurt, to make others feel what I felt 
- it's gone."
She looks at Cyrus with wonder and gratitude:
"You've given me back myself. Not life, but... self. I am Lady 
Korinthe again, not just the screaming thing that died in the 
flames."
She floats down until she's standing on the Chapel floor - or appearing to 
stand, her feet hovering just an inch above the stone.
"Thank you, priest of Mishakal. You have shown me more mercy 
than I have shown anyone in three hundred years."
 
KESSA'S OBSERVATION:
"The temperature's rising. The Chapel doesn't feel cursed anymore - it feels... 
sacred again. Like whatever corruption held this place is lifting."
She's right. The oppressive cold is fading. The frost has melted completely. 
The scorch marks on the walls seem less stark, less accusatory.
 
LADY KORINTHE TURNS TO JOHANNES:
"Four days until judgment arrives. Four days for Soth to prepare. 
Four days for me to... decide what I truly want from this."
She looks toward the Chapel doors, toward where the Great Hall and Lord 
Soth lie beyond.
"I should speak with him. After three hundred years of screaming 
accusations through these walls, I should... speak. With clarity. 
With the truth you've shown me."
She looks uncertain - the first time she's shown true vulnerability rather than 
rage or grief.
"Will you accompany me? All three of you? I do not think I can face 
him alone. Not yet. Not after everything."
 
JOHANNES, CYRUS, KESSA:
Lady Korinthe - peaceful now, transformed, but still bearing three centuries of 
complex emotions - wants to confront Lord Soth before Goldmoon arrives 
with the Disks.
Do you:
1.	Accompany her immediately - facilitate the conversation between 
Soth and Korinthe now
2.	Suggest waiting - let her process this transformation first, speak to 
him closer to judgment day
3.	Prepare differently - discuss what should be said, how to approach 
this reunion
4.	Handle the Starjewel first - the now-purified gem is sitting on the 
altar, and it was what the Dragon Army sought
What's your approach?
My Lady, we will gladly assist you. But, would you first permit us one small 
favor? Even as your pain has transformed you, his guilt and pain has 
transformed your husband. May we have your leave to first show him the 
Starjewel as Testament of our words regarding what has happened here? That 
he might be prepared when you do come before him, and that he might know 
what comes with Goldmoon?
Dec 10
LADY KORINTHE'S RESPONSE
She considers Johannes's request, looking back at the altar where the 
Starjewel now rests - no longer corrupted with sickly green-black light, but 
glowing with pure silver-white radiance. The symbol of Soth's former honor, 
now restored.
"The Starjewel..." Her voice is soft, contemplative. "Three hundred 
years it has sat there, corrupted, a reminder of everything that was 
lost. And now, because I chose truth over vengeance, it cleanses 
itself."
She floats closer to the altar, studying the gem.
"You would show it to him first? Prepare him for... for seeing me as 
I am now, rather than as I have been?"
She's quiet for a moment, then nods slowly.
"Yes. That is... wise. And kind."
She looks at Johannes with genuine respect. "If you walk into that hall 
with me at your side, after three hundred years of my lament 
echoing through his existence, he will not be prepared. He will 
expect rage, accusation, perhaps another three centuries of 
torment."
"But if you show him the Starjewel first - proof that something has 
changed, that redemption is possible, that the curse is shifting - 
then when I appear, he might be able to hear me rather than simply 
brace for punishment."
She touches the Starjewel gently - her spectral hand doesn't pass through it, 
but rests upon it as if she were still flesh.
"This was his greatest treasure. The symbol of his worthiness as a 
Knight of the Rose, given to him by Paladine's blessing. When it 
corrupted with the curse, it broke something in him beyond the 
obvious."
"If you show him it's pure again... you show him that 
perhaps he can be pure again. That three hundred years of penance 
might actually mean something."
She carefully lifts the Starjewel from the altar - her transformed state allowing 
her to interact with physical objects - and offers it to Johannes.
"Take it to him. Show him what his wife's choice to forgive, to seek 
truth rather than vengeance, has accomplished. Let him see that 
mercy can cleanse what guilt could not."
"And tell him..." She pauses, choosing her words carefully. "Tell him that 
I am coming. Not to torment. Not to rage. But to witness. To hear 
truth. To be present when the gods finally judge whether we have 
suffered enough."
"Tell him that Lady Korinthe - his Korinthe, not the screaming 
thing in the Chapel - wishes to speak with him. If he will have me."
Her voice wavers slightly on those last words - a vulnerability that shows how 
much courage this is taking.
"I will wait here. In this Chapel where I died, now made sacred 
again. And when you return with his answer... we will face three 
hundred years of pain together, and see if understanding can heal 
what time could not."
 
THE STARJEWEL
Johannes now holds the Starjewel - a fist-sized gem in an elegant silver 
setting. It's warm to the touch, pulsing with holy light. This is a relic of 
Paladine, given to knights who exemplify honor, courage, and wisdom.
Cyrus examines it (Religion check: 19):
"This is... Johannes, this is a major holy relic. In its corrupted state, the 
Dragon Army wanted to use it as leverage, as proof they could restore Soth's 
honor. But now, purified? This proves divine grace is possible even for the 
fallen. This is evidence that redemption isn't just theological theory - it's real, 
tangible, achievable."
Kessa: "So we walk into the Great Hall, show a death knight that his most 
treasured possession - corrupted for three hundred years - is suddenly pure 
again, and tell him his dead wife wants to talk. No pressure."
She manages a slight smile despite the gravity. "Let's do this before I overthink 
it."
 
RETURNING TO THE GREAT HALL
The three of you leave the Chapel, the Starjewel's holy light illuminating the 
corridor. The Gallery of Ancestors seems different now - less oppressive, less 
haunted. The portraits of the family watch you pass with what might be 
approval.
As you enter the Great Hall, Lord Soth remains on his throne exactly as you 
left him. The skeletal warriors stand motionless. The ghostly figures hover 
near the ceiling.
But as you approach, carrying the Starjewel, Soth's head turns slowly. The 
burning points of light in his eye sockets focus on the gem in Johannes's 
hands.
He rises from his throne.
The movement is sudden, almost violent. The greatsword clatters to the stone 
floor - the first time in three hundred years he's dropped it.
"That light... that is..."
His voice - usually hollow and grinding - cracks with something that might be 
hope or might be anguish.
"The Starjewel. But it cannot be. It has been corrupted since the 
curse fell. It has been green-black poison for three centuries, a 
reminder of everything I destroyed."
He descends the steps, moving toward you with purpose but not aggression. 
The cold flames around his armor flare and dim erratically, as if his emotional 
state is disrupting the curse's manifestation.
He stops twenty feet away, staring at the gem.
"How? How is it pure? What have you done?"
 
JOHANNES - THE FLOOR IS YOURS
You hold the Starjewel, proof of transformation. You carry Lady Korinthe's 
message. You have four days until Goldmoon arrives with the Disks for 
judgment.
What do you tell Lord Soth? How do you explain what happened in 
the Chapel, and how do you deliver Korinthe's message?
Everything. In order
Dec 10
JOHANNES'S ACCOUNT
Johannes stands before Lord Soth, the purified Starjewel glowing in his hands, 
and speaks with the same honest clarity he used with Sir Caradoc, with Soth 
himself, and with Lady Korinthe.
"My lord, we entered the Chapel as you permitted. We found Lady Korinthe 
there, as you warned - a banshee, consumed by three centuries of rage and 
grief."
He pauses, letting that truth settle.
"She attacked us with words, with fury. She believed you had murdered 
Gladria. She believed you had let her and Peradur burn through choice rather 
than helplessness. She was trapped in the moment of her death, reliving it 
eternally, unable to see beyond that single terrible truth."
Soth remains motionless, the blue-white points of light in his eye sockets fixed 
on Johannes.
"So I showed her truth. Not my truth, not your truth, but the truth. Using 
illusions, I surrounded her with images - what she was in life, beautiful and 
kind. Her son Peradur, laughing and innocent. The Cataclysm itself, showing 
her she was not alone in suffering, that millions died in that divine judgment."
Johannes's voice remains steady, matter-of-fact, delivering the narrative as it 
happened.
"I showed her you on the road to Istar. Turning back. Choosing her over the 
world. I showed her you at the Chapel doors, wreathed in flames, trying 
desperately to break through and failing. Not because you didn't love her, but 
because even the finest knight cannot stand against the gods' judgment."
"I showed her what she became - the banshee beside the woman she was. Past 
and present. Grace and rage. I gave her perspective beyond the single moment 
that had trapped her for three centuries."
He looks directly at Soth.
"And she understood. She saw the truth. That her death was not murder but 
consequence. That you failed the world to save her, and the world burned, and 
she burned with it. Not because you didn't care, but because you cared too 
much. You chose love over duty, and divine judgment answered."
 
SOTH'S REACTION
The death knight's form trembles. The cold flames around his armor dim 
almost to nothing.
"She... she saw? She understood?"
His voice is barely audible, stripped of the grinding echo.
"Three hundred years I have listened to her lament. Three hundred 
years of accusation, of her voice singing my failures. And you 
showed her... truth?"
 
JOHANNES CONTINUES
"More than that, my lord. I gave her a choice."
He holds up the Starjewel so its light fills the space between them.
"I told her she could accept Brother Cyrus's rites, find peace, pass beyond to be 
reunited with her son. She had earned that rest. No one would question her 
right to it."
"But I also told her that others remain trapped here. You. Sir Caradoc. The 
knights who followed you. Bound by consequence, loyalty, and love. I offered 
her the opportunity to wait, to be present when divine judgment finally 
comes."
"I told her we would bring the Disks of Mishakal here. That Goldmoon, who 
bears them, would stand witness. That after three hundred years, you could 
face judgment from the gods themselves - not self-inflicted torment, but actual 
divine assessment of whether your penance has been sufficient."
Soth takes one step forward, then stops, as if afraid to hope.
"The Disks... here? Judgment? After three centuries of silence, the 
gods would finally... speak?"
 
JOHANNES DELIVERS THE MESSAGE
"Lady Korinthe chose to wait. She chose to forgo her own rest to witness your 
judgment. Not because she forgives you - she's not certain she can, not yet. But 
because she wants to know the complete truth. She wants the gods to 
pronounce it, not her assumptions or your guilt."
He gestures to the Starjewel.
"And when she made that choice - when she chose mercy and truth over 
vengeance and rest - this happened. The Starjewel purified itself. Three 
hundred years of corruption cleansed in a moment because she chose to see 
you not as the monster she died believing you were, but as the man who failed 
catastrophically while trying to save her."
Johannes's voice becomes gentler, more personal.
"Brother Cyrus performed a ritual. He transformed her from the banshee 
you've heard screaming for three centuries into... herself again. Lady Korinthe. 
Peaceful. Whole in spirit if not in flesh. Still a spirit, still undead, but no longer 
consumed by rage."
He delivers her message directly:
"She is coming. Not to torment. Not to rage. But to witness. To hear truth. To 
be present when the gods finally judge whether you have suffered enough."
A pause.
"She asks if you will have her. If you will speak with her - not as death knight 
to banshee, but as Soth to Korinthe. As the man and woman you were before 
the Cataclysm, trying to understand what you've become and whether 
redemption is possible."
 
THE STARJEWEL'S MEANING
Johannes holds the gem forward, offering it.
"This is proof, my lord. Proof that divine grace can cleanse what guilt cannot. 
Proof that three hundred years of penance might actually mean something. 
Proof that when someone chooses mercy over vengeance, the curse itself 
responds."
"Lady Korinthe transformed this through her choice. She gave you back your 
honor - symbolically, at least. The Starjewel is pure again because she chose to 
see you clearly rather than through the lens of rage."
"In four days, Goldmoon arrives with the Disks of Mishakal. In four days, you 
stand before divine judgment. And Lady Korinthe will be there, bearing 
witness, seeking truth alongside you."
Johannes lowers the Starjewel slightly, his voice becoming a question:
"Will you speak with her? Will you face three hundred years of pain together 
and see if understanding can heal what time could not?"
 
LORD SOTH'S RESPONSE
The death knight stands absolutely still for a long moment. Then, slowly, he 
sinks to one knee - not in submission, but in something like prayer, or perhaps 
simply the weight of centuries of guilt finally being acknowledged.
"She chose to wait. For me. For judgment. For truth."
His gauntleted hands come up to cover his face - a gesture of overwhelming 
emotion from something that technically has no face to cover.
"Three hundred years I have sat in this hall, believing she died 
hating me. Believing her rage was eternal and justified. Believing I 
deserved every moment of her lament, every accusation sung 
through these walls."
"And you tell me she chose to remain? Not as punishment, but as 
witness? Not to torment me, but to stand beside me when the gods 
finally judge?"
He looks up at Johannes, at the Starjewel.
"I will speak with her. Gods help me, I will speak with her. I do not 
know what to say after three hundred years of silence between us, 
after three hundred years of her screaming and my guilt. But if she 
has the courage to face me, then I must have the courage to face 
her."
He rises slowly, and for the first time since you entered Dargaard Keep, he 
sounds almost... human.
"Bring her to me. Let us speak truth before the gods arrive to judge 
us. Let us see if two people who loved catastrophically, who failed 
utterly, who have suffered eternally... can find some measure of 
understanding."
He looks at the skeletal warriors along the walls, then at the ghostly figures 
near the ceiling.
"And when Goldmoon arrives with the Disks... when judgment 
comes... let it fall upon me fairly. I have carried my guilt for three 
centuries. If the gods deem it sufficient, let me rest. If they deem it 
insufficient..."
A pause.
"Then at least I will have stood before them honestly, with 
Korinthe as witness, and known that my penance was measured by 
something greater than my own endless self-flagellation."
 
CYRUS SPEAKS
"My lord, before Lady Korinthe comes before you, I should prepare you. She 
is... changed. Peaceful. She looks as she did in life - beautiful, graceful, whole 
in spirit. But she is still a spirit, still bearing the weight of what happened. This 
conversation will not be easy for either of you."
"But it is necessary. For both of you. And perhaps... perhaps it's 
the beginning of healing that three centuries couldn't bring."
 
JOHANNES, CYRUS, KESSA:
Lord Soth has agreed. He will speak with Lady Korinthe. He will face 
judgment when Goldmoon arrives.
Do you:
1.	Return to the Chapel immediately - bring Korinthe to the Great

2.	Give Soth time to prepare - let him process this revelation first

Dec 10
JOHANNES PLACES THE STARJEWEL
Johannes approaches Lord Soth and extends the Starjewel toward him - not 
throwing it, not placing it carelessly, but offering it with the respect due a 
sacred relic.
"This is yours, my lord. It always has been. A symbol of your honor, given by 
Paladine when you achieved Knight of the Rose. It corrupted with your fall, 
and now it's pure again because of your wife's choice to seek truth over 
vengeance."
He places the gem in Soth's gauntleted hand.
"Hold it. Remember who you were. Prepare yourself for who you might speak 
with - not the screaming banshee you've heard for three centuries, but Lady 
Korinthe as she was. As she's chosen to be again."
 
SOTH HOLDS THE STARJEWEL
The death knight's fingers close around the gem, and for a moment, the cold 
flames wreathing his armor flicker wildly. The pure light of the Starjewel 
seems to war with the curse's darkness, neither winning but both coexisting.
"I had forgotten how it felt. Warm. Alive. Holy."
He clutches it to his chest, where his heart once beat.
"I will... I need time. To find words. To remember how to speak to 
her as a husband rather than as a cursed thing addressing its 
tormentor. Go. Bring her when she is ready. I will be here."
He returns to his throne slowly, the Starjewel still held against his chest. The 
skeletal warriors remain motionless, but somehow their presence feels less 
threatening - more like honor guards waiting for something significant rather 
than eternal punishment.
 
RETURN TO THE CHAPEL
The three of you leave the Great Hall and make your way back through the 
Gallery of Ancestors. The portraits of the family seem to watch with 
anticipation rather than judgment.
When you enter the Chapel, Lady Korinthe turns from where she's been 
standing - or appearing to stand - near the altar. Her transformed appearance 
still takes a moment to process: the peaceful, graceful spirit rather than the 
rage-filled banshee.
"You spoke with him?"
Her voice carries anxiety, hope, and three centuries of complicated emotion.
"Does he... will he see me? Or does he prefer I remain here, out of 
sight, until the judgment arrives?"
She's wringing her hands - a nervous gesture that's heartbreakingly human.
 
CYRUS SPEAKS GENTLY
"He will see you, my lady. He wants to see you. We gave him the Starjewel, 
showed him it's pure again because of your choice. And he... he broke, in a 
way. The guilt, the hope, the possibility that three centuries of suffering might 
actually mean something - it overwhelmed him."
"He's preparing himself now. Trying to find words for a conversation he never 
thought possible."
 
KESSA ADDS
"He's terrified. We could see it even through the curse, even through the 
undeath. He's afraid of what you'll say, what you'll ask, what three hundred 
years of truth will sound like when spoken aloud rather than screamed 
through walls."
She looks at Korinthe with surprising compassion. "You're both scared. 
That's... actually good. Fear means this matters. Fear means you're both 
present, both invested in what happens next."
 
LADY KORINTHE TAKES A BREATH (unnecessary but habitual)
"Three hundred years. Three hundred years we have been 
separated by rage and guilt, by my accusations and his self-
punishment. And now..."
She looks down at her hands - spectral but solid, graceful rather than clawed.
"Now I must walk into that hall and speak with the man I died 
believing was a murderer. The man I now know was a catastrophic 
failure, but not a villain. The man who loved me enough to doom 
the world."
"I don't know if I can forgive him. I don't know if forgiveness is 
even what this is about. But I can face him. I can hear him. I can 
stand beside him when judgment comes."
She looks at the three of you.
"Will you... will you stay? In the hall, when we speak? Not to 
mediate or intervene, but simply to... bear witness? If three 
centuries of pain spill out between us, I would have impartial 
witnesses present. And if understanding emerges... I would have it 
recorded by those who brought truth to us both."
"I do not wish to do this alone. And I do not think Soth should 
either."
 
JOHANNES, CYRUS, KESSA:
Lady Korinthe is ready to face Lord Soth. She asks that you remain in the

This is a pivotal moment: three hundred years of curse, guilt, grief, and rage 
coming to a head before divine judgment arrives in four days.

JOHANNES'S RESPONSE
"We'll be there, my lady. As witnesses. This moment - after three hundred

CYRUS NODS

KESSA
"Besides, someone needs to make sure this conversation actually happens

LADY KORINTHE'S GRATITUDE
"Thank you. All three of you. You have done more for us in hours 
than three centuries of isolation accomplished. You brought truth 
where there was only assumption. You brought mercy where there 
was only rage."
She smooths her spectral gown - a nervous gesture, preparing herself.
"Very well. Let us... let us face what we have avoided for so long."
 
PROCESSION TO THE GREAT HALL
The four of you leave the Chapel together:
*	Lady Korinthe leads, floating gracefully but with visible tension
*	Johannes, Cyrus, Kessa follow several paces behind, a supportive 
presence
Through the Gallery of Ancestors, past the family portraits that seem to 
witness this moment. Down the grand corridor toward the Great Hall.
As you approach the massive doors, now fully open, Lady Korinthe pauses. 
Her spectral form flickers slightly - nervousness made manifest.
"Three hundred years. And now... moments away."
She steels herself, then continues forward.
 
ENTERING THE GREAT HALL
Lord Soth sits on his throne, the Starjewel clutched in his gauntleted hands, 
held against his chest. The cold flames around his armor are dim, subdued. 
The skeletal warriors stand at perfect attention along the walls. The ghostly 
figures hover near the ceiling, watching.
As Lady Korinthe enters, floating into the hall with Johannes, Cyrus, and 
Kessa behind her, Lord Soth rises.
The movement is careful, almost reverent. He descends the steps from the 
throne platform, the Starjewel still held against his heart.
They stand forty feet apart - death knight and transformed spirit, husband and 
wife, two souls who have been separated by more than death for three 
centuries.
LADY KORINTHE SPEAKS FIRST
Her voice is steady but carries the weight of centuries:
"Soth."
Not "Lord Soth." Not "my lord." Not "husband." Just his name, stripped of 
title and relationship, as if starting from the beginning.
LORD SOTH'S RESPONSE
"Korinthe."
His voice - normally hollow and grinding - is barely a whisper. The burning 
points of light in his eye sockets are fixed on her, unblinking, as if afraid she'll 
disappear if he looks away.
"You are... you look as you did. As I remember you. Before the 
flames. Before..."
He trails off, unable to finish.
 
THE SILENCE STRETCHES
Three hundred years of things unsaid, accusations unspoken (or screamed 
without response), grief unexpressed - it all hangs in the air between them.
Finally, Lady Korinthe floats forward ten feet. Stops. Continues.
She stops twenty feet from him. Close enough to speak without raising her 
voice. Far enough to maintain distance.
LADY KORINTHE CONTINUES
"For three hundred years, I believed you murdered Gladria. That 
you killed your first wife to have me. That you were corrupt, fallen, 
a betrayer of every vow you swore."
Soth doesn't defend himself. Doesn't interrupt. Just listens.
"I believed that when the Cataclysm came, you stood outside the 
Chapel and LET us burn. That you heard Peradur crying for you 
and CHOSE not to save him. That our deaths meant nothing to you 
compared to your own guilt."
"I have screamed these accusations through these walls for three 
centuries. I have sung your failures, your betrayals, your murders. 
I have made this place a monument to your damnation and my 
rage."
She pauses, and her voice becomes quieter:
"And I was wrong."
 
LORD SOTH REACTS
The death knight's form shudders. The cold flames around his armor flare 
briefly, then dim almost to nothing.
"You were not wrong. I AM fallen. I DID betray my vows. I DID 
fail-"
KORINTHE INTERRUPTS
"You did not murder Gladria. She died - perhaps by her own hand, 
perhaps by grief, perhaps by fate. But not by your sword. Not by 
your design."
"You did not CHOOSE to let us burn. You tried. Gods help you, you 
TRIED. The flames were divine judgment, and no mortal strength 
could overcome them. You failed, but not for lack of trying. Not for 
lack of love."
"And our deaths... they meant EVERYTHING to you. So much that 
three hundred years later, you still sit on this throne, reliving your 
failure, punishing yourself more thoroughly than any god could 
devise."
She floats closer - fifteen feet now.
"These truths were shown to me. By these three-" she gestures to 
Johannes, Cyrus, and Kessa, "-who risked their lives to bring clarity to 
both of us."
 
LORD SOTH'S CONFESSION
"I chose you over the world."
His voice is raw, honest, stripped of three centuries of practiced guilt.
"The gods sent me a vision. Told me to ride to Istar, to stop the 
Kingpriest, to prevent the Cataclysm. I could have saved millions. I 
could have prevented the destruction of everything we knew."
"But Gladria's family accused me. They poisoned you against me 
with their words - or perhaps with truth I refused to see. And when 
I rode out, when I was on that road to Istar, I thought only of YOU. 
Of proving myself to YOU. Of returning to YOU."
"So I turned back. I abandoned my divine mission. I chose personal 
love over cosmic duty."
"And the Cataclysm struck. Millions died. The world broke. And 
when I returned here, you were burning. Peradur was screaming. 
And I could do NOTHING."
He clutches the Starjewel tighter.
"That is my sin. Not murder. Not cruelty. But loving you MORE 
than I loved the world. Choosing one woman over millions of lives. 
Being willing to let civilization burn if it meant I could prove myself 
worthy of your love."
"And you died anyway. Believing I was a murderer. Believing I 
didn't love you. When the truth was I loved you SO MUCH that I 
damned the entire world for you."
 
LADY KORINTHE'S RESPONSE
She's silent for a long moment, processing this. Then:
"That is... that is the most selfish, catastrophic, TERRIBLE 
declaration of love I have ever heard."
A pause.
"And it explains everything. Why the curse. Why three hundred 
years of torment. Why the gods judged you so harshly."
"Because you didn't fail out of weakness or evil. You failed out of 
LOVE. Misguided, selfish, world-destroying love. And that is 
somehow worse, because it means you were capable of great good 
but CHOSE personal devotion over universal salvation."
She floats closer - ten feet now.
"I don't know if I can forgive you for that. For loving me so much 
that millions died. For making my love the cause of such suffering."
"But I can understand it. And I can stand beside you when the gods 
judge whether three hundred years of guilt has been sufficient 
penance for choosing love over duty."
 
THE STARJEWEL PULSES
As if responding to this moment of truth, the Starjewel in Soth's hands flares 
with brilliant light - not blinding, but warm, present, undeniable. The pure 
radiance fills the hall, touching every corner, illuminating the skeletal 
warriors, the ghostly figures, Johannes, Cyrus, and Kessa.
For just a moment, the curse seems to lift. The cold flames around Soth's 
armor vanish completely. Korinthe's spectral form becomes more solid, 
more real.
They stand there - death knight and spirit, husband and wife - seeing each 
other clearly for the first time in three hundred years.
Then the moment passes. The curse reasserts itself. But something has 
fundamentally changed.
 
LORD SOTH SPEAKS
"When Goldmoon arrives with the Disks... when the gods judge 
me... will you speak for me or against me?"
It's not a plea. Just a question. He genuinely doesn't know and genuinely 
wants to hear her answer.
 
LADY KORINTHE'S ANSWER
"I will speak truth. That you loved catastrophically. That you failed 
cosmically. That you have punished yourself eternally."
"And I will ask the gods this: Is three hundred years of torment 
sufficient? Has the man who chose love over duty learned what 
duty means? Has the knight who failed the world earned rest, or 
must he suffer longer?"
"I do not know their answer. But I will be there when they speak it. 
And whatever they decide... I will accept it."
She extends her hand toward him - not to touch, the distance is still too far, 
but as a gesture of... not forgiveness, but acknowledgment.
"We failed together, Soth. You failed the world to save me. I failed 
to see truth through my rage. We have both paid in centuries of 
suffering."
"In four days, that payment is assessed. And for the first time since 
the Cataclysm, we face it together rather than separated by walls 
and assumptions."
 
THE HALL IS SILENT
Johannes, Cyrus, and Kessa have witnessed this - three hundred years of curse 
and guilt confronted, not resolved but acknowledged. Truth spoken. 
Understanding reached.
It's not redemption. It's not forgiveness. But it's a beginning.
LORD SOTH RETURNS TO HIS THRONE
He sits slowly, the Starjewel still clutched against his chest. He looks less like a 
cursed monster and more like a man awaiting judgment - afraid, hopeful, 
resigned.
LADY KORINTHE REMAINS IN THE HALL
She doesn't return to the Chapel. She floats to a position near the throne - not 
beside it, but present. Waiting together.
 
FOUR DAYS UNTIL GOLDMOON ARRIVES
The curse remains. The keep remains haunted. But something essential has 
shifted. Truth has been spoken. Understanding has been reached. Two souls 
who have suffered in isolation now suffer in company, awaiting divine 
judgment.
JOHANNES, CYRUS, KESSA:
You have accomplished something extraordinary. What do you do during 
these four days while waiting for Goldmoon and the Disks to arrive?
Options:
1.	Remain at Dargaard Keep - continue supporting Soth and Korinthe, 
perhaps speak with other cursed spirits like Sir Caradoc
2.	Return to Dargaard Village - update the villagers, rest in relative 
safety
3.	Scout the region - ensure the route for Goldmoon's arrival is clear
4.	Prepare for the judgment ritual - discuss with Cyrus and Soth what 
this divine judgment might entail
What's your plan?
Skip to arrival
Dec 10
FOUR DAYS LATER - GOLDMOON'S ARRIVAL
The party has spent the intervening days at Dargaard Keep, bearing witness to 
the slow transformation of the cursed fortress. Lord Soth and Lady Korinthe 
have spoken at length - not constant conversation, but careful exchanges of 
truth, memory, and three centuries of unspoken grief. Sir Caradoc and the 
other bound spirits have felt the shift, their eternal vigils becoming something 
closer to hopeful waiting than mindless punishment.
Johannes, Cyrus, and Kessa have alternated between the keep and Dargaard 
Village, assuring the fearful residents that something momentous is 
happening, that the screaming has stopped, that perhaps the curse is finally 
approaching its end.
 
DAY FOUR - MIDDAY
You're standing with Lord Soth and Lady Korinthe in the Great Hall when 
Cyrus's head snaps up.
"They're here. I can feel it - Mishakal's presence. The Disks are close."
Through the partially open main gates, you can see movement on the southern 
approach road. A small group, perhaps eight people, making their way up the 
mountain path.
LORD SOTH RISES FROM HIS THRONE
"After three hundred years... judgment arrives."
His voice carries fear, hope, and resignation in equal measure. The Starjewel 
gleams against his blackened armor.
LADY KORINTHE FLOATS BESIDE HIM
Not touching, but present. United in awaiting what comes.
 
THE DELEGATION ENTERS
Through the gates, across the courtyard, into the Great Hall come:
Goldmoon - A Plainswoman in her mid-thirties, tall and regal, with silver-
gold hair despite her youth. She carries a leather satchel, and even from across 
the hall, you can feel the divine presence emanating from it. The Disks of 
Mishakal.
Commander Laurana - Elven woman, tactical and composed, but clearly 
awed by what she's witnessing. She's brought four resistance soldiers as 
escort, but they remain near the entrance, clearly uncomfortable.
Elistan - An elderly human cleric, thin and scholarly, wearing robes of 
Paladine. His eyes are sharp, assessing the cursed keep with both caution and 
curiosity.
Brother Marius - The cleric from Haven who briefed you about death 
knights. He's here as theological support and witness.
 
GOLDMOON APPROACHES
She walks forward with absolute confidence, the satchel held reverently. Her 
escorts remain behind. She stops thirty feet from Lord Soth's throne and looks 
up at the death knight without fear.
Then she looks at Lady Korinthe - recognizing immediately what she is, what 
she's become.
Finally, her eyes find Johannes, Cyrus, and Kessa.
"Brother Cyrus. Johannes. Kessa." Her voice is warm, melodious, carrying 
natural authority. "Commander Laurana told me you sent urgent word. That a 
death knight seeks judgment. That his cursed wife bears witness. That three 
hundred years of penance might end today."
She looks around the Great Hall - the skeletal warriors, the ghostly figures, the 
weight of centuries.
"I confess, when I received your message, I thought it impossible. Death 
knights don't seek redemption. Banshees don't transform peacefully. Curses 
don't simply... wait for judgment."
She looks back at Soth and Korinthe.
"But I brought the Disks of Mishakal. Because impossible things have been 
happening since these holy relics returned to Krynn. And if the gods wish to 
speak judgment here, I will be their vessel."
 
ELISTAN STEPS FORWARD
"I am Elistan, High Priest of Paladine. I have come because if Lord Soth is to 
be judged, it should be by the god he once served. The god whose knight he 
was before his fall."
He looks at Soth with a mixture of sorrow and steel.
"Knight of the Rose. Death Knight of Dargaard. After three hundred years of 
self-imposed penance, do you seek true judgment? Do you petition the gods to 
assess whether your suffering has been sufficient, or whether it must 
continue?"
 
LORD SOTH'S RESPONSE
The death knight stands, descends from his throne, and - for the first time in 
three hundred years - kneels.
Not in submission. But in proper respect before divine authority.
"High Priest Elistan. Bearer Goldmoon. I am Lord Loren Soth, 
Knight of the Rose, Death Knight of Dargaard Keep."
"I failed my divine mission. I chose personal love over the world's 
salvation. Millions died because of my choice. I have borne three 
hundred years of guilt, torment, and curse as consequence."
"I petition the gods for judgment. Not for mercy - I do not deserve 
mercy. But for assessment. Has my penance been sufficient? Or 
must I endure until the end of time itself?"
"I submit myself to divine will. Whatever the gods decree, I will 
accept."
 
LADY KORINTHE SPEAKS
"I am Lady Korinthe, wife of Lord Soth, mother of Peradur. I died 
in the Cataclysm. I rose as a banshee, consumed by rage for three 
hundred years."
"I stand here transformed, no longer raging, seeking truth rather 
than vengeance. I bear witness to Lord Soth's judgment. I will 
speak honestly of his failures and his penance."
"I ask the gods this: Has he suffered enough? Has three hundred 
years of torment balanced the scales? Or must the curse continue?"
She looks at Goldmoon.
"I do not ask for his forgiveness. I ask for divine clarity. Let the 
gods decide what mortal understanding cannot."
 
GOLDMOON OPENS THE SATCHEL
She reaches in carefully and withdraws them - the Disks of Mishakal. 
Ancient platinum disks, inscribed with holy text in languages lost since the 
Cataclysm. They glow with pure divine radiance, filling the Great Hall with 
warmth that hasn't existed here in three centuries.
The skeletal warriors along the walls drop to one knee simultaneously. The 
ghostly figures bow. Even Sir Caradoc, bound to his chapel, can likely feel this 
moment.
"Lord Soth. Lady Korinthe. Before witnesses, before the gods 
themselves, we gather for judgment."
Goldmoon's voice resonates with power beyond her own - Mishakal speaking 
through her chosen vessel.
"Johannes Constantinius, Kessa Darrow, Brother Cyrus - you who 
brought truth to this place, who broke three centuries of isolation 
with mercy and understanding - bear witness. Record what 
transpires."
"Commander Laurana, Elistan, Brother Marius - you who 
represent the living world beyond this curse - bear witness as well."
She places the Disks on the floor before Soth, and they begin to glow brighter, 
their light expanding to fill the entire hall.
 
THE GODS SPEAK
The light becomes overwhelming but not blinding. And then - voices. Not 
words exactly, but presence. Divine judgment made manifest.
MISHAKAL'S PRESENCE (through Goldmoon, warm but 
unflinching): "Loren Soth. You chose love over duty. Personal devotion over 
cosmic responsibility. Your choice led to millions of deaths. This is truth."
PALADINE'S PRESENCE (through Elistan, stern but not cruel): "You were 
my knight. My champion. Given a quest to save the world. You failed not 
from weakness, but from misguided love. This is truth."
THE DIVINE ASSESSMENT BEGINS
The Disks pulse with each statement, as if weighing Soth's very soul:
"Three hundred years you have endured. Three hundred years of guilt. Three 
hundred years of torment. Self-imposed, yes, but genuine. You have not fled 
your punishment. You have not sought escape. You have borne witness to 
your failure every night, reliving the moment of catastrophe."
"Your wife transformed from rage to understanding. Not through your 
efforts, but through the efforts of those who brought truth. Yet her 
transformation reflects upon you - the capacity for redemption exists."
"The Starjewel purified itself when she chose mercy. Divine artifacts respond 
to moral shifts. The curse itself has begun to weaken not because time has 
passed, but because understanding has been reached."
The light intensifies further:
"Loren Soth. The question before us: Has your penance balanced your 
failure? Have three hundred years of suffering equaled the cost of millions of 
deaths and a world broken?"
 
THE JUDGMENT PAUSES
The divine presence seems to wait - not for Soth to answer, but for something 
else.
Goldmoon speaks, her own voice returning: "The gods wish to hear from 
others. Those who bear witness. Those who know what you've become and 
what you were."
She looks at Lady Korinthe first.
"Lady Korinthe. You who suffered most directly from his choice. Speak truth. 
Has he suffered enough?"
 
Johannes, Cyrus, Kessa - you are about to witness Lady Korinthe's 
testimony, then potentially be asked to speak yourselves. This is 
the culmination of everything you've worked toward.
What happens next will determine whether Lord Soth and all those 
bound to him find release, or whether the curse continues.
Wait with baited breath
Dec 10
LADY KORINTHE'S TESTIMONY
She floats forward, positioning herself between Soth and the Disks, her 
spectral form illuminated by their divine radiance.
"Three hundred years ago, I died in terror and pain. I believed my 
husband was a murderer. I believed he let me and our son burn out 
of cruelty or indifference."
"I became rage incarnate. I screamed accusations through these 
walls for three centuries. I killed anyone who entered this place. I 
made this keep a monument to my hatred."
"But three days ago, three mortals showed me truth."
She gestures to Johannes, Cyrus, and Kessa.
"They showed me the Cataclysm. They showed me Soth's choice - to 
turn back from his quest, to choose me over the world. They 
showed me him at the Chapel doors, trying desperately to reach us 
and failing because no mortal strength could overcome divine 
judgment."
"They showed me what I became. And they gave me a choice: rest 
for myself, or witness for others."
She turns to face Soth directly.
"Has he suffered enough? I cannot answer that from a place of 
cosmic justice. I am not a god. I cannot weigh millions of deaths 
against three centuries of torment."
"But I can speak to this: He loved catastrophically. He failed 
utterly. And he has never once tried to escape the consequences. 
He has sat on that throne for three hundred years, accepting his 
punishment, never seeking relief, never claiming it was unfair."
"He made the worst choice a knight could make - personal love 
over universal duty. But he made it out of love, not malice. Out of 
devotion, not cruelty."
"And if the gods ask whether a man can love so much that he 
dooms the world... the answer is yes. Soth is proof."
She pauses, her voice becoming softer:
"I do not forgive him. I am not certain I can. But I no longer hate 
him. I understand him. And I believe three hundred years of 
reliving his failure, of hearing his son's screams, of carrying the 
weight of millions of deaths... that is punishment beyond what 
mortal courts could devise."
"So I say to the gods: If you deem his suffering sufficient, release 
him. Release us all. Let this curse end."
"And if you deem it insufficient... then I will remain with him. Not 
as his tormentor, but as his companion in continued penance. We 
will bear this together rather than in isolation."
"That is my testimony."
 
THE DISKS PULSE
The divine light shifts, acknowledging her words, weighing them.
GOLDMOON TURNS TO THE OTHERS
"The gods have heard the wife. Now they would hear from those who broke the 
curse's isolation."
She looks at Cyrus first.
"Brother Cyrus, servant of Mishakal. You transformed Lady Korinthe from 
banshee to peaceful spirit. You have walked these halls, spoken with the 
cursed, seen their suffering. Speak truth. Has Lord Soth suffered enough?"
 
CYRUS STEPS FORWARD
He approaches the Disks, kneels respectfully, then rises to speak:
"I am Brother Cyrus, healer and servant of Mishakal. I have 
witnessed suffering - in battle, in the aftermath of war, in those 
broken by loss and guilt."
"But I have never seen suffering like Lord Soth's. Three hundred 
years of self-imposed torment. Every night, reliving his failure. 
Every day, sitting in judgment of himself more harshly than any 
god could."
"When we arrived, he didn't attack us. He listened. He granted us 
safe passage. He allowed us to investigate, to learn, to bring truth 
to his wife. He showed restraint, honor, and acceptance of 
consequences that many living knights could not match."
"Sir Caradoc, bound to the chapel below, has prayed for three 
hundred years. The knights who followed Soth share his curse not 
because they committed his sin, but because they served him 
loyally. They have borne punishment for another's failure."
"I believe three hundred years is enough. I believe the curse has 
served its purpose - Soth has learned what duty means through its 
catastrophic absence. He has learned the cost of choosing love over 
responsibility. He has learned it so thoroughly that it has become 
his entire existence."
"Mishakal teaches that healing requires both time and 
transformation. Three hundred years is time. The change in this 
keep - the transformation of Lady Korinthe, the purification of the 
Starjewel, the willingness of Soth to seek judgment rather than 
hide from it - that is transformation."
"I say: Release them. Let the curse end. Let those who have 
suffered find rest."
 
THE DISKS PULSE AGAIN
Goldmoon turns to Kessa.
"Kessa Darrow. You who observe, who see truth others miss. Speak. Has Lord 
Soth suffered enough?"
 
KESSA HESITATES, THEN STEPS FORWARD
She's clearly uncomfortable being asked to judge cosmic matters, but she 
speaks honestly:
"I'm not a cleric. I'm not a knight. I'm just... someone who's seen a 
lot of people make terrible choices and live with the 
consequences."
"Lord Soth made the worst choice imaginable. Millions died 
because he chose one woman over the world. That's... that's 
unforgivable in a lot of ways."
"But here's what I saw: When we entered this place, he could have 
killed us. Death knights are powerful enough. Instead, he listened. 
He granted permission. He allowed us to walk freely through his 
domain because we approached with respect rather than greed."
"When we told him his wife wanted to speak with him, he didn't 
rage or blame. He asked if she would have him. Three hundred 
years of her hatred, and his first response was humility."
"And Lady Korinthe - she could have taken her rest, her peace. 
Instead, she chose to stay and witness his judgment. That tells me 
something about who these people were before the curse, and who 
they're trying to be now."
"I don't know if three hundred years balances millions of deaths. I 
can't do that math. But I know that keeping them cursed forever 
doesn't bring back the dead. It doesn't undo the Cataclysm. It just 
perpetuates suffering."
"So yeah. I say release them. Let them rest. They've paid enough."
 
THE DISKS PULSE A THIRD TIME
Finally, Goldmoon looks at Johannes.
"Johannes Constantinius. You who saw the path to truth. You who broke Lady 
Korinthe's rage with mirrors of reality. You who convinced a death knight to 
seek judgment rather than remain in isolation. Speak. Has Lord Soth suffered 
enough?"
 
THE HALL IS SILENT
Every eye - living, dead, and undead - turns to Johannes. Lord Soth kneels, 
head bowed. Lady Korinthe waits. The Disks glow, ready to receive the final 
testimony.
Johannes, what do you say?
Those who have already spoken have shared the thoughts of my own heart 
and mind on this matter. I do not care to add.
Dec 10
JOHANNES'S TESTIMONY
Johannes steps forward, but doesn't kneel. He stands before the Disks with 
the same honest directness he's shown throughout this entire mission.
"Those who have already spoken have shared the thoughts of my 
own heart and mind on this matter. I do not care to add."
His voice is simple, clear, without elaboration or flourish.
 
GOLDMOON STUDIES HIM
For a moment, she seems surprised by the brevity. Then she smiles slightly - 
understanding.
"Sometimes the most profound testimony is agreement. You 
brought them to this moment. Your work speaks louder than 
additional words could."
She turns back to the Disks, which pulse with acknowledgment.
 
THE DIVINE JUDGMENT
The light from the Disks intensifies until the entire Great Hall is bathed in 
radiance. The voices return - MISHAKAL and PALADINE speaking in concert:
"We have heard. Wife and companions. Healer and observer. Truth-bringer 
who needs not elaborate."
"Four witnesses speak with one voice: Three hundred years is sufficient. The 
curse has served its purpose. Transformation has occurred. Understanding 
has been reached."
The light focuses on Lord Soth, still kneeling:
"Loren Soth. You failed your divine mission. You chose love over duty. 
Millions died because of your choice. This cannot be undone. This cannot be 
forgiven in the way mortals forgive."
"But you have borne witness to your failure for three centuries. You have 
punished yourself more thoroughly than we could devise. You have accepted 
consequence without escape, without excuse, without deflection."
"And in the end, when mortals brought truth to your domain, you did not 
resist. You allowed understanding. You sought judgment rather than hiding 
from it."
"This is not redemption. But it is acknowledgment. It is penance completed."
The light shifts to Lady Korinthe:
"Korinthe. You suffered through no fault of your own. You died in terror. You 
rose in rage. But when given the choice between personal peace and bearing 
witness for others, you chose witness."
"This choice breaks the cycle. This choice transforms curse into conclusion."
 
THE JUDGMENT IS PRONOUNCED
"Loren Soth. Your curse is LIFTED. Your penance is COMPLETE. You have 
suffered three hundred years for failing the world out of love. That suffering 
ends now."
"Korinthe. Your suffering is ACKNOWLEDGED. Your transformation is 
WITNESSED. You are released from rage, released from this place, released 
to find peace beyond."
"All who are bound here - Sir Caradoc, the knights who followed, the spirits 
who serve - your vigil ENDS. Your loyalty has been witnessed. Your 
suffering is concluded."
 
THE TRANSFORMATION BEGINS
The cold flames around Lord Soth's armor begin to fade - not flickering, 
but dissolving. The blackened plate lightens, the corruption lifting like smoke. 
Beneath, the armor of a Knight of the Rose, tarnished but whole.
The burning points of light in his eye sockets dim, and then... flesh begins to 
return. Slowly, like ice melting, his undead form transforms. Not back to life - 
that's not possible - but into something peaceful. A body at rest rather than 
cursed animation.
Lord Soth collapses forward, no longer able to sustain his kneeling position. 
He lies on the stone floor as the transformation continues.
LADY KORINTHE'S CHANGE
Her spectral form becomes more solid, more real - and then begins to fade in 
the opposite direction. Not vanishing into nothing, but ascending. Becoming 
pure light, pure spirit, free from earthly binding.
She looks down at Soth one final time:
"We failed together. We suffered together. Now... we rest."
Her form dissolves into silver radiance that rises toward the ceiling and 
beyond.
 
THROUGHOUT THE KEEP
Every witness feels it:
*	Sir Caradoc in his chapel - the armor clatters to the floor, empty. His 
spirit rises, free at last.
*	The skeletal warriors along the walls collapse into dust, their bones 
finally permitted to rest
*	The ghostly figures fade with expressions of relief, finally released 
from their vigil
*	The keep itself - the oppressive cold lifts, the darkness recedes, the 
weight of centuries evaporates
In the space of minutes, Dargaard Keep transforms from cursed fortress to 
empty ruins. Just stone and memory.
 
LORD SOTH'S FINAL MOMENT
He lies on the floor before the throne, his transformation complete. No longer 
a death knight. No longer cursed. Just... a body at rest.
He looks up at Goldmoon, at Elistan, at Johannes, Cyrus, and Kessa. His eyes - 
human eyes now, weary beyond measure - show gratitude and peace.
"Thank you."
Two words. Three hundred years of suffering ending in simple gratitude.
"Tell... tell the world... that love can doom as surely as hatred. That 
duty matters as much as devotion. That choices... choices echo 
across centuries."
His eyes close.
"And tell them... that even the damned... can find mercy... if they're 
willing... to face judgment."
His breathing slows. Stops.
Lord Loren Soth, Knight of the Rose, Death Knight of Dargaard Keep, dies 
cleanly. Three hundred years after the Cataclysm, he finally finds the death 
that was denied him.
 
THE GREAT HALL IS SILENT
The Disks' radiance fades to a gentle glow. Goldmoon carefully returns them 
to their satchel.
Commander Laurana and the resistance soldiers stand in awed silence.
Elistan and Brother Marius both have tears running down their faces - 
witnesses to divine mercy they never expected to see.
 
GOLDMOON APPROACHES JOHANNES, CYRUS, AND KESSA
"What you have accomplished here... this will be remembered. Not 
just in military histories, but in theological texts. You broke a 
three-hundred-year curse. You brought a death knight to judgment 
and saw him released. You transformed a banshee into a peaceful 
spirit."
"The gods themselves bore witness to your work. That is... that is 
extraordinary."
 
COMMANDER LAURANA
"I came expecting... I don't know what I expected. A battle, maybe. Or another 
mission. But this?" She gestures to the now-peaceful hall. "This is something 
else entirely."
She looks at the three of you with newfound respect.
"When you're ready, return to Haven. We need to discuss... well, everything. 
What happened here changes our understanding of curses, of redemption, of 
what's possible."
 
THE KEEP IS EMPTY NOW
Just ruins. Just stone. The cursed fortress of Dargaard Keep is now simply 
Dargaard Keep - an ancient fortress, scarred by the Cataclysm, but no longer 
haunted.
Outside, if you were to look, you'd see that Dargaard Village is celebrating. The 
oppressive presence that has hung over them for generations has lifted. 
Children are laughing. People are crying with relief.
 
JOHANNES, CYRUS, KESSA:
You have witnessed the conclusion of a three-hundred-year curse. You have 
seen divine judgment enacted. You have accomplished something that will be 
spoken of for generations.
What do you do now? Do you:
1.	Remain at the keep - explore what's left, reflect on what transpired
2.	Go to Dargaard Village - share the news, receive their gratitude
3.	Return to Haven with the delegation - debrief and plan next steps
4.	Something else
And how do you feel about what you've just witnessed?
The Keep is a major strategic point; the resistance must immediately move 
forces to maintain control.
Dec 10
JOHANNES'S STRATEGIC ASSESSMENT
Johannes turns to Commander Laurana, his tactical mind already processing 
the implications.
"Commander, Dargaard Keep is a major strategic point. It controls the 
mountain passes, has excellent sight lines, and is structurally sound despite 
the Cataclysm damage. The Dragon Army will realize the curse has lifted - 
they'll move to claim it if we don't."
He gestures to the fortress around them.
"The resistance must immediately move forces to maintain control. Garrison 
it, fortify it, make it a resistance stronghold before the Dragon Army can 
respond."
 
LAURANA'S IMMEDIATE RESPONSE
She nods sharply, her military training snapping into focus after the spiritual 
weight of the judgment.
"You're absolutely right. I was so focused on the divine spectacle that I nearly 
overlooked the tactical reality."
She turns to her escort soldiers. "Kael, ride back to Haven immediately. Fast 
horse, don't stop. Tell Marshal Theros we need a garrison force here - 
minimum fifty soldiers, engineers to assess structural integrity, supplies for 
fortification. Move within 24 hours."
One soldier salutes and sprints from the hall.
Laurana continues: "The Dragon Army had a patrol here eight days ago. They 
died, but their commanders will expect a report eventually. When that report 
doesn't come, they'll send investigators. We have maybe two weeks before they 
realize something significant has changed."
She looks around the Great Hall with new eyes - not as a cursed throne room, 
but as a command center.
"This keep could anchor our entire northeastern defensive line. Control of 
these passes means control of trade routes, troop movements, and access to 
the mountain settlements."
 
GOLDMOON ADDS
"There's another consideration: this place is now sacred. Divine judgment was 
rendered here. The curse of three centuries was lifted. Pilgrims will come. 
Clerics will want to study what happened. This isn't just a military asset - it's a 
spiritual one."
She looks at Elistan, who nods agreement.
"We should establish a small chapel here. Dedicate it to both Mishakal and 
Paladine, honoring both the healing and the judgment that occurred. It would 
serve the garrison's spiritual needs and mark this place as under divine 
protection."
 
ELISTAN'S SUGGESTION
"I will remain here temporarily, if Commander Laurana permits. I can 
consecrate the Chapel of the Order, perform rites to ensure no residual curse 
energy lingers, and serve as spiritual advisor to the garrison until permanent 
clergy arrive."
He looks at the spot where Lord Soth died.
"And we should inter Lord Soth properly. He died redeemed, after divine 
judgment. He deserves burial with honor, not to be left lying in this hall. A 
simple tomb, marked with his name and rank: Knight of the Rose. Let history 
remember he fell, but also that he accepted his punishment and found peace."
 
BROTHER MARIUS
"The lower levels should be cleared thoroughly. Sir Caradoc and the other 
bound spirits are released, but their armor and effects remain. Those should 
be collected, catalogued, and either preserved as historical artifacts or given 
proper burial."
"And the Starjewel-" He looks to where it still rests with Soth's body. "That's 
a holy relic of Paladine. It should be secured, either here in a consecrated 
chapel or transported to a temple for safekeeping."
 
COMMANDER LAURANA'S ORDERS
She's thinking tactically now, issuing rapid decisions:
"Immediate priorities:
1.	Secure the perimeter - My remaining three soldiers will establish 
watch positions until reinforcements arrive.
2.	Structural assessment - Johannes, Cyrus, Kessa - you know this 
keep better than anyone. Can you do a quick survey? Identify which 
sections are stable, which need repair, where we should focus defensive 
efforts?
3.	Local relations - Dargaard Village has lived in fear for generations. 
Someone needs to formally announce the curse is lifted, that the keep is 
now resistance-held, and that we'll protect them from Dragon Army 
retaliation.
4.	Intelligence security - The Dragon Army cannot learn about the 
divine judgment or the Disks being here. Publicly, we say: 'Resistance 
forces cleared the keep of undead through conventional military action.' 
The spiritual truth stays classified.
5.	Soth's internment - Elistan handles this, with full honors. Tomorrow, 
after we've secured the site."
She looks at the three of you.
"You've done the impossible here. But I'm asking for one more day 
of work. Help us secure this place properly. Survey the keep, advise 
on fortifications, help transition this from cursed fortress to 
resistance stronghold."
"After that, you've earned rest. Real rest. And whatever rewards 
Haven can provide."
 
KESSA SPEAKS UP
"What about the Starjewel? That's a powerful holy relic. Leaving it here, even 
in a consecrated chapel, feels risky. The Dragon Army specifically came 
seeking it."
GOLDMOON CONSIDERS
"She's right. The Starjewel is too valuable and too vulnerable here. I'll take it 
with the Disks back to Haven, where we can properly protect it. Eventually, it 
should go to a Temple of Paladine, but until one is re-established..."
She carefully retrieves the gem from where it rests near Soth's body.
"I'll safeguard it. The Dragon Army will never know it was purified."
 
THE PLAN IS SET
Next 24 hours:
*	Johannes, Cyrus, Kessa survey the keep and advise on fortifications
*	Elistan consecrates the Chapel and prepares Soth's burial
*	Laurana's soldiers establish perimeter security
*	Messengers coordinate with Dargaard Village
*	Reinforcements depart Haven (arriving in 2-3 days)
After that:
*	Return to Haven for proper debriefing and rest
*	The keep becomes a resistance stronghold
*	The story of what truly happened remains classified
 
JOHANNES, CYRUS, KESSA:
You're being asked to spend one more day here - surveying the keep's tactical 
value, identifying fortification priorities, and helping transition this place from 
supernatural horror to military asset.
Do you:
1.	Accept immediately - begin the survey work
2.	Negotiate terms - request specific compensation or support
3.	Delegate differently - suggest an alternative approach
4.	Ask questions - clarify anything about the plan
What's your response?
The Jewel should stay here. The Dragon Army wanted it because they thought 
that because it was corrupted, they could use it to control Soth and his

within their grasp; it is a living embodiment of Paladine, just as the Disks. 
Leaving it here not only honors Soth and his story; it will actively resist Takhisis 
and her forces far better than even a whole garrison of troops.
Dec 10
JOHANNES'S COUNTER-ARGUMENT
Johannes steps forward, his voice firm and confident.
"The Jewel should stay here. The Dragon Army wanted it because they 
thought that because it was corrupted, they could use it to control Soth and his 
retinue. With it cleansed, Soth redeemed? The Jewel is not only no longer 
within their grasp; it is a living embodiment of Paladine, just as the Disks are 
of Mishakal."
He looks at Goldmoon directly, respectfully but with conviction.
"Leaving it here not only honors Soth and his story; it will actively resist 
Takhisis and her forces far better than even a whole garrison of troops. This 
place was cursed for three centuries. Now it's blessed. That's a weapon the 
Dragon Army can't counter."
 
GOLDMOON PAUSES
She's holding the Starjewel, feeling its warm radiance. She closes her eyes, 
listening - or perhaps praying.
After a moment, she opens them and nods slowly.
"You're right. I can feel it - Mishakal agrees. The Starjewel doesn't want to 
leave. It belongs here."
She looks at Elistan. "What do you think, High Priest? You know Paladine's 
ways better than any of us."
 
ELISTAN'S ASSESSMENT
The elderly cleric approaches, studying the gem with scholarly intensity and 
spiritual sensitivity.
"Johannes speaks truth. The Starjewel was given to Lord Soth as a symbol of 
his worthiness. It corrupted with his fall. It purified with his redemption. This 
isn't just a holy relic - it's a testament."
He gestures around the Great Hall.
"This place witnessed three hundred years of curse, then witnessed divine 
judgment and mercy. The Starjewel anchors that story. If we remove it, we're 
just taking a valuable item. If we leave it, properly consecrated, it becomes 
something greater - a beacon. A ward. A reminder that even the fallen can find 
redemption."
He looks at Johannes with approval.
"And tactically, you're correct. Holy relics actively resist evil. Dragon Army 
forces would find this place... uncomfortable. Dragonborn serving Takhisis, 
dark clerics, undead servants - they'd feel the Starjewel's presence. It would 
weaken them, disadvantage them, make holding this keep nearly impossible 
for them even if they took it by force."
 
COMMANDER LAURANA'S TACTICAL PERSPECTIVE
"So you're proposing we leave a priceless holy relic in a frontier fortress that 
will be under constant Dragon Army pressure?"
She considers this, then slowly smiles.
"Actually... that's brilliant. The Dragon Army knows this keep exists. They 
know it was cursed. They sent a patrol that never returned. If they attack and 
find it garrisoned, they'll think we just cleared out undead and occupied it."
"But if their forces start experiencing unexplained difficulties - exhaustion, 
failed spells, moral degradation, their undead auxiliaries refusing to enter - 
they'll realize something supernatural is at work. They'll think the curse 
persists in a different form. It'll make them hesitant, cautious, afraid."
She nods decisively. "Leave the Starjewel. But we protect it properly."
 
GOLDMOON PLACES THE STARJEWEL
She carries it to the altar in the Chapel of the Order, where it originally rested 
for centuries before the Cataclysm.
"Then here it stays. In the Chapel where Lady Korinthe died and was 
transformed. Where divine judgment was sought and granted. Where the 
curse ended."
She places it carefully on the altar, and immediately the Chapel feels different 
- warmer, brighter, more present.
ELISTAN PERFORMS A QUICK CONSECRATION
He raises his hands over the Starjewel:
"Paladine, Platinum Dragon, God of Justice and Honor - witness this relic's 
return. The Starjewel, once corrupted by curse, now purified by redemption, 
rests here as testament to your mercy. Let it stand as beacon and ward. Let it 
remind all who enter that justice tempered with mercy is the highest virtue. 
Let it resist darkness and strengthen light. So it is witnessed. So let it be."
The Starjewel pulses with brilliant light, then settles into a steady, warm glow.
 
BROTHER MARIUS
"We'll need to establish protocols. The Chapel should be restricted - garrison 
soldiers can pray here, but the altar itself should be guarded. No one touches 
the Starjewel without clerical permission. And we document what it is, what 
happened here, so future garrisons understand they're protecting something 
sacred, not just a pretty gem."
 
LAURANA AGREES
"Understood. The Chapel becomes consecrated ground with restricted access. 
I'll assign guards who understand they're protecting a holy site, not just a 
tactical position."
She looks at Johannes with genuine respect.
"You saw what I missed - that spiritual power is tactical power. That leaving 
the Starjewel here makes this place stronger than any fortification we could 
build."
She extends her hand.
"Thank you. For everything. The mission, the judgment, and this counsel. You 
think like a commander, fight like a champion, and apparently understand 
divine strategy better than most clerics."
 
THE PLAN IS FINALIZED
Dargaard Keep becomes:
*	Resistance military garrison (50+ troops)
*	Sacred site with consecrated Chapel
*	Home of the Starjewel (guarded, restricted access)
*	Strategic stronghold controlling mountain passes
*	Symbolic victory - cursed fortress redeemed and reclaimed
Next steps:

*	Spread carefully controlled information to Dargaard Village
 
GOLDMOON APPROACHES THE THREE OF YOU
"You've earned my deepest respect. And Mishakal's attention. What you've

She looks at Cyrus specifically.
"Brother Cyrus, you transformed a banshee through compassion and wisdom.

Then to all three:
"When you return to Haven, seek me out. I'd like to speak with you about...

do their work. And you three have proven you understand what that work 
entails."
 
THE SUN IS SETTING
Through the damaged sections of the Great Hall, you can see the sky turning 
gold and red. The oppressive darkness that hung over this place for three 
centuries is gone. It's just a fortress now - scarred, damaged, but clean.
